rel=\"noopener\">deep-touch therapy</a> — similar to the comfort created by swaddling babies.</li><li><a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=89663&urllink=gravityblankets.com%2Fnkets.com%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored\">Gravity Blankets</a> makes one of the most popular options, and the company has a version of its blanket specifically designed to have a cooling effect.</li><li>I've been sleeping under the <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=89663&urllink=gravityblankets.com%2Fproducts%2Fcooling-blanketling-blanket\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored\">Cooling Blanket ($205)</a>, and it's definitely the most breathable and best-looking of any weighted blanket I've tested.&#160;&#160;</li><li>It comes with a steep price tag, but if you're looking for the best — and can comfortably afford it — this is a solid option.</li><li>See more: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-weighted-blanket\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The best weighted blankets</a></li></ul><div id=\"ProductCard_5e34376424306a7d6b4f7194\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe src=\"https://produktor.businessinsider.com/productCardService?id=5e34376424306a7d6b4f7194&type=small&live=true\" width=\"100%\" height=\"150%\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\" style=\"position:absolute; top:0; left: 0\"></iframe></div><p>There are few purchases in my adult life that I would say have been truly life-changing — and most of them have incidentally wound up been sleep-related. I have two <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=83399&urllink=luxepillow.com%2Fillow.com%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored\">fantastic pillows</a>&#160;and a <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=63899&urllink=laylasleep.com%2Fproduct%2Flayla-topper%2Fla-topper%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored\">mattress pad</a> that inspires me to actually rush to bed, and one new addition is weighted blankets.</p><p>I truly didn't know how much better my quality of sleep could get until I started sleeping under a 15-pound weighted blanket. And an improvement to sleep impacts pretty much every area of your life; with deeper, more restful shut-eye, I was finding I had more energy during the day and actively looked forward to getting to bed earlier at night.</p><p>If you're in the early stages of research to find the right one for yourself, you've probably already run into the name <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=89663&urllink=gravityblankets.com%2Fnkets.com%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored\">Gravity Blankets</a>. It's a Kickstarter-alum that now sells one of the most popular — and luxurious — options on the market.</p><p>The original <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=89663&urllink=gravityblankets.com%2Fproducts%2Fgravity-blanketvity-blanket\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Gravity Blanket ($195)</a> is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-weighted-blanket\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">one of the best weighted blankets you can buy</a>. However, sleeping under an inherently dense, adult-sized weight isn't always appealing for those who sleep hot, or who hate the idea of blasting the AC and running up the energy bill over the summer.</p><p>For those sleepers, Gravity has the <a href=\"https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=89663&urllink=gravityblankets.com%2Fproducts%2Fcooling-blanket%3Fvariant%3D28622152499274622152499274\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Cooling Blanket ($199)</a>.</p><p>To see if it could actually hold up on a swampy summer night, I tried it in my small NYC apartment that suffers from a greenhouse effect with its heat.&#160;</p><h2>How do weighted blankets work?</h2><p><a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=89663&urllink=gravityblankets.com%2Fproducts%2Fcooling-blanketling-blanket\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d0a4d02d0dafe32da2cf7a6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"190402_GB_GOTG_7890_1024x1024\" height=\"819\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Gravity&#39;s Cooling Blanket won&#39;t feel exactly like &#34;the cold side of the pillow&#34; all the time, but it is cool and smooth to the touch — and held up in muggy NYC summer living conditions.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Gravity Blankets</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>Weighted blankets work through <a href=\"https://www.webmd.com/sleep-disorders/news/20180402/seeking-better-sleep-under-a-weighted-blanket\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">deep pressure touch stimulation therapy (or DPTS)</a> that's similar to the effect achieved by swaddling babies or putting dogs in \"thunder jackets.\" While light touches can alert the nervous system, deep pressure (such as a good massage or tight and heavy blanket) has a relaxing, calming effect on the body. That's essentially why weighted blankets are used for the therapeutic treatment of sensory disorders, anxiety, depression, autism, insomnia, and more. They're a relatively inexpensive, effective, and medication-free way to encourage calmness and relaxation. According to a Mayo Clinic Minute interview with Dr. Adam Perlman, it's kind of like what happens in the body <a href=\"https://newsnetwork.mayoclinic.org/discussion/mayo-clinic-minute-how-weighted-blankets-may-lift-anxiety/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">when you get a hug</a>.</p><p>More specifically for sleep, deep pressure can help relax the nervous system, <a href=\"http://sitn.hms.harvard.edu/flash/2016/research-into-our-sense-of-touch-leads-to-new-treatments-for-autism/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reduce the stress hormone cortisol</a>, and encourage serotonin and dopamine production, which promotes relaxation and regulates our moods. Then, serotonin converts to melatonin, and that makes you sleepy. The tangential feelings of calm, safety, relief, and comfort only aid in your body's natural processes. There are also studies that demonstrate how grounding the human body during sleep <a href=\"https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/15650465\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">measurably reduces or eliminates pain and stress</a>.&#160;</p><h2>How to choose the right weight for your weighted blanket</h2><p>If you're looking into giving one a shot, aim for a weight that's about 10% of your own body weight. My 15-pound blanket is a little more than 10% of my body weight, but it still feels perfect. If you feel like something heavier might make it harder to roll over or give you a feeling of being trapped, err on the lighter side.&#160;</p><h2>What makes Gravity's Cooling Blanket different?</h2><p><a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=89663&urllink=gravityblankets.com%2Fproducts%2Fcooling-blanketling-blanket\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d0a4d320a2849257b11ab91?format=jpeg\" alt=\"190402_GB_GOTG_7317_1080x\" height=\"810\" width=\"1080\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Cooling Blanket is definitely the most elegant iteration of a weighted blanket, and meshes well with the rest of my decor — something worth mentioning for traditionally bulky blankets.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Gravity Blankets</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>The <a href=\"https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=89663&urllink=gravityblankets.com%2Fproducts%2Fcooling-blanket%3Fvariant%3D28622152499274622152499274\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Cooling Blanket ($199)</a> is the company's cooler, more breathable version of its original, the <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=89663&urllink=gravityblankets.com%2Fnkets.com%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored\">Gravity Blanket ($195)</a>. It still uses glass beads instead of plastic poly pellets for a better experience (glass beads are smaller, denser, and make the blanket noticeably less bulky), but the duvet cover is made with a \"faux Tencel\" material that encourages airflow and keeps you from overheating. Like its predecessors, it too has Gravity's gridded stitching to keep the internal glass beads from dispersing unevenly during sleep.&#160;</p><p>You can find in understated <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=89663&urllink=gravityblankets.com%2Fproducts%2Fcooling-blanketling-blanket\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored\">white, gray, and navy</a> colors.&#160;</p><h2>Review of Gravity's Cooling Blanket</h2><p>The <a href=\"https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=89663&urllink=gravityblankets.com%2Fproducts%2Fcooling-blanket%3Fvariant%3D28622152499274622152499274\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Cooling Blanket</a> is still a weighted blanket, so I was skeptical of how much an updated duvet cover could do. In person, though, it did seem to keep me unnaturally well-regulated throughout the night. If you're imagining it feeling like the cold side of the pillow all the time, that's not quite the case. But it does feel cool, silky, and breathable at first touch and when readjusting — it's just not a persistent phenomenon. The cooling is more subtle, though nonetheless effective, than that. In this, it reminded me of workout gear: Good performance materials let me get through a yoga class without cursing whoever makes my leggings, but rarely do I notice the work being done to wick away moisture and dissipate heat while it's happening.</p><p>I slept with the <a href=\"https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=89663&urllink=gravityblankets.com%2Fproducts%2Fcooling-blanket%3Fvariant%3D28622152499274622152499274\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Cooling Blanket ($199)</a> as my main blanket with temperatures in the mid-80s with 75% humidity without AC or a breeze and never woke up uncomfortable. I was impressed with how well it managed to regulate my temperature. It won't be as airy as a linen top sheet, but it would be unrealistic to expect it to be. If you're looking for a way to make a heavy, 15-pound blanket more breathable, this may be your best option, though my personal experiences might differ from yours.</p><p>Another thing worth mentioning if you're going to drop $200+ on a blanket is that it's by far the most aesthetically pleasing weighted blanket I've ever used. If you care about the overall aesthetic of your room, and the rest of it sounds justifiable to you, this is the one that will be the most undetectable. It looks fresh and crisp — like any other quilt.</p><p><a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=89663&urllink=gravityblankets.com%2Fproducts%2Fcooling-blanketling-blanket\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d0a4da50a2849258b7b24b2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"190402_GB_GOTG_7577_1024x1024\" height=\"768\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Gridded stitching makes sure the blanket&#39;s internal glass beads remain uniformly distributed.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Gravity Blankets</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><h2>The bottom line</h2><p>The <a href=\"https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=89663&urllink=gravityblankets.com%2Fproducts%2Fcooling-blanket%3Fvariant%3D28622152499274622152499274\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Gravity Cooling Blanket</a> is worth it if you want to experience the benefits of a weighted blanket but don't want to risk overheating or having to blast your AC all night.</p><p>If that doesn't describe you, it's worth looking into some alternatives before giving up the dream of owning a weighted blanket. There are under-$100 options on Amazon — like this <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B075F9ST7G/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&th=1&linkCode=sl1&tag=biip_061819_gravity-cooling-blanket-20&linkId=ac7e65381cad3fcad1878c5edf3122c8&language=en_US8&#38;language=en_US\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored\">$70 version</a> I also own and love — though you'll probably need to throw on the AC in the summer if you plan to use it then (and once you start it's hard to stop, so I'd plan for that).</p><p>Your budget and needs will determine what's the best value deal for you, but, regardless of which one you ultimately choose, I couldn't recommend trying a weighted blanket highly enough.&#160;</p><div id=\"ProductCard_5e34376424306a7d6b4f7194\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe class=\"copyright\">Thomas Barwick/Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Job adverts that offer flexible hours could bring in 20% more women applicants, a new study by insurance giant Zurich has suggested.</li>\n<li>Gender-neutral language and flexible working options in Zurich's job adverts led to a 20% jump in women applying for management roles, and a 16% rise in href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A new study by insurance giant Zurich suggests advertising flexible hours on senior roles leads to more women applying.</p><p>The UK government-commissioned research studied Zurich job vacancies between March 2019 and February 2020. It found that a combination of gender-neutral language as well as flexible working options led to a near-20% jump in women applying for management roles.</p><p>It also triggered an overall 16% rise in women applying for jobs at the Swiss insurance firm, according to the <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/a-field-trial-with-zurich-insurance-to-advertise-all-jobs-as-part-time\">study</a>.</p><p>Zurich, which employs 4,500 in the UK and a total of 54,000 worldwide, became the first company in the UK in March 2019 to advertise part-time, job share, or flexible working options in all of their job vacancies.</p><p>Since changing the policy on job ad wording, the number of women hired for top jobs at Zurich has increased 33%, the study found.</p><p>The results form part of a wider UK government-commissioned study with think tank <a href=\"https://www.bi.team/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Behavioural Insights Team</a> and Zurich to discover the issues preventing women from progressing in their career.&#160;</p><p>The study revealed an initial lack of applications from women for senior Zurich jobs, many of which had not offered flexible working options.</p><p>The adverts offering flexible working hours attracted more applications from both males and females, suggesting flexibility was <a href=\"https://www.zurich.co.uk/en/about-us/media-centre/company-news/2020/zurich-sees-leap-in-women-applying-for-senior-roles-after-offering-all-jobs-as-flexible\">\"just as important\" for men</a>, the study said.</p><p>Steve Collinson, Zurich's head of HR, <a href=\"https://www.zurich.co.uk/en/about-us/media-centre/company-news/2020/zurich-sees-leap-in-women-applying-for-senior-roles-after-offering-all-jobs-as-flexible\">said</a> in a statement: \"We've seen hugely encouraging results, simply by adding six words to our job adverts.\"</p><p>\"By offering roles that fit flexibly around family life, employers could open the floodgates to a much wider pool of untapped talent. This will also help women progress into higher paid jobs whilst fitting other commitments around their careers,\" Collinson said.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/women-leaving-workforce-pandemic-workplace-report-mckinsey-lean-in-2020-9?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">One out of every four working women</a> is considering leaving their job or scaling back their careers, according to results from a study of around 40,000 employees by McKinsey and Co. in September.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a election","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/zuckerberg-dorsey-facebook-twitter-senate-hearing-hunter-biden-trump-election-2020-11","description":"<iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/OT3OgojnhFM\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Facebook CEO Mark Zuckerberg and Twitter CEO Jack Dorsey are testifying before the Senate Judiciary Committee Tuesday at 10 a.m. Eastern.</li>\n<li>Lawmakers are expected to grill the tech CEOs about how their platforms moderated content before and after Election Day.</li>\n<li>The hearing was scheduled last month after Facebook and Twitter temporarily restricted the spread of an unverified New York Post article about Joe Biden's son Hunter, which made its way to the Post through Rudy Giuliani, President Trump's personal lawyer.</li>\n<li>Republicans have accused the tech platforms of anti-conservative bias for that content moderation and for fact-checking false claims made by Trump, while Democrats have urged tech companies to crack down more harshly on misinformation.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Facebook CEO Mark Zuckerberg and Twitter CEO Jack Dorsey are testifying before the Senate Judiciary Committee Tuesday morning to answer questions about their platforms' handling of the 2020 election.</p><p>The two tech CEOs were summoned by Senate Republicans who were upset with the tech platforms' content moderation before and after the election. Facebook and Twitter have both added labels to posts made by President Donald Trump that falsely claimed victory in the election — Joe Biden <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/2020-election-results\">won the election</a> with 306 electoral votes — and spreading misinformation about voter fraud. Facebook also <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/facebook-political-advertising-ban-extended-memo-trump-spreads-election-misinformation-2020-11\">suspended all political ads</a> following the election to prevent the spread of false claims.&#160;</p><p>Republicans have argued that those warning labels amount to anti-conservative censorship, while Democrats have called on tech companies to more robustly crack down on hate speech and misinformation. On both sides of the aisle, lawmakers say tech companies should face more legal scrutiny.</p><p>The hearing comes as Republican leaders scramble to bolster Trump's claims that he actually won the election due to increasingly far-fetched theories — from a widespread conspiracy to \"rig\" the results to evidenceless claims that hundreds of thousands of votes were cast illegally. Rudy Giuliani, the president's personal lawyer who <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-campaign-lawsuits-election-results-2020-11\">is leading Trump's lawsuits</a> challenging the election, was linked to a story about Joe Biden's son in the New York Post that Facebook and Twitter both temporarily restricted last month amid questions about its accuracy.</p><p>Senate Judiciary chair Lindsay Graham, a South Carolina Republican, has also taken an outsize role in that push — Georgia's Republican Secretary of State <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/lindsey-graham-pressured-georgia-top-election-official-to-toss-ballots-2020-11\">said Monday</a> that Graham pressured him to find ways to discard legally cast ballots as the state conducts a hand recount this week.</p><p>Lawmakers are also expected to grill Zuckerberg and Dorsey about whether their companies should retain legal protections afforded by Section 230, a law that shields social media sites from being held liable for users' posts in the way that publishers are responsible for content they produce.</p><p>\"When it comes to social media platforms and Section 230, change is going to come,\" Graham said in his opening statement at the hearing Tuesday.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a (Aaron Holmes)","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn83@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-54-041_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=_iyZhQ3B_II:IIJpGst6V_0:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn80@2020_1/2020/11/17/16-31-51-541_1ae88282da99993e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=_iyZhQ3B_II:IIJpGst6V_0:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn52@2020_2/2020/11/17/16-31-49-882_7781037aa0a7cc16.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn96@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-50-199_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=_iyZhQ3B_II:IIJpGst6V_0:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn20@2020_1/2020/11/17/16-31-55-398_8548404ea56e4d27.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/_iyZhQ3B_II":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn100@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-47-692_170a12f2a70fb345.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630688400},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"4 trends in technology that emerged during the pandemic and are here to stay","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-trends-that-will-remain-popular-post-pandemic-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e8de44a29d6d9403f14d215?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman laptop working remote work home office\" height=\"4080\" width=\"6144\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Corporate leaders can focus on these trends to stay competitive and growing post-pandemic.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ridofranz/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The pandemic brought on a slew of changes including teleconferencing, remote work, and other tech innovations.&#160;</li>\n<li>Trends like automation, artificial intelligence, and touchless products and services are expected to shape our future workforces.</li>\n<li>Employees will need regular support and training on platforms and technologies to meet heightened job demands, while companies need to oversee any automation or AI processes to ensure a continued smooth transition.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p dir=\"ltr\">Last year, 2020 was heralded as the exciting start of the century's third decade. Today, its conclusion can't come fast enough for most entrepreneurs. Yet the recent sweeping societal and corporate changes likely won't subside when the calendar hits 2021. In fact, they've altered life for the foreseeable future, and that's not all bad for businesses.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Case in point: Teleconferencing — <a href=\"https://www.inc.com/minda-zetlin/bill-gates-predictions-zoom-teams-videoconferencing-screen-size.html\">predicted long ago by Bill Gates</a> — has risen as an acceptable alternative to professional meetings and casual hangouts. As a result, Zoom's busting at the seams and <a href=\"https://www.inc.com/jason-aten/zoom-is-already-where-we-do-pretty-much-everything-it-just-got-even-better-at-it.html\">adding new perks and amenities</a>. And who could deny that many employees and companies are now&#160;<a href=\"https://www.inc.com/justin-bariso/microsofts-new-6-word-remote-work-policy-is-brilliant-heres-why-your-company-should-steal-it.html\">seeing remote work with fresh eyes</a>?</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Gartner research from July&#160;<a href=\"https://www.gartner.com/en/newsroom/press-releases/2020-07-14-gartner-survey-reveals-82-percent-of-company-leaders-plan-to-allow-employees-to-work-remotely-some-of-the-time\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">showed 82% of executives</a>&#160;surveyed expected to allow telecommuting in some fashion post-pandemic. Even Google has&#160;<a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/07/27/google-is-first-major-company-to-extend-work-from-home-to-summer-2021.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">backed off from an in-person headquarters mentality</a>, allowing some team members to work from home until at least mid-2021.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Virtual working and coronavirus-linked workforce transformations have ushered in some massive tech innovations and opportunities. Consequently, corporate leaders should keep an eye on the following trends aimed at swiftly adapting to tomorrow's norms.</p><p dir=\"ltr\"><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-build-company-wellness-program-employees-healthy-motivated-2020-8\">How to build a comprehensive wellness program that keeps employees happy, healthy, and motivated for the long haul</a></em></p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">1. Remote workers requiring savvier back-end support and training</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">When COVID struck and workers decentralized en masse, work-home boundaries blurred. This phenomenon of \"work is everywhere and nowhere\" will continue as people lean toward more hybrid, fluid methods of balancing the professional and the personal.&#160;</p><p dir=\"ltr\">A boundary-less business world isn't necessarily conducive to buoyed worker confidence, however, especially when workers must rapidly make pivotal decisions without immediate managerial support. Employees therefore need to undergo regular training on platforms and tech they regularly use.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">IT staff will especially require heavy doses of regular education to meet heightened job demands. Yet Inc. 5000's IBEX IT Business Experts CEO and president Tracey Grace&#160;<a href=\"https://www.under30ceo.com/tech-expert-tracey-grace-on-cybersecurity-and-work-from-home-culture/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">believes</a>&#160;ongoing tech knowledge shouldn't be limited to information systems or IT personnel. Instead, all corporate system end users should be taught to recognize and mitigate security breaches so that everyone's empowered to make wise choices.</p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">2. Next-gen levels of automation</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">Automation has gone into hyperdrive with employees clamoring for better, faster ways to make their lives easier by mechanizing everyday processes in order to concentrate on more complex to-do items. As Placester COO and cofounder Fred Townes <a href=\"https://www.businessnewsdaily.com/9835-automation-tech-workforce.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">noted</a>, any repetitive task can be the catalyst for an automated solution.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">This doesn't mean there isn't a downside to automation, particularly when it comes to customer experience. Too much automation can lead to a drop in personalization, which sometimes leaves prospects and clients with an unsettled feeling.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">To combat the need for hyper-automation without losing the human touch, automated functions may benefit from occasional babysitting. Rather than truly being set-it-and-forget-it processes, they should be checked and tweaked. For example, an automated flurry of prospective buyer touch points could be regularly dusted off and retested with target personas. Just a bit of maintenance can ensure automation does what's intended.</p><p dir=\"ltr\"><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mailchimp-set-clear-goals-key-managing-remote-teams-2020-8\">Mailchimp's chief product officer says clarifying priorities should be your number one focus when managing a 100% remote team — here's how to start setting clear, actionable goals</a></em></p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">3. Predictive emotional AI</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">Imagine a machine that could gauge a user's emotions to determine which message to show next. This type of predictive AI, known as artificial emotional intelligence, is coming down the pike faster all the time. In fact, it's <a href=\"https://www.searchenginejournal.com/what-is-artificial-emotional-intelligence/255769/#close\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">been in the testing phases for years</a>.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">As AI becomes more adept at reading a prospective shopper's emotions, AI programming can assist in influencing behaviors. And the AI doesn't have to rely only on visual cues, either. Already, AI chatbots are learning to recognize when buyers are frustrated or may want to opt out by the words and punctuation they choose.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">The biggest challenge with predictive artificial emotional intelligence lies in successfully interpreting signals. It's a fact of life that different people from different cultures will have different responses to the same stimuli, even if they share an overarching emotion. Therefore, until AI can prove itself to be airtight, marketers will still want to regulate and oversee this&#160;emergent technology.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Nevertheless, the idea of using AI to analyze everything from a raised eyebrow to a slight frown could give companies an edge. AI facial recognition equipment might one day be useful in retail situations to help reduce buyer hesitance and improve conversions.</p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">4. Touchless everything</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">A final tech trend that's taken off during the pandemic has been a move toward touchless-ness. Restaurants are touting curbside, contactless pickup. Retailers are offering touchless payment options. And more touch-free transactions are sure to come.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">However, not all organizations offer products or services that are conducive to being without touch. Being able to feel a pricey cashmere sweater can make the difference for a sale.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Before companies embrace a fully contactless society, they may need to consider other safe alternatives in order to give buyers and browsers a choice. Already, this is happening with self-checkouts and&#160;<a href=\"https://www.ultraleap.com/enterprise/touchless-interfaces/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">touchless ordering screen interfaces</a>&#160;to some extent.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">The coronavirus may have stunted economic growth, but it didn't stunt tech innovation. As companies slide into 2021, corporate leaders will be faced with a bevy of technological choices to remain competitive, enhance growth, and win back sales.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"5 ways you can still get things done with a disorganized boss","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/tips-for-getting-things-done-with-disorganized-boss-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e346d3e62fa814ead0ae616?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Woman talking to boss\" height=\"2200\" width=\"3300\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You can offer to organize your boss&#39;s files or ask meaningful questions.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Barwick/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Starting a new job can be challenging, but it can be especially tough if your boss is disorganized.</li>\n<li>Take some time to understand the work flows and team dynamics before changing everything to match your work style.</li>\n<li>Reach out to coworkers or previous people in your position, but be wary of building connections or bonding over your boss' shortcomings.&#160;</li>\n<li>Set clear parameters, questions, or expectations when asking your boss for help to keep them on track and focused on the problem at hand.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>You're excited about your new job. The pay is good, the office setting is comfortable, and the commute is easy. But as you start the actual work, you confront an unsettling truth: A&#160;disorganized boss&#160;is at the helm.</p><p>He hasn't mapped out a plan for your first few days or weeks. He doesn't give you any guidance on the projects you'll need to tackle. He can't find the papers he needs you to fax or sign. He hasn't introduced you to potential key allies in the company. It doesn't take long to wonder how you'll survive without (A) going nuts or (B) going completely nuts.</p><p>Have no fear. We found organization and communication experts to offer some tips to help you keep your cool, get up to speed, and make the most of this train wreck of a&#160;situation.</p><h2><strong>Start slow</strong></h2><p>\"Most&#160;<a href=\"https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/what-to-do-if-your-boss-is-incompetent\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">disorganized bosses</a> know they are disorganized and scattered,\" said Santa Barbara business coach Clay Nelson. \"Do not walk into this and start changing things or channeling everything through you. You need to find out how to keep the flow going, what the possibility is inside the thinking of your boss. Then, slowly start shifting how things are working in very small increments, and make sure you have your boss's approval.\"</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/i-was-the-first-employee-of-startup-what-i-learned-2019-7\">I was the first employee of a huge startup. Here's my advice to anyone thinking about joining an early-stage company.</a></em></p><h2><strong>Do your due diligence</strong></h2><p>Philadelphia-based organization consultant Liz Bywater advocates doing some research before you begin the full-court press to&#160;<a href=\"https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/managing-up-mary-abbajay\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reform your boss</a>. \"Get a lay of the land from those who already work there,\" she said. Speak to the person who formerly held your position if you can, as well as your existing coworkers, to gain their insight into your boss's MO.</p><h2><strong>Listen up</strong></h2><p>\"Listen to verbal cues when your boss is in a panic and looking for that report,\" said Laura Leist, coauthor of the book \"Eliminate Chaos\" and president and founder of a Seattle company by the same name.</p><p>Leist also suggests&#160;<a href=\"https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/Five-Ways-to-Stay-Organized\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">offering to organize</a>&#160;your boss's files for him and to ask plenty of questions along the way. This will ensure the filing system you help to create is actually useful and meaningful to your boss.</p><h2><strong>Work the network</strong></h2><p>Jeanne Hurlbert, a sociology professor at Louisiana State University and president of Optinet Resources in Baton Rouge, Louisiana, suggests establishing a support network. \"New employees need to build relationships with coworkers anyway,\" Hurlbert said. Working with a disorganized boss, \"however, exacerbates the need for that.\"</p><p>What a new employee shouldn't do is \"start off making negative comments about the boss or thinking that shared antipathy toward the boss provides good common ground on which to build relationships,\" she said. \"That's dangerous.\"</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/resources-resesarch-help-prepare-job-interview-2020-9\">The smartest candidates always use these 5 resources when prepping for interviews, according to an executive recruiter who's interviewed thousands of applicants.</a></em></p><h2><strong>Lead by example</strong></h2><p>The best defense is a good offense, so Studio City, California-based Bill Bliesath, also known as the&#160;<a href=\"http://www.theorganizingguy.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Organizing Guy</a>, suggests making sure&#160;<a href=\"https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/get-organized-at-work\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">you are as organized as possible</a>. \"When you have questions about your responsibilities or projects, present them by topic in an order that flows smoothly and requires the minimal amount of input — i.e., yes or no answers,\" Bliesath said. \"Disorganized people tend to lose focus easily if there are no clear parameters or expectations. So you want to stay on the subject, and if the conversation strays, keep steering it back on track — with a smile of course.\"</p><p>One final thought from Nelson: \"The boss wouldn't be the boss — unorganized or not — if he/she weren't successful at what he/she does. So you don't want to mess with how that success gets done. You do want to be the person that makes that success come about easier.\"</p><p>That said if a disorganized boss is impeding your own personal career development, it's time to look for a job elsewhere.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/tips-for-getting-things-done-with-disorganized-boss-2020-11'>Business The company's stock is up about 335% year-to-date, compared to the broader S&#38;P 500's 11% rise.</p><p>On December 21, the company will join the prestigious S&#38;P 500 index — one of the most important measures of success of America's largest publicly-traded firms.</p><p>Founder and CEO <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/elon-musk-wealth-rockets-billion-tesla-sp-500-inclusion-2020-11-1029809564\">Elon Musk's wealth grew by $15 billion</a> to about $117 billion after the announcement, when its stock rose 15% in after-hours trading. homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul><p>Facebook CEO Mark Zuckerberg and Twitter CEO Jack Dorsey will appear in front of Congress on Tuesday for a virtual <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/zuckerberg-dorsey-facebook-twitter-senate-hearing-hunter-biden-trump-election-2020-11\">hearing on how the social media companies moderate content</a>. The hearing will be live-streamed starting at 10 a.m. ET Tuesday on the <a href=\"https://www.judiciary.senate.gov/meetings/breaking-the-news-censorship-suppression-and-the-2020-election\">Senate Judiciary Committee's website</a>.</p><p>The Senate Judiciary Committee scheduled the hearing following a New York Post story, published on October 14 about Joe Biden's son, which contained dubious claims that Hunter Biden was working with Ukrainian officials. Twitter and Facebook's handling of the article fueled the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-happened-twitter-ny-post-biden-moderation-policies-2020-10\">right's ongoing, oft-disproven theory</a> that the tech industry discriminates against conservative content on their platforms, a notion that President Donald Trump has amplified since Twitter began fact-checking his posts in May. Republican lawmakers will likely grill the tech leaders over what they say is censorship of right-leaning posts.</p><p>As <a href=\"https://www.cnet.com/news/facebook-twitter-ceos-to-visit-congress-again-how-to-watch-on-tuesday/\">CNET</a> notes, Vice President-elect Kamala Harris will be in attendance at the hearing and will also question the CEOs.&#160;</p><p>Twitter responded to the Post's article by immediately banning the story's URL without an explanation. The company later said the ban was due to its policies on how hacked materials are shared on its site, but Dorsey eventually issued an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/twitter-jack-dorsey-blocking-ny-post-hunter-biden-story-wrong-2020-10\">apology</a> and said the decision was \"wrong.\" Facebook didn't ban the story, but it did restrict its reach until third-party fact-checkers could verify its claims. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/senators-to-subpoena-twitter-ceo-dorsey-after-hunter-biden-articles-2020-10\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"1b6ebf761a40bcc4b1db0d0cb96a9c54\">Republicans subpoenaed Dorsey</a> following his company's ban of the story, and he willingly agreed to testify on Tuesday.</p><p>Tuesday's hearing comes on the heels of a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/zuckerberg-dorsey-section-230-could-harm-internet-free-speech-2020-10\">late-October Senate hearing</a>, when lawmakers grilled Dorsey, Zuckerberg, and Google CEO Sundar Pichai over the protections afforded to them by Section 230, an internet law that prevents them from being liable for content that people post on their platforms. Revising the law has largely been a bipartisan issue, but while Democrats wish to strip it back in an effort to limit misinformation and hate speech, Republicans wish to do so to crack down on what they believe is anti-conservative bias.</p><p>Democratic Sen. Brian Schatz used his entire allotted time during the October hearing to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/senator-chatz-section-230-tech-hearing-dorsey-zuckerberg-pichai-sham-2020-10\">accuse Republicans</a> of politicizing Section 230 protections.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a $300 and sold out rapidly. \n   <p class=\"copyright\">Home Depot</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\"> \n <li><strong>Home Deport has seen record sales numbers as the pandemic has kept customers home and led to a surge in home improvement projects.&nbsp;</strong></li> \n <li><strong>The company's latest quarter was particularly big, and few items symbolize that success better than the wildly popular 12-foot skeleton: Executives say it sold out before October even started, despite a $300 price tag.</strong></li> \n <li><strong>\"Halloween was the strongest event we've ever had,\" Home Depot executives said on an investor call Tuesday morning.</strong></li> \n <li><strong><a href=\"http://www.businessinsider.com/\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories.</a></strong></li> \n</ul>\n<p>In a year like 2020, it's no surprise that a lot of people were in the market for a 12-foot giant skeleton.</p>\n<p>The absolutely massive Halloween decoration <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/home-depot-12-foot-skeleton-halloween-inspiration-2020-10\">went viral this year</a>, and was so popular with Home Depot shoppers that it sold out before Halloween month even began.</p>\n<p>Home Depot was the only place carrying the bony behemoth, and it helped to drive <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/home-depot-earnings-staff-pay-sales-beat-analsyt-predictions-covid-2020-11\">record Halloween sales for the company</a>.&nbsp;</p>\n<p>\"Customers responded to our larger assortment of animatronics, inflatables, and yard decor, as evidenced by our 12-foot giant skeleton, which sold out before October, helping drive a record sell through for the event,\" Home Depot executives said on an investor call Tuesday morning.</p>\n<p>The company has seen huge sales increases throughout the year due to increased pandemic spending on home goods, maintenance, and DIY projects — <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/home-depot-earnings-staff-pay-sales-beat-analsyt-predictions-covid-2020-11\">increases which continued in its most recent quarter</a>: Overall net sales beat analyst estimates, increasing 23.2% to $33.54 billion.</p>\n<p>Home Depot's Halloween event was a particularly strong driver of that growth, spurred by the massive success of Mr. Bones.&nbsp;</p>\n<p>\"Halloween was the strongest event we've ever had,\" executives said. Despite the ongoing pandemic's impact on employment and income, shoppers turned out more than ever for Halloween decorations. To help explain why that is, he compared holidays in 2020 to \"what we've historically seen in storm markets.\"&nbsp;</p>\n<p>Though people are looking for supplies to survive and rebuild, they're also looking for \"some kind of normalcy.\" And in 2020, a 12-foot giant skeleton helped to do just that.</p>\n<p><em><strong>Got a tip?</strong>&nbsp;Contact Business Insider senior correspondent Ben Gilbert via email (<a href=\"mailto:bgilbert@businessinsider.com\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">bgilbert@businessinsider.com</a>),</em><em>&nbsp;or Twitter DM (<a href=\"https://twitter.com/RealBenGilbert\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">@realbengilbert</a>). +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5fb3eb8b3ad3bb3a542bceac?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"538a351dce150a8a545441ed7f151f2c","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn17@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-44-675_e5f8f6ae225b8547.webp","destWidth":4949,"destHeight":3712,"sourceBytes":1305868,"destBytes":1305868,"author":"insider@insider.com Gilbert)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fb3ea0484aa3036c339d8c4?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn44@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-48-790_761ea7cfb5dff75a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn83@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-54-041_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=2ySeOdSAP0M:L5aboh_UGpM:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn35@2020_1/2020/11/17/16-31-49-616_5161fe458ab28dd8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=2ySeOdSAP0M:L5aboh_UGpM:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn35@2020_5/2020/11/17/16-31-47-980_ae189876fbfaf664.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn96@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-50-199_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=2ySeOdSAP0M:L5aboh_UGpM:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn32@2020_5/2020/11/17/16-31-47-218_ee9f8b79707b5417.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/2ySeOdSAP0M":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn47@2020_2/2020/11/17/16-31-45-541_676c238bd0987004.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630688503},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"Pauline Ducruet isn't so different from other 26-year-old entrepreneurs — she just happens to be Grace Kelly's granddaughter","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/pauline-ducruet-talks-gender-neutral-clothing-entrepreneurship-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8d8db59e9fe4001900a02f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Pauline Ducruet\" height=\"2666\" width=\"3555\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Pauline Ducruet\n<p class=\"copyright\">Photo by Francois Durand/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Pauline Ducruet, 26, is the founder of the gender-neutral fashion line, <a href=\"https://alter-designs.com\">Alter Designs</a>.&#160;</li>\n<li>Born and raised in Monaco, Ducruet is a granddaughter of Grace Kelly.</li>\n<li>Like entrepreneurs without royal lineage, she went to college before working internships that led to her launching a business.</li>\n<li>In an interview with Business Insider, she describes why gender-neutral fashion is the future of the industry, why sustainability is so important, and the pressure that comes with being from her family.</li>\n<li>\"My work has to be irreproachable,\" she says.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Pauline Ducruet, 26, isn't so different from most young entrepreneurs these days.</p><p>After college, she bounced around a bunch of jobs after a series of internships and got to the point where she was ready to launch her own business, and she spent two years getting it on its feet.</p><p>Then she was met with the sudden, forceful winds of the pandemic.&#160;</p><p>Most entrepreneurs don't have quite her family background, though. Born and raised in Monaco, Ducruet is a granddaughter of Grace Kelly through her mother, Princess Stéphanie of Monaco. A member of the Monegasque Royal Family, her uncle is reigning monarch Prince Albert II of Monaco, and&#160;she is 16th in line to the throne.</p><p>Ducruet's business, founded in 2019, is Alter Designs, a gender-neutral fashion brand she says she self-funded. She's obviously grateful to have her family background, but she also said it's added to the pressure of running her own business.</p><p>\"My work has to be irreproachable,\" she said.&#160;</p><p>The brand is gender-neutral, she told Business Insider, because she wanted her clothes to be for everyone. Personally, she said she loves unisex clothing and likes to wear men and women's clothes equally. It also embraced sustainability years before the pandemic challenged most fashion lines' bottom line.</p><p>And she told Business Insider that she got her start just like any other entrepreneur.</p><h2>Internships and climbing the ranks</h2><p>After holding internships at Vogue and Louis Vuitton, Ducreut worked as a stylist's apprentice at the Istituto Marangoni in Paris, and graduated from the prestigious Parsons School of Design in New York in 2017, with a degree in fashion.</p><p>From the start, Alter only used natural fibers such as pesticide-free silk and cotton in its clothing. The brand especially employs a lot of upcycling, meaning she reuses old fashion products so she doesn't have to produce much herself. She buys dead stalks of leather and denim and reuses them, so much of her inventory was never going to go to waste this year — everything was always going to be reused.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8d8f28c21cfb0019468b2b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Pauline Ducruet\" height=\"4146\" width=\"5528\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Pierre Suu / Contributor / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Alter sells products such as <a href=\"https://alter-designs.com/produit/apron/\">$292 denim skirts</a> and <a href=\"https://alter-designs.com/produit/draped-tunic/\">$759 satin draped tunics</a>. Her first collection was presented in Paris in 2019.</p><p>Right now, Alter Designs is direct-to-consumer and eCommerce only, but the brand does do pop-up shops — an important part of her strategy in terms of connecting and growing her consumer base. Ducruet declined to disclose the finances for her business, citing the pandemic. \"Doing it all by myself, for now, it's a really hard rhythm to keep up,\" she said. \"I wanted to slow down a little bit.\"</p><p>The brand would have been celebrating the one-year anniversary of its first collection this past June, but the pandemic didn't just interrupt that — it forced the whole company to move.&#160;</p><h2><strong>Less than a year after opening her business, the pandemic almost ended it for good</strong></h2><p>Ducruet is usually based in New York, but she left the US in February to return to Monaco, just a few weeks before the EU <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/eu-opens-up-to-some-travelers-but-not-americans-11593524652\">shut its borders</a> for non-essential travel due to the pandemic.</p><p>Once she landed back in Monaco, Ducruet realized it might be years before she would be able to successfully bring her business back to the US, so she decided to move the entire production of her fashion line to France, which posed certain challenges. \"Monaco is such a tiny country,\" she said. \"We don't have factories here.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8d8ee2c21cfb0019468b2a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Pauline Ducruet\" height=\"3000\" width=\"3999\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Pauline Ducruet dressing a model.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Francois Durand / Stringer / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>This meant she had to, once again, find suppliers and factories that could house her collections. All when <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-italy-coronavirus-lockdown-is-impacting-luxury-industry-2020-3\">factories were already shutting down</a> worldwide and when the fashion and retail industries were taking huge hits from the pandemic.</p><p>In February, Boston Consulting Group and Bernstein <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-italy-coronavirus-lockdown-is-impacting-luxury-industry-2020-3\">estimated that the luxury sector</a> could lose nearly $45 billion in sales in 2020.&#160;</p><p>\"It was basically starting from scratch and it was challenging,\" Ducruet said. \"Especially as a young brand, you put all your effort into the people that do your pattern-making and sewing and everything.\"</p><p>The result? She adjusted the amount of clothing she produced and decided to sit out of Paris Fashion Week as she figured out the next steps for her brand. \"I've decided that I'm only going to do one collection a year. There's not going to be seasons now. It's just going to be a collection per year.\"&#160;</p><p>This will help the brand become even more sustainable, as it will cut down on&#160;excessive waste and on any extra inventory, especially as she continues adjusting her operations to keep her brand afloat during the pandemic.</p><h2>How to deal with a spotlight from a famous family? Emphasizing brand values</h2><p>Ducruet acknowledged that she has clearly benefited from the fact that her mother is a princess, and she is a member of a&#160;royal family.&#160;</p><p>\"People were following the family for years and years and years,\" she said. \"I have the spotlight on the brand, so that was a great thing, obviously, but I think it's also hard because then you put the spotlight on the bad things as well.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9c285d69331a0011bc64b8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Pauline Ducruet\" height=\"3266\" width=\"4354\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Pauline Ducruet, Princess Stephanie of Monaco, Prince Albert II of Monaco, Louis Ducruet and Camille Gottlieb\n<p class=\"copyright\">SC Pool - Corbis/Corbis via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Other notable members of the Monegasque royal family include the Casiraghi siblings, one of whom married billionaire heiress Tatiana Santo Domingo of the Santo Domingo Family — <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tatiana-santo-domingo-billionaire-richest-citizen-heiress-monaco-royal-family-2019-10\">she is reportedly now the richest citizen in Monaco,</a> with a net worth of $2 billion. There's also <a href=\"https://www.tatler.com/article/monaco-royal-louis-ducruet-nottingham-forest-football-job\">Ducruet's brother Louis</a>, who was just tapped to become an advisor for international projects at the UK football club Nottingham Forest.</p><p>Monaco overall is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/royal-family-monaco-net-worth-lifestyle-home-photos-2019-6\">one of the wealthiest nations in the world</a>, and it <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mind-blowing-facts-about-monaco-wealth-2019-5\">has a poverty rate of zero</a>. About 32% of the population is made of up millionaires. It has even been nicknamed \"<a href=\"https://www.mansionglobal.com/articles/buyers-in-monte-carlo-have-access-to-a-billionaires-playground-202155\">Billionaires Playground</a>\" — her uncle Prince Albert II has a reported net worth of $1 billion, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/royal-family-net-worth-europe-ranked-2018-5#4-queen-elizabeth-ii-england-7\">double the estimated net worth</a> of Queen Elizabeth II.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8d90939e9fe4001900a039?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Pauline Ducruet\" height=\"5084\" width=\"6778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Pauline Ducruet at her pop up show in Paris.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Pierre Suu/Getty Images / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The brand has been putting much of its time into developing \"inclusive\" marketing campaigns, Ducruet says.</p><p>For example, the brand recently did a campaign called \"Beyond Genders\" which saw Alter Designs reach out to the LGBTQ+ community and get their insights on gender fluidity, as well as comments on how they feel they are being represented in the world of fashion.</p><p>\"I like to give content about the real people that are representing Alter,\" she said. \"It's a brand that's here for the people, and to put light on the personality of everyone that is wearing it.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8d8f079e9fe4001900a033?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Pauline Ducruet\" height=\"3181\" width=\"4242\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Pauline Ducruet at her pop up show in  Monaco.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Arnold Jerocki / Stringer / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>She has been using social media to appeal to a \"small community\" of people who genuinely like the brand, but for the most part, she said she doesn't depend on it too heavily to market her work.</p><p>She doesn't pay influencers or content creators, and when asked if she is on TikTok, she admits she's not even sure if she knows how to use the platform. \"I feel like I'm a real millennial,\" she says. \"I'm still learning how to use it.\" &#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8d8f979e9fe4001900a034?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Pauline Ducruet\" height=\"3610\" width=\"4814\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Stephanie of Monaco,Pauline Ducruet and Charlotte Casiraghi attend the Alter Design Menswear Spring Summer 2020 show as part of Paris Fashion Week on June 18, 2019 in Paris, France.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Pierre Suu / Contributor / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>She says she has learned throughout the past year the importance of creating values for a business — and then really sticking to them.&#160;</p><p>\"In fashion, obviously the clothes and the quality of the clothes are really, really important,\" she continued. \"But sticking to the values and the image that you set for yourself and the brand is also important. I would even say more important than the clothes itself.\"&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Davis)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f8d8db59e9fe4001900a02f?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn24@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-42-022_4fc0837261f63561.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f8d8f28c21cfb0019468b2b?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn40@2020_5/2020/11/17/16-31-52-170_55053d66c071a2b2.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f8d8ee2c21cfb0019468b2a?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn87@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-50-849_a26a4ceb7b976e33.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f9c285d69331a0011bc64b8?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn20@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-53-101_8278b9607813fe91.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f8d90939e9fe4001900a039?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn15@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-55-512_9cd8c485759a3915.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f8d8f079e9fe4001900a033?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn31@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-55-039_d112596529490db0.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f8d8f979e9fe4001900a034?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn43@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-49-614_2ae58aa0d5892366.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn83@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-54-041_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=EAwsJ5iY8GA:gpvKY6-kKYs:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn11@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-45-798_c875268c906eca5a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=EAwsJ5iY8GA:gpvKY6-kKYs:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn23@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-46-922_87590d73f6650f9b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn96@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-50-199_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=EAwsJ5iY8GA:gpvKY6-kKYs:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn64@2020_5/2020/11/17/16-31-47-241_e970a92288e508fb.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/EAwsJ5iY8GA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn87@2020_2/2020/11/17/16-31-48-478_e193e5bc5fc32a8c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630688445},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"I was a Democratic poll challenger in Detroit. I watched the absentee vote count and can assure you that Trump and the GOP's fraud claims are nonsense.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/detroit-poll-challenger-trump-gop-voter-fraud-ballot-allegations-absurd-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faed379402d49001924edd3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"detroit votes\" height=\"487\" width=\"975\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Election challengers watching through a window after being told the capacity for election challengers had been met at a vote-counting location at TCF Center in Detroit on November 4.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/election-challengers-watche-through-a-window-after-being-news-photo/1229460734?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Elaine Cromie/Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Absentee ballots were counted accurately and securely in Detroit.</li>\n<li>Republican challengers were in the room at all times.</li>\n<li>GOP challenges were an extension of their national strategy of suppression.</li>\n<li>Ned Staebler was a Democratic poll challenger at TCF Center in Detroit on November 4.</li>\n<li>This is an opinion column. The thoughts expressed are those of the author.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Just two days after Election Day, President Donald Trump stood at the podium of the White House press briefing room and levied numerous baseless claims about the legitimacy of <a href=\"https://www.fox2detroit.com/news/trump-lambastes-detroit-in-ballot-counting-criticism-calling-it-corrupt\">absentee vote counting in Detroit</a>. The city is a stronghold for Michigan Democrats and helped tip the scales toward the eventual president-elect, Joe Biden, in our state.</p><p>After listening to the president's attacks on the process in the city, I want to share what I observed over 15 hours as a Democratic Party ballot challenger at TCF Center, the city's site for processing absentee ballots. Given the level of misinformation circulating about what went on inside TCF — much of it perpetuated by our president — I want to set the record straight.</p><h2>The ballot-counting process</h2><p>I went to TCF after I learned that throngs of Republican challengers had begun arriving there at about midnight on election night. My mandate — the same for all challengers regardless of affiliation — was to observe the process, raise a challenge if I had a legitimate reason to believe the law was not being followed, and contest any baseless challenges raised by others.</p><p>I saw election staff members working incredibly hard to count 165,000 absentee ballots in two days. For context, that's nearly three times as many as were processed in 2016.</p><p>The election workers were professional, efficient, diligent, and dedicated. They were working in a fishbowl with, at times, eight or 10 people crowding around them and yelling and harassing them about their work. These predominantly older, Black women wore masks and risked exposure to COVID-19 in a city that for much of the spring was a COVID-19 hot spot. They didn't get paid very much, but they never complained. They were heroes.</p><p>I also saw diverse and dedicated Democratic and nonpartisan volunteers. Our job was simple: Do everything we could (within the law) to shield the election workers from a withering barrage of unwarranted abuse from our GOP counterparts.</p><p>Repeatedly, we called supervisors and even police officers to blunt the attempts of the GOP challengers to slow, stop, muddy, or otherwise derail the process. We didn't have much to eat. We wore the wrong shoes. Our phones were dead or dying the whole time. We alternated between way too hot or too cold. But, through it all, we were laser focused on protecting our Democracy.</p><h2>The GOP got their challengers, despite what they claim</h2><p>That brings me to the final group of people I saw: the GOP poll challengers. In contrast to our goal, a speedy and secure tabulation of legal ballots, they had a single mission: to slow down or stop the counting as much as possible.</p><p>They had been told and were exhorted repeatedly by Republican organizers throughout the day to \"be more aggressive.\" They bullied. They complained. They <a href=\"https://www.freep.com/story/news/politics/elections/2020/11/02/poll-challengers-removed-detroit-ballot-processing-begins/6122976002/\">accused everyone of fraud</a>. They documented everything. They challenged everything. At times they challenged ballots before the ballots were even opened. At times, they tried to \"blanket\" challenge thousands of ballots at a time for some ridiculous reason or another. Blanket challenges are not legal.</p><p>When one of their <a href=\"https://www.wxyz.com/news/problems-arise-as-challengers-descend-up-detroits-tcf-center-not-allowed-in-due-to-capacity\">challengers was removed</a> for physically intimidating election workers and refusing after multiple warnings from supervisors to stop, the entire floor of workers cheered.</p><p>Why? Because these largely white, suburban, and rural challengers hurled insult after insult at hardworking, predominantly Black Detroiters — mostly women — simply trying to do their difficult jobs.</p><p>They accused them of fraud. They attacked their competence and their motives and their professionalism. They <a href=\"https://www.freep.com/story/news/politics/elections/2020/11/04/tcf-center-challengers-detroit-michigan/6164715002/\">stood too close</a>. They leaned in and over workers in the middle of a pandemic. They were <a href=\"https://www.bridgemi.com/guest-commentary/first-person-i-was-detroit-poll-challenger-gop-came-make-havoc\">rude and at times downright threatening</a>. One was removed for asserting his First and Second Amendment rights (think about that for a minute) in response to a request to step back a couple of feet.</p><p>Claims that GOP challengers were denied access to the room are utter nonsense. Each party was allowed 134 challengers (one for each table), in addition to lawyers. At one point <a href=\"https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/factcheck/2020/11/10/fact-check-videos-crowd-locked-out-detroit-center-lack-context/6195038002/\">at least 230 Republican challengers</a> were signed into the room, and access to the room was stopped for everyone because the room was at capacity. This caused <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/joe-biden-donald-trump-michigan-elections-detroit-1eb5f7ea8cbfb0031769e300f4d529ce\">the GOP to file a lawsuit</a>. Ironically, they filmed an interview about this lawsuit with the media from inside the room they claimed they were denied access to.</p><p>The entire process was a microcosm of the current dynamic between our two parties. The GOP wants to disenfranchise and discourage and suppress democracy. The Democratic Party wants everyone to be empowered in the process and their voice and vote to matter.</p><p>My experience inside TCF only further underscored for me the work that needs to be done to fight voter suppression in America. But it also gave me hope for the future of this effort. I saw a lot of ugliness in that room, but I also saw a diverse group of people — Black and white and Asian and Hispanic, students and retirees, union reps, voting-rights activists, community organizers, people of all religions, and folks from the entire gamut of sexual identity and expression — working hard to protect the Democratic process and ensure every legal vote in that room was counted.</p><p>I entered TCF at 9 a.m. and left 15 hours later, hungry, exhausted and clear that our efforts were not the end to the process, but another step forward in the movement to ensure that in every city and every community of color across America, every vote counts.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a He will be succeeded by Jim Esposito, Goldman's global co-head of its global markets division, who will step into Lemkau's role on Jan. 1.</br></br></p>\n  <p>Lemkau's exit and Esposito's move to co-head the investment banking division means that Wall Street's top bank for mergers and acquisitions will be led by two people with experience in other areas.</p>\n  <p><strong style=\"color: #000000;\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/gregg-lemkau-departing-goldman-sachs-banking-michael-dell-msd-partners-2020-11\">Read the full memos the bank sent about the exit.</a></strong></p>\n </section>\n <hr>\n  <section>\n   <section>\n    <section>\n     <h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-bank-akoya-data-sharing-aggregator-api-agreement-plaid-yodlee-2020-11\">Akoya, a data aggregator backed by major banks, just nabbed its first client</a></h2>\n     <figure> \n      <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2d6fa402d49001924f36d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Gareth Gaston US Bank\" height=\"1329\" width=\"2659\" charset=\"\"> \n       <figcaption> \n        <p class=\"copyright\">US Bank</p> \n       </figcaption> </img>\n     </figure>\n     <p>Data aggregators like Plaid and Yodlee were born out of the need to efficiently distribute data between fintechs and banks, serving as the the pipes behind the fintech revolution. But a new competitor is making a push to set a common data-sharing standard.&nbsp;</p>\n     <p>Originally created at financial-services giant Fidelity in 2018,&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/fidelitys-parent-company-is-spinning-out-its-akoya-personal-data-startup-11582202940\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"5d53faa607a9b73216afedfac2c198b8\">Akoya was spun out earlier this year</a>. src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ec44de23f7370099064a2dd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"home depot\" height=\"1335\" width=\"1999\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Home Depot has benefited from a surge in sales during the pandemic.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Luis Cortes/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Home Depot Inc said Tuesday it will spend around $1 billion more on employees' pay annually, as it benefits from a surge in demand for tools, paint, and building materials in the COVID-19 pandemic.</li>\n<li>Overall net sales increased 23.2% to $33.54 billion, beating analysts' estimate of $32.04 billion.</li>\n<li>Home Depot have provided staff with temporary weekly bonuses and more hours of paid time off. Some of these will now become permanent, it said.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Home Depot said on Tuesday it would spend about $1 billion more on employees' compensation annually, as the home improvement chain benefits from a sustained surge in demand for tools, paint, and building materials due to the COVID-19 pandemic.</p><p>With limited options for travel or leisure activities, Americans are spending more time at home and using their discretionary income on minor home remodeling and repair work.</p><p>\"Despite elevated activity for most of 2020, [the home improvement] trend shows no sign of weakening and, if anything, is intensifying as we come into the winter months as consumers will be forced to stay inside more,\" said Neil Saunders, managing director of GlobalData Retail.</p><p>The elevated activity has, however, also led&#160;Home&#160;Depot&#160;to spend more on its staff working through the health crisis, by providing temporary weekly bonuses and more hours of paid time off.</p><p>The company said on Tuesday it would change some of those programs to permanent forms of additional compensation for frontline hourly employees.</p><p>\"The Company is now transitioning from these temporary programs to invest in permanent compensation enhancements for frontline, hourly associates. This will result in approximately $1 billion of incremental compensation on an annualized basis,\" it said.</p><p>Home&#160;Depot's blue-chip stock, which has risen over 28% this year, fell 1.8% in premarket trading, despite the company beating quarterly sales and profit estimates.</p><p>The company, which on Monday said it would buy HD Supply Holdings Inc in a deal valued at about $8 billion, posted a 24.1% rise in same-store sales for the third quarter ended Nov. 1, beating analysts' average estimate of a 14.8% increase.</p><p>Net earnings surged 23.9% to $3.43 billion, or $3.18 per share. Analysts had expected a profit of $3.06 per share, according to IBES data from Refinitiv.</p><p>Overall net sales jumped 23.2% to $33.54 billion, beating analysts' average estimate of $32.04 billion.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/home-depot-earnings-staff-pay-sales-beat-analsyt-predictions-covid-2020-11'>Business
