Duffy,Reuters)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5ec44de23f7370099064a2dd?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn52@2020_5/2020/11/17/16-31-54-761_1ca87c788e460c43.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn83@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-54-041_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=yWebxju7leI:WnXrhVt8THI:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn20@2020_1/2020/11/17/16-31-54-459_e5670fd0bb65adcf.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=yWebxju7leI:WnXrhVt8THI:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn31@2020_2/2020/11/17/16-31-52-152_be71e10afdd731a8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn96@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-50-199_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=yWebxju7leI:WnXrhVt8THI:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn20@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-48-729_5b8d3924dcaad5f2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/yWebxju7leI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn75@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-50-015_57cdf2913a5ca1c9.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630688613},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"These are the latest cities and states to tighten lockdown restrictions as a third wave of COVID-19 hits the US","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-covid-state-rules-restrictions-california-philadelphia-washington-new-jersey-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb3b4e5bc85bb296f77f9da?format=jpeg\" alt=\"medical coronavirus flu virus nyc street face mask gloves covid19 stores shut down closed restaurants social distancing delivery cox 280\" height=\"1417\" width=\"1889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Crystal Cox/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>States and cities across the US including New Jersey, Philadelphia, and California have tightened their COVID-19 restrictions amid a third wave of the virus.</li>\n<li>Most of the restrictions focus on restricting indoor gatherings between people from multiple households.</li>\n<li>Some states and cities have issued new rules affecting gyms, schools, and restaurants.</li>\n<li>Some have also issued revised mask mandates.</li>\n<li>New states to enforce tougher rules include California, Iowa, and New Jersey, while Kansas City, Missouri and Philadelphia, Pennsylvania have announced their own restrictions.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>States and cities across the US have tightened their COVID-19 restrictions as cases continue to spiral.</p><p>The country is in the midst of a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-third-coronavirus-surge-is-tsunami-comparison-spring-summer-2020-11\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"cc7b69b4c1c0f98a30c6d1fd3261a688\">third wave of the virus</a>, and state authorities are reintroducing restrictions to curb the impact on local health services.</p><p>New states to enforce tougher rules include California, Iowa, and New Jersey. The cities of Kansas City, Missouri and Philadelphia, Pennsylvania have also announced their own restrictions.</p><p>Some states have introduced dining curfews or blanket bans on on-site dining, while others have issued mask mandates or ordered that all high school teaching must be brought online.</p><p>In the week to November 16, the US recorded 1 million new COVID-19 cases, including 170,333 on Friday alone,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/covid-19-cases-breaks-record-trump-tweets-unproven-voter-fraud-2020-11\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"cd374239fc0d2ea1a94cb9280eeafe2a\">breaking the single-day count for the fourth day in a row</a>, according to data from&#160;<a href=\"https://covidtracking.com/data/national\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"dff8659e5faa8e6fd61584c9876f9aa5\">The COVID Tracking Project.</a></p><p>This has brought total US cases to 11 million — almost 20% of all worldwide cases recorded since the first case of the virus in late 2019. It is the world's highest tally.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tCalifornia\n\t\n\t<p>California governor Gavin Newsom <a href=\"https://twitter.com/GavinNewsom/status/1328484534212411395\">announced Monday</a> that the state is \"pulling an emergency brake\" after witnessing \"alarming increases\" in COVID-19 cases.</p><p>Counties representing more than 94% of the state's population will move into California's most restrictive tier, which means that some indoor gatherings, such as for dining, are now banned.</p><p>Newsom also warned he may impose a curfew after the state recorded its fastest increase seen since the start of the pandemic.&#160;State officials told residents not to meet with people from other households.</p><p>In San Francisco, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/LondonBreed/status/1328438032760860672\">non-essential offices have to close</a>. Gyms can stay open, but are restricted to 10% capacity.</p>\n\tIowa\n\t\n\t<p>After new daily cases and hospitalizations in Iowa doubled in two weeks, its governor Kim Reynolds <a href=\"https://governor.iowa.gov/sites/default/files/documents/Public%20Health%20Proclamation%20-%202020.11.16.pdf\">introduced tighter restrictions Monday</a>, including a limited mask mandate.</p><p>From Tuesday, residents will have to wear masks when they are indoors &#8211; but this only applies to people spending 15 minutes or more within 6 feet of someone from a different household.</p><p>Reynolds also imposed a 10 p.m. curfew on restaurants and bars, and limited indoor gatherings, including weddings and funerals, to 15 people.</p><p>Gyms are allowed to stay open, but group fitness activities are banned.</p>\n\tNew Jersey\n\t\n\t<p>After New Jersey's total cases reached 280,000 Monday, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/GovMurphy/status/1328350116282060802?s=20\">Governor Phil Murphy signed an executive order</a> retightening restrictions on gatherings.</p><p>From Tuesday, indoor gatherings are limited to a maximum of 10 people. However, indoor religious and political events, weddings, and funerals can continue under rules previously issues by the state, which limit attendees to 25% of a room's capacity, up to 150 people.</p><p>On Saturday and Sunday, New Jersey recorded the <a href=\"https://twitter.com/GovMurphy/status/1328383700904669184?s=20\">first- and second-highest daily counts</a> of COVID-19 since the start of the pandemic.</p>\n\tKansas City, Missouri\n\t\n\t<p>From Friday, Kansas City is reducing restaurant capacity and banning indoor gatherings of more than 10 people.</p><p><a href=\"https://twitter.com/MayorLucasKC/status/1328442410641350657?s=20\">Announcing the restrictions on Monday</a>, Mayor Quinton Lucas said the city had reached its \"greatest crisis moment\" since the start of the pandemic.</p><p>Lucas also issued a 10 p.m. curfew for bars and restaurants and halved their capacity. Diners must wear masks at all times, except for when eating or drinking, and must remain seated.</p><p>Fitness and recreational facilities, including gyms, are also limited to half capacity and covered by a mask mandate.</p>\n\tNew Mexico\n\t\n\t<p>On Monday, <a href=\"https://cv.nmhealth.org/2020/11/13/n-m-hits-reset-re-enacting-most-heightened-level-of-statewide-public-health-restrictions/\">New Mexico reintroduced its highest level of restrictions</a> and urged people to only leave the house if essential during a two-week lockdown.</p><p>Essential businesses can operate at a limited capacity, but all other businesses and activities must close. Essential stores must follow a 10 p.m. curfew.</p><p>On-site dining is banned, although food outlets can still offer delivery or curbside collection.</p><p>\"We face a life-or-death situation and we cannot fail to act,\" <a href=\"https://twitter.com/GovMLG/status/1328368559500664835/photo/1\">said Governor Michelle Lujan Grisham</a>.</p><p>On Sunday, the state's COVID-19 hospitalizations reached a \"frightening record high\", Grisham said.</p><p>&#160;</p>\n\tNorth Dakota\n\t\n\t<p>North Dakota governor Doug Burgum's executive order that limits indoor gatherings <a href=\"https://www.governor.nd.gov/news/burgum-announces-new-requirements-businesses-gatherings-and-masks-delays-winter-activities\">came into effect Monday</a>.</p><p>Burgum issued a 10 p.m. curfew for all bars and places serving food, though they are allowed to operate take-out, curbside, and delivery services outside of these hours. In-person dining is limited to 50% capacity.</p><p>Event venues are limited to 25% capacity and sports activities have heavy restrictions.</p><p>A mask mandate also came into effect Friday. The State Health Officer order mandates residents to wear face coverings in indoor businesses and indoor public settings, as well as outdoor public settings where physical distancing isn't possible.</p><p>The state introduced the measures to ensure hospitals aren't overloaded and to keep schools and the economy open.</p>\n\tPhiladelphia, Pennsylvania\n\t\n\t<p>From Friday, high schools, museums, indoor dining, and gyms in Philadelphia must close, and indoor gatherings with people from more than one household are banned.</p><p>This includes weddings and funerals.</p><p>The city <a href=\"https://www.phila.gov/2020-11-16-philadelphia-announces-new-safer-at-home-restrictions-in-response-to-rising-covid-19-cases/\">announced the new restrictions on Friday</a>. Unlike most other state and city lockdown measures announced over the past week, which generally last a month or less, Philadelphia's will be in place until the new year.</p><p>High schools and colleges must move to online instruction only. Food outlets will no longer be able to offer indoor dining, but can still offer take-out, delivery, and outdoor dining.</p><p>Entertainment and recreational venues such as theaters, movie theaters, museums, libraries, and casinos have to shut.</p><p>Gyms and indoor exercise classes will also have to close, although exercise groups and classes will be allowed to continue outdoors.</p><p>Stores and beauty salons can stay open at limited capacity, but all visitors have to wear a mask.</p>\n\tWashington\n\t\n\t<p>Washington's four-week partial lockdown <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/washington-michigan-covid-19-lockdown-covid19-covid-rules-thanksgiving-2020-11\">started on Tuesday</a>.</p><p>Over the weekend, Washington reported more than 2,000 cases a day, and average cases in the state have doubled over the past two weeks.</p><p>\"This spike puts us in a more dangerous a position as we were in March,\" Governor Jay Inslee said during a press conference Sunday.</p><p>\"And it means, unfortunately, the time has come to reinstate restrictions on activities statewide to preserve the public's well-being, and to save lives.\"</p><p>Leisure and entertainment facilities including gyms, movie theaters, and museums have to close.</p><p>Stores can remain open, but only at 25% capacity.</p><p>From Wednesday, restaurants and bars will also no longer be able to offer dine-in services. Diners can eat outside, but only five are allowed per table.</p>\n\tMichigan\n\t\n\t<p>Michigan is entering <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/washington-michigan-covid-19-lockdown-covid19-covid-rules-thanksgiving-2020-11\">a three-week partial lockdown from Wednesday</a>.</p><p>Restaurants won't be allowed to offer indoor dining, colleges and high schools must shift to online learning, and movie theaters and casinos have to shut.</p><p>Gyms and swimming pools will remain open for individual exercise at 25% capacity, but group exercise classes will be banned.</p><p>However, meeting outside as a group of up to 25, dining outdoors, and visiting parks will still be allowed.</p><p>Colleges and high schools must end all in-person teaching, but elementary and middle schools can remain open.</p><p>On November 10, the state recorded 57 COVID-19 deaths &#8211; the highest daily total since early May.</p><p>\"If we don't act now, thousands more will die, and our hospitals will continue to be overwhelmed,\" Governor Gretchen Whitmer said.</p>\n</div><div class=\"read-original\">Read the Dean)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fb3b4e5bc85bb296f77f9da?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn21@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-29-463_deace8dbc223c91a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn83@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-54-041_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=uvALH3A5-NQ:_ytP0XGnDD0:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn4@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-47-615_68e0fe2bd06a345b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=uvALH3A5-NQ:_ytP0XGnDD0:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn3@2020_2/2020/11/17/16-31-55-254_6262bedcfa43602f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn96@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-50-199_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=uvALH3A5-NQ:_ytP0XGnDD0:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn83@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-49-956_305f1575a19200ed.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/uvALH3A5-NQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn19@2020_2/2020/11/17/16-31-53-635_7ae5d44d0c8964c8.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630688614},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"Cybercrimes can cost companies money, customers, and employees. Here's what types of cybersecurity protocols every business needs to keep their data and information safe.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-cybersecurity-protocols-companies-need-keep-data-information-safe-2020-11","description":"<div class=\"content-header\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa5b68e1df1d5001821963d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Risk and Resilience banner\" height=\"314\" width=\"2501\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></div><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fae9f671e8d500019813580?format=jpeg\" alt=\"fingerprint online cybersecurity\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1777\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Cybercrimes are up during the pandemic — it&#39;s worth making sure your business is protected.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Trutschel/Photothek via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Cybercrime reports have jumped from about 1,000 per day pre-pandemic to almost 4,000 per day, according to the FBI.</li>\n<li>With more employees working from home, companies are more vulnerable than ever to cyberattacks, which can be costly for businesses.&#160;</li>\n<li>Companies should invest in cybersecurity tech to protect remote workers, including tools to control access, encrypt and protect data, detect attacks, and backup and recover data from cybercrimes.</li>\n<li>This article is part of a series called <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/risk-and-resilience\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"3bd7cedddd71859d5db262d88397af1c\">Risk and Resilience</a>, which focuses on identifying some of the growing risks that companies should be aware of to help them build more resilient companies in the coming year.</li>\n</ul><p>More people are <a href=\"https://news.gallup.com/poll/318173/remote-workdays-doubled-during-pandemic.aspx\">working remotely</a> these days, as businesses strive to keep their employees safe and help stop the spread of COVID-19. But with so many employees working outside the office, organizations may be opening the door to a different kind of threat: a cyberattack.</p><p>The FBI's Internet Crime Complaint Center (IC3) has seen an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fbi-official-number-of-coronavirus-cyber-complaints-on-rise-2020-4\">uptick in cybercrime reports</a> during the coronavirus crisis, with <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/top-cyber-security-experts-report-4-000-cyber-attacks-a-day-since-covid-19-pandemic-1029493070\">3,000 to 4,000 a day</a> compared to 1,000 a day before the pandemic. As of May 28, IC3 had received <a href=\"https://www.fbi.gov/news/testimony/covid-19-fraud-law-enforcements-response-to-those-exploiting-the-pandemic\">320,000 complaints for the year</a>, almost as many as the 400,000 or so for all of 2019.</p><p>Cybercriminals tend to take advantage of crises, like COVID-19, and the shift to remote work has made businesses more vulnerable. When employees are working from home, they're likely using their home internet and not protected by a company's on-premise firewall, creating ripe conditions for a cyberattack, said <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/domatthews\">Doug Matthews</a>, vice president of data protection and compliance at <a href=\"https://www.veritas.com/\">Veritas Technologies</a>, a data management company.</p><p>Many companies simply aren't prepared and lack a cybersecurity configuration capable of fully protecting their data while employees aren't in the office, he added. That's why there's been an \"<a href=\"https://www.interpol.int/en/News-and-Events/News/2020/INTERPOL-report-shows-alarming-rate-of-cyberattacks-during-COVID-19#:~:text=INTERPOL%20report%20shows%20alarming%20rate%20of%20cyberattacks%20during%20COVID%2D19,-4%20August%202020&text=An%20INTERPOL%20assessment%20of%20the,corporations%2C%20governments%20and%20critical%20infrastructure.ure.\">alarming rate</a>\" of cyberattacks during COVID-19, according to an Interpol report from August, with the most common cyberthreats being online scams and phishing, ransomware, data harvesting malware, malicious domains, and misinformation scams.</p><h2>Investing in cybersecurity tech is good for business</h2><p>Too many organizations mistakenly believe they're not a target, and that puts them at risk, said <a href=\"https://globalmedia.umgc.edu/richard-white-ph-d/\">Richard White</a>, an adjunct professor of cybersecurity information assurance at the <a href=\"https://globalmedia.umgc.edu/\">University of Maryland Global Campus</a>, \"There's no reason why any responsible business owner, regardless of size, should say, 'Cybersecurity doesn't matter to me,'\" White said.</p><p>Cyberattacks cost businesses in more ways than one. In 2019, victims lost more than $3.5 billion due to reported cybercrimes, according to the <a href=\"https://www.fbi.gov/news/stories/2019-internet-crime-report-released-021120\">FBI</a>. Business email compromise alone led to $1.7 billion in losses.</p><p>Businesses could lose customers, too, said <a href=\"https://www.dickinson-wright.com/our-people/sara-h-jodka?tab=0\">Sara Jodka</a>, an employment and cybersecurity attorney at law firm <a href=\"https://www.dickinson-wright.com/our-people/sara-h-jodka?tab=0\">Dickinson Wright</a>, \"[Cyberattacks can] become a customer-experience and brand-reputation issue that no amount of money can usually account for, especially if it's made public,\" Jodka said.</p><p>Consumers expect companies to protect their information. According to a 2019 survey by digital payment platform <a href=\"https://www.businesswire.com/news/home/20190917005012/en/New-Global-Research-Shows-Poor-Data-Security\">PCI Pal</a>, 83% of US consumers said they would stop doing business with a company for a few months after a data security breach, and 21% would never do business with the company again.</p><p>A company's cybersecurity program could also help with hiring and employee retention, as a company's brand increasingly factors into the decisions people make about where they want to work.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Factoring in all of these costs, White said the price of cybersecurity is \"worth its weight in gold.\" The cost of cybersecurity technology varies widely, but he said investing $10,000 to $15,000, though it may seem like a lot to some businesses, will protect your most valuable assets.</p><h2>What an ideal work-from-home setup should include</h2><p>The first step in creating a cybersafe remote-work setup is to provide employees with a laptop with the correct security configuration for access control, encryption, and a perimeter firewall, White said.</p><p>Access control refers to a two-factor (or multi-factor) way to authenticate, encrypt, and grant access to employees working from home. It requires users to provide multiple pieces of information before access is granted and protects their credentials.&#160;</p><p>Encrypting all data ensures confidentiality and privacy, and a firewall protects the network, he said, \"So you can allow access remotely and control it and monitor it.\"</p><p>A VPN (virtual private network) is also needed to secure data and ensure that it's transmitted through an encrypted path. Without a VPN, White said, \"data would move through clear text across the hostile internet, and there'd be no way to control the path that the data would take.\"</p><p>Malware scanning technology should be included to protect systems from a variety of attacks, including ransomware, Matthews added. \"If you do it effectively, that's going to stop 99+% of the problem,\" Matthews said. \"But sometimes something is so new, those tools haven't detected it yet and aren't ready to detect it.\"</p><p>A detection capability is another must for identifying problems as they happen. Early detection of a cyberattack lets you remedy the situation immediately and pinpoint exactly when your data was compromised if an attack occurs, Matthews added.</p><p>Backup and recovery technologies are vital, too. Matthews suggested relying on a \"three, two, one rule\" to protect and recover lost data. \"You need three copies of every bit of data in at least two locations, one of which is completely air-gapped,\" he said.</p><h2>Everyone within an organization must embrace cybersecurity protocol</h2><p><a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2018/06/21/the-biggest-cybersecurity-risk-to-us-businesses-is-employee-negligence-study-says.html\">Employee negligence</a>, such as clicking on a suspicious link, is the biggest cybersecurity risk for businesses. So for a cybersecurity program to be successful, it must be a top-down initiative with ongoing communication from the C-suite to all employees, Jodka said.</p><p>Employees also need to know who to call and what to do if they're faced with a potential cyberattack, and if there's disciplinary action for negligence. Organizations should hold regular training on cybersecurity, including testing employees' abilities to recognize phishing attempts, White said. Training should also cover industry-specific data protection regulations, such as the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA) in the healthcare sector. Regular reminders about cybersecurity will keep it fresh on everyone's mind, too.</p><p>According to <a href=\"https://www.pwc.com/us/en/library/covid-19/workforce-pulse-survey.html\">PwC's Workforce Pulse Survey</a> from July, just 30% of employees said they received training on protecting company and personal data and information, even though about 70% of technology officers said they increased cybersecurity training because of the pandemic. And 23% of employees said their organization didn't offer a \"compelling case\" for good cybersecurity practices, and less than 30% said their employer provided a device for them to use while working remotely without having to use their own personal equipment.</p><p>Data breaches from cyberattacks could land company leaders in legal trouble, Jodka said. In January 2019, former officers and directors of <a href=\"https://casetext.com/case/in-re-yahoo-inc-sholder-derivative-litig-1\">Yahoo agreed to pay $29 million</a> to settle claims that they had mishandled customer data during several cyberattacks from 2013 to 2016 that compromised three billion user accounts.</p><p>The Yahoo case \"changed the game,\" Jodka said, showing that cybercrime could be seen as a breach of the duty of care and duty of loyalty that officers and boards of directors have to their organizations.</p><p>As the transition to remote work continues, cyberthreats will likely intensify, and investing in cybersecurity to tighten security remains a critical issue for businesses of all sizes.</p><p>\"The issue is still significant as thousands and thousands of dollars continue to go out the door in response to these phishing and other schemes,\" Jodka said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"As Trump keeps blocking Biden's transition, warnings of the damage it will do to the US are getting louder and more dire","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-refusal-to-allow-biden-transition-prompts-growing-alarm-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb3b38030303a28805b3f5c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"president trump\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President Donald Trump in Ohio in August.\n<p class=\"copyright\">JIM WATSON/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Steadily more people are warning of the dangers of President Donald Trump's refusal to allow President-elect Joe Biden's transition to proceed.</li>\n<li>Biden initially brushed off the risks of a delayed transition, but on Monday he said bluntly that \"people may die\" if it is delayed further.</li>\n<li>Republicans, once silent on the matter, have also started to warn of the damage Trump is causing.</li>\n<li>Barack and Michelle Obama, who <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/timeline-of-2016-and-2020-election-transitions-between-trump-obama-2020-11?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">gave a smooth transfer to the Trump administration</a>, have said US democracy is on the line.</li>\n<li>Some Senate Republicans <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2020/11/12/republicans-biden-should-get-presidential-briefings-436303\">have said</a>&#160;that briefings should still happen while Trump legally challenges the outcome of the election.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>President Donald Trump's refusal to let President-elect Joe Biden start his transition is prompting a growing chorus of alarm, including from Trump's own allies.</p><p>Since most news networks called the election for Biden on November 7, Trump has refused to concede and has filed <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-campaign-lawsuits-election-results-2020-11\">multiple lawsuits contesting the results</a>.</p><p>He has also refused to allow the General Services Administration to authorize a presidential transition process that releases funds, briefings, and resources.</p><p>Biden initially downplayed the significance of being denied a full transition. \"We don't see anything that's slowing us down,\" he told reporters on November 10.</p><p>While Trump's intransigence is embarrassing for the nation, Biden said, it is \"not of much consequence.\"</p><p>One week later, Biden's tone changed dramatically. \"People may die,\" he said on Monday, arguing that a smooth handover was vital to helping him battle the COVID-19 pandemic.</p><p>Biden is not the only one. What began as a chorus of mostly Democrats and government ethics experts now includes:</p><ul><li>John Kelly, a former Trump chief of staff, who <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2020/11/13/kelly-criticizes-trump-over-delay-of-biden-transition-436465\">told Politico on Friday</a> that the delay \"hurts our national security.\"</li><li><a href=\"https://uk.news.yahoo.com/more-republicans-urge-trump-allow-003441182.html\">Several Republican senators</a> who urged Trump to let Biden <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2020/11/12/republicans-biden-should-get-presidential-briefings-436303\">receive classified briefings</a>. James Lankford, a Republican senator from Oklahoma, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/republican-senator-step-in-biden-isnt-given-intelligence-briefings-friday-2020-11?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">said he would intervene</a> to help make it happen.</li><li>Four Bush- and Obama-era Department of Homeland Security chiefs who <a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/2020-election/live-blog/2020-11-11-biden-harris-transition-n1247340/ncrd1247458#blogHeader\">said that</a> \"we do not have a single day to spare to begin the transition.\"</li><li>Andy Card, once President George W. Bush's chief of staff, who <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/11/11/former-bush-chief-of-staff-cites-9/11-warns-about-slow-transition.html\">told CNBC</a> that a shaky transition from the Clinton to the Bush administration might have hurt the response to 9/11.</li><li>Dr. Anthony Fauci, the top US infectious-disease expert, who is averse to partisan politics but has pushed for a transition. \"It's like passing the baton in a race,\" <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/video/politics/officials-warn-of-harmful-consequences-as-trump-continues-to-stonewall-biden-transition/2020/11/15/537d8149-48c8-4606-b0d5-acc98f5c0e02_video.html\">he said</a>. \"You don't want to stop and then give it to somebody. You want to just essentially keep going.\"</li><li>Trump's national security advisor, Robert O'Brien, who <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/robert-obrien-trump-nsa-obviously-seems-biden-won-election-2020-11?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">appeared to break rank with others in the White House</a> and speak of \"a very professional transition\" to Biden's team — though that was predicated on \"if\" the victory was confirmed.</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/obama-sense-truth-decay-us-as-election-shows-divided-nation-2020-11\">Barack</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/michelle-obama-instagram-post-trump-refusing-to-concede-racist-lies2020-11\">Michelle Obama</a>, who have only occasionally spoken out against Trump but called for him to concede and urged him to \"think beyond your own ego.\"</li></ul><p>As time passes, the warnings are likely to become more urgent still.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original 2020 13:09:44 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5fb3b6b8fb298327691e77a4?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"99d960488d39061b5a0944a5918a90f6","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn8@2020_2/2020/11/17/16-31-44-417_9b46129d79d222b0.webp","destWidth":1778,"destHeight":1334,"sourceBytes":181170,"destBytes":181170,"author":"mjankowicz@businessinsider.com (Mia Jankowicz)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fb3b38030303a28805b3f5c?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn28@2020_1/2020/11/17/16-31-47-986_8591af329b6ed1ea.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn83@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-54-041_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=HkKYLpRWGBI:WoXFgYpzXT4:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn56@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-54-767_8fcf605728a12d4c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=HkKYLpRWGBI:WoXFgYpzXT4:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn3@2020_1/2020/11/17/16-31-50-092_0dd5bd4993f8c1e4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn96@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-50-199_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=HkKYLpRWGBI:WoXFgYpzXT4:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn67@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-54-840_d0283dcd2929d84e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/HkKYLpRWGBI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn56@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-51-362_903433dd55bb2ee0.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630688611},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"A divided government means Biden won't be able to do much, except in one area where most Americans want change","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/even-with-divided-government-biden-can-make-foreign-policy-changes-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb30845402d49001924f48b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Joe Biden\" height=\"600\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President-elect Joe Biden.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The most likely conclusion to the 2020 election is a government divided between Democrats holding the House of Representatives and White House and Republicans with a slim majority in the Senate.</li>\n<li>A divided government usually means gridlock on most issues, but President-elect Joe Biden will have the power to pursue a foreign policy of restraint that many Americans have shown they support, writes Defense Priorities fellow Bonnie Kristian.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Recounts and court battles and Senate&#160;<a href=\"https://www.cbsnews.com/news/georgia-senate-runoff-elections-perdue-ossoff-leoffler-warnock-january/\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.cbsnews.com/news/georgia-senate-runoff-elections-perdue-ossoff-leoffler-warnock-january/&source=gmail&ust=1605647727857000&usg=AFQjCNGqhE0hSo3609_G_-cBDvWpke_rrgcBDvWpke_rrg\">runoff races</a> are yet to come, but the likeliest final conclusion of the 2020 election is a President Joe Biden entering office and serving with a narrowly Republican Senate, a Democratic House, and a conservative-majority Supreme Court. We're probably back to divided government, at least for two years.</p><p>A partisan split like this typically means gridlock on the Hill and a steady stream of executive orders from the White House. For foreign policy, it should mean reform, restraint, and a pivot to peace.</p><p>American voters have been seeking peace with our presidential picks for years, after all. George W. Bush was elected <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=F9SOVzMV2bc\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v%3DF9SOVzMV2bc&source=gmail&ust=1605647727857000&usg=AFQjCNFIjJLhQf4gPxtnLbo96DunUk5IwQo96DunUk5IwQ\">promising</a> to make the United States \"humble\" abroad, to reject nation building and decline to interfere in other nations' affairs. Instead he invaded Afghanistan and Iraq, launched nation-building projects in both, and introduced drone warfare.</p><p>Barack Obama <a href=\"https://edition.cnn.com/2017/01/09/opinions/obamas-foreign-policy-reckless-kristian-opinion/index.html\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://edition.cnn.com/2017/01/09/opinions/obamas-foreign-policy-reckless-kristian-opinion/index.html&source=gmail&ust=1605647727857000&usg=AFQjCNEPUxtkh76SC7SxJ3WPeB9kLdll7QWPeB9kLdll7Q\">ran on a</a> repudiation of the Iraq War and the Bush administration's interventionism more broadly. He left office the <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2016/05/15/us/politics/obama-as-wartime-president-has-wrestled-with-protecting-nation-and-troops.html\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/05/15/us/politics/obama-as-wartime-president-has-wrestled-with-protecting-nation-and-troops.html&source=gmail&ust=1605647727857000&usg=AFQjCNFq9BZs466NuozdBzPohpY9QUq5CwPohpY9QUq5Cw\">only president</a> in American history to complete two terms entirely at war, expanding American military intervention into Syria, Libya, and Yemen while maintaining it in Afghanistan, Iraq, Pakistan, and Somalia.</p><p>Donald Trump campaigned in 2016 and 2020 alike by castigating these two predecessors for the foreign policy legacy they left him. <a href=\"https://www.realclearpolitics.com/video/2020/09/16/trump_iraq_war_was_the_worst_mistake_the_mostly_costly_mistake_in_the_history_of_our_country.html\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.realclearpolitics.com/video/2020/09/16/trump_iraq_war_was_the_worst_mistake_the_mostly_costly_mistake_in_the_history_of_our_country.html&source=gmail&ust=1605647727857000&usg=AFQjCNEw_L6hGBV3YDHcooBS2JXZYDgwIwBS2JXZYDgwIw\">He called</a> \"going into the Middle East\" the \"worst\" and \"most costly mistake in the history of our country,\" promising again and again <a href=\"https://nationalinterest.org/blog/skeptics/donald-trumps-erratic-foreign-policy-failure-121886\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://nationalinterest.org/blog/skeptics/donald-trumps-erratic-foreign-policy-failure-121886&source=gmail&ust=1605647727857000&usg=AFQjCNEjGkpRegPj2PmCt-WkbAvH7I_XEAWkbAvH7I_XEA\">to end</a> \"endless wars,\" especially the war <a href=\"https://www.theamericanconservative.com/articles/reality-check-same-number-of-troops-at-beginning-and-end-of-trump-term/\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.theamericanconservative.com/articles/reality-check-same-number-of-troops-at-beginning-and-end-of-trump-term/&source=gmail&ust=1605647727857000&usg=AFQjCNGZDAcH0MAPNc2-x6EqQ0szPkJp1wEqQ0szPkJp1w\">in Afghanistan</a>.</p><p>Now he appears due to shortly leave office without concluding a single conflict, even <a href=\"https://inkstickmedia.com/the-next-president-should-get-us-out-of-yemen/\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://inkstickmedia.com/the-next-president-should-get-us-out-of-yemen/&source=gmail&ust=1605647727857000&usg=AFQjCNFGrxoE9rbqmW1h6rVZoBEStl_2jQVZoBEStl_2jQ\">having vetoed</a> multiple bipartisan congressional attempts to extricate the United States from exacerbating Yemen's civil war and humanitarian crisis.</p><p>And so we come to Biden, preparing to take office after <a href=\"https://www.cbsnews.com/news/transcript-joe-biden-on-face-the-nation-february-23-2020/\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.cbsnews.com/news/transcript-joe-biden-on-face-the-nation-february-23-2020/&source=gmail&ust=1605647727857000&usg=AFQjCNHoMhQNKw-y797gJkd0zCBAuMW-owd0zCBAuMW-ow\">likewise pledging</a> to bring two decades of aimless, counterproductive, costly war and nation building to a close. While divided government may stymie many other portions of his agenda, it need pose no obstacle here. That's so in two ways.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5efba4a3aee6a82e530e5869?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Trump\" height=\"1334\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President Donald Trump with US troops during an unannounced visit to Bagram Air Base in Afghanistan, November 28, 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tom Brenner/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>First, the Constitution <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/agenda/story/2017/04/trumps-dangerous-expansion-of-executive-war-powers-000387/\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.politico.com/agenda/story/2017/04/trumps-dangerous-expansion-of-executive-war-powers-000387/&source=gmail&ust=1605647727857000&usg=AFQjCNGarlHYImq2QcbyRaUvoWbU_kOk_wUvoWbU_kOk_w\">gives Congress</a> the power to declare war, but once a military intervention is already underway, the president's authority as commander-in-chief means he can end it at will. Biden does not need a cooperative Senate to fulfill his <a href=\"https://joebiden.com/americanleadership/\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://joebiden.com/americanleadership/&source=gmail&ust=1605647727857000&usg=AFQjCNFZpyxXizlkHymLSI9lmmc966Pf3g9lmmc966Pf3g\">promise to</a> \"end the forever wars in Afghanistan and the Middle East,\" including \"end[ing] our support for the Saudi-led war in Yemen.\" Divided government is no impediment to Biden making good here.</p><p>Also very much under presidential purview, even with divided government, is Biden's pledge to \"elevate diplomacy as the premier tool of our global engagement.\" Though he'll need congressional help if he wants to increase the State Department budget or confirm new ambassadors, Biden can nominate diplomatic candidates more reliably <a href=\"https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2018/11/state-department-empty-ambassador-to-australi/574831/\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2018/11/state-department-empty-ambassador-to-australi/574831/&source=gmail&ust=1605647727857000&usg=AFQjCNF8pfcuXs8OZK586I3Vt4Zt7WZDcA3Vt4Zt7WZDcA\">than Trump has</a> and fill lower-level roles without Senate consent.</p><p>But the likely GOP-held Senate will be involved in some of Biden's staffing process, which is the second way divided government could move us toward restraint.</p><p>Sen. Mitch McConnell (Kentucky), widely expected to continue as the leader of a Republican majority, is reportedly planning to \"push Biden to go with more centrist options,\" <a href=\"https://www.axios.com/gop-senate-biden-transition-50ebe6c8-e318-4fdb-b903-048908b3b954.html\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.axios.com/gop-senate-biden-transition-50ebe6c8-e318-4fdb-b903-048908b3b954.html&source=gmail&ust=1605647727857000&usg=AFQjCNHPzTlfZ6FETdPTlTqtXXK_iMeRKgqtXXK_iMeRKg\">per Axios</a>, expressing willingness to \"work with Biden on centrist nominees but no 'radical progressives' or ones who are controversial with conservatives.\"</p><p>This may have its most significant effects on domestic policy — keeping Biden from nominating, say, a Treasury Secretary Elizabeth Warren — and what someone in Washington defines as \"centrist\" does not necessarily mean restraint in American foreign policy.</p><p>In fact, as the above review of our last three administrations demonstrates, both party establishments tend toward an interventionist foreign policy of invasion, nation building, and diplomacy downplayed—and Biden and McConnell are about as establishment as they come.</p><p>But that review equally shows that most Americans, most of the time, want a more prudent approach to matters of war and peace. We have voted for an end to arrogant, hawkish interventionism so many times now. By this measure, restraint is centrism. Americans generally do not want to posture the United States as a meddlesome superpower, constantly and recklessly inserting our military into situations unconnected to vital US security interests.</p><p>For the next two years, a government split between both major parties could well mean more of the failures that have defined US foreign affairs the post-9/11 era. But foreign policy should be one point on which a divided government can be united, finally giving voters the peace they keep endorsing.</p><p><em>Bonnie Kristian is a fellow at Defense Priorities, contributing editor at The Week, and columnist at Christianity Today. Her writing has also appeared at CNN, NBC, USA Today, the Los Angeles Times, and Defense One, among other outlets.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a you this week, Amazon has officially unveiled <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-starts-selling-prescription-medication-in-us-2020-11\">its long-awaited Amazon Pharmacy service, selling prescription medications and offering discount services for Prime members</a>.&#160;</p><p>Much like Amazon's original foray into the pharmacy space through its acquisition of PillPack, the news of Amazon Pharmacy's official launch has <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/cvs-walgreens-riteaid-stock-price-reaction-amazon-digital-pharmacy-launch-2020-11-1029811333\">sent story here.&#160;</a></strong></p><p>Also today in healthcare news: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fdas-peter-marks-on-the-coronavirus-vaccine-review-process-2020-11\">The man in charge of vaccine</a>.&#160;</p><hr><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3fcfc042f43f001ddfe41b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Peter Marks\" height=\"683\" width=\"910\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Peter href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fdas-peter-marks-on-the-coronavirus-vaccine-review-process-2020-11\" data-analytics-position=\"1\" data-analytics-module=\"\">The man in charge of evaluating coronavirus vaccines for the FDA lays out why it will take weeks to vet a COVID-19 shot</a></h3><ul><li>As coronavirus vaccines inch closer to reality, the man in charge of reviewing the approval applications wants Americans to trust the process.</li><li>That means we're not going to get surprise Food and Drug Administration approvals in the coming days, despite two COVID-19 vaccine frontrunners announcing success over the past week.</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fdas-peter-marks-on-the-coronavirus-vaccine-review-process-2020-11\">The review process will be measured in weeks, Dr. Peter Marks, director of the FDA's center for biological products, told Business Insider on Friday.</a></li></ul><p><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fdas-peter-marks-on-the-coronavirus-vaccine-review-process-2020-11\">Read the full story from Andrew Dunn here&#62;&#62;</a></strong></p><hr><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-pharmacies-hospitals-could-profit-from-covid-19-vaccine-2020-11\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2788a1c741f0019ac9ec1?format=jpeg\" Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-pharmacies-hospitals-could-profit-from-covid-19-vaccine-2020-11\">Pharmacies, doctor's offices and hospitals are gearing up to give coronavirus vaccines to millions of Americans. Here's how they're preparing and how much they stand to profit along the way.</a></h3><ul><li>Drug companies Pfizer and Moderna in November announced that their coronavirus vaccines are highly effective at preventing COVID-19, an encouraging sign in the fight to end the pandemic.</li><li>Pharmacies, hospitals and clinics are preparing to play a role in getting the COVID-19 vaccines into the arms of millions of patients, when a vaccine becomes available.</li><li>Administering the COVID-19 vaccine could be an $8.5 billion market, according to Morgan Stanley analysts.</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-pharmacies-hospitals-could-profit-from-covid-19-vaccine-2020-11\">Analysts suggest that chain pharmacies could profit the most among providers from administering the vaccine, while hospitals and medical clinics may not make as much revenue.</a></li></ul><p><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-pharmacies-hospitals-could-profit-from-covid-19-vaccine-2020-11\">Read the full story from Shelby Livingston here&#62;&#62;</a></strong></p><hr><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-vaccine-trial-was-part-of-trump-operation-warp-speed-2020-11\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb28ce81c741f0019ac9eef?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Moderna vaccine\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>University of Miami Miller School of Medicine lab tech Sendy Puerto processes blood samples from study participants in the specimen processing lab￼, Wednesday, Sept. 2, 2020 in Miami. potential","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-macbook-air-m1-review","description":"<p class=\"financial-disclaimer\"><i>When you buy through our links, we may earn money from our affiliate partners. <a href=\"https://www.insider-inc.com/commerce-on-insider-inc/\">Learn more.</a></i></p><p><a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&xs=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-mac%2Fmacbook-airbook-air\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2f11f402d49001924f434?format=jpeg\" alt=\"MacBook Air red open\" height=\"750\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lisa Eadicicco/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li>Apple's M1-powered <a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&xs=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-mac%2Fmacbook-airbook-air\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">MacBook Air</a> brings benefits like speedier performance and longer battery life to the company's flagship lightweight laptop.</li><li>The M1 is Apple's first processor for the Mac, and the new MacBook Air is one of the first devices to run on it.</li><li>In addition to faster performance and longer battery life, the addition of Apple's chip also means that iPhone and iPad apps can run on the Mac for the first time.</li><li>But, without a touch screen, it may be hard to experience the benefits of using mobile apps on the desktop.&#160;</li><li>The MacBook Air also lacks modern Apple features, like Face ID and a nearly borderless screen.</li><li>Here's what the newest MacBook Air is up against in our guide for the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-laptop\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">best laptops</a>.</li></ul><div id=\"ProductCard_5fab087019bb5e51403e5023\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe src=\"https://produktor.businessinsider.com/productCardService?id=5fab087019bb5e51403e5023&type=small&live=true\" width=\"100%\" height=\"150%\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\" style=\"position:absolute; top:0; left: 0\"></iframe></div><p>&#160;</p><p>It's no secret that laptops have started to more closely resemble tablets and smartphones in recent years. Tech giants like Apple, Microsoft, and many others have been chasing what has become the Holy Grail of computing: blending the benefits of mobile devices with the processing power that comes with desktop-class machines.</p><p>Apple's ambitions here are coming into full focus with <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-m1-chip-risk-moving-away-from-intel-macbook-pro-2020-11\">the debut of the M1</a>: its first homemade processor designed to power its line of Mac computers.</p><p>The launch of its M1 chip means a few promising things for Apple loyalists. For one, the processors powering Apple's laptops and desktops will run on the same basic architecture as those inside the iPhone and iPad, enabling mobile apps from the iOS App Store to run on the Mac for the first time.</p><p>But, most important of all, Apple is guaranteeing that its M1 chip will introduce major gains in performance and power efficiency. That's already become evident after using the new $1,000 M1-powered <a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&xs=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-mac%2Fmacbook-airbook-air\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">MacBook Air</a> for just a few days, which is leagues ahead of Apple's Intel-powered MacBook Air when it comes to areas like performance and webcam quality.</p><p>Plus, the MacBook Air's newer fanless internal design means you'll no longer need to worry about your laptop sounding like a jet engine when it's enduring a particularly heavy workload.</p><p>Yet, it's going to take some time before we understand whether making iPhone apps compatible with the Mac brings anything new to the experience. And, even though Apple's M1 chip delivers noticeable improvements in power and efficiency, Apple's laptops still lack some of the benefits of Windows devices, like facial recognition for a more seamless login experience, borderless screens, and most importantly: touch support.</p><p>But overall, the M1-powered MacBook Air is a step up from its Intel-powered predecessor. It offers faster performance for the same price with virtually no compromises even when running apps that are not yet optimized for Apple's new silicon.</p><bi-shortcode id=\"table-of-contents-sticky\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-type=\"h2\">Table of Contents: Masthead Sticky</bi-shortcode><h2>Apple MacBook Air (Late 2020, M1) specifications</h2><ul><li><strong>Display:</strong> 13.3-inch Retina display (2,560 x 1,600) with True Tone</li><li><strong>Processor:</strong> 8-core Apple M1 SoC (7~8-core GPU, 16-core Neural Engine)</li><li><strong>Estimated battery life:</strong> Up to 15 hours of web browsing</li><li><strong>Memory:</strong> 8GB to 16GB&#160;</li><li><strong>Storage:</strong> 256GB or 512GB SSD configurable up to 2TB</li><li><strong>Ports:</strong> Two Thunderbolt 3/USB-C ports, one headphone jack</li><li><strong>Camera:</strong> 720p FaceTime camera</li><li><strong>Authentication:</strong> Touch ID fingerprint sensor</li></ul><h2>Performance</h2><p><a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&xs=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-mac%2Fmacbook-airbook-air\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2f1461c741f0019aca215?format=jpeg\" alt=\"MacBook AIr Yellow\" height=\"750\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lisa Eadicicco/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>Let's start with performance, since it's one of the biggest ways in which Apple's new MacBook Air stands out from its Intel-powered predecessor.</p><p>The Apple silicon MacBook Air I've been using has eight processor cores and 8GB of RAM, while the Intel-powered version I've been testing it against has a 1.1GHz quad-core Intel core i5 processor with 8GB of RAM.</p><p>The Intel edition replaced by this model topped out at four cores, and the base model came with a dual-core Intel Core i3, which as I noted in <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-macbook-air-2020-review\">my previous review</a> felt underpowered. A processor with more cores usually means it's better at multitasking, since it has additional cores to drive multiple processes at once.</p><p>Apple claims the M1-equipped MacBook Air model offers 3.5 times the computing power, five times the graphics performance, and up to nine times the machine learning capabilities compared to the previous-generation Intel version. In other words: it should be faster when it comes to everything from gaming to editing high-resolution photos and more.&#160;</p><p>In my experience, the performance gains are most noticeable in photo editing apps and video games. When exporting 50 photos from Adobe Lightroom in full size at 100% quality, the M1-powered MacBook Air performed the task in 16.5 seconds, while the Intel version took 46.3 seconds. It was also faster at stitching together five images to create a panoramic shot: the M1 MacBook Air did so in 11.2 seconds, while the Intel edition took 19.3 seconds.</p><p>Exporting a complex image that was 1GB in size and 15,000 x 12,000 pixels — the biggest file in my Lightroom library by a long shot — only took about 30 seconds on the first try when using the M1 MacBook Air and 17 seconds on the second test. The Intel MacBook Air, by comparison, took over three minutes to export the same image file both times.</p><p>The MacBook Air isn't meant to be a gaming laptop, but the M1 version is certainly more capable than its Intel-powered counterpart. Don't expect to play games at the highest resolution on the M1 MacBook Air, but I was able to comfortably play \"Shadow of the Tomb Raider\" at a resolution of 1,900 x 1,200 without much compromise.</p><p>The Intel-equipped MacBook Air can also run the game at that same resolution, but performance is a bit stuttery in comparison, especially when panning the camera across busy scenes. The M1 MacBook Air also loaded my save slot about 13 seconds faster than the Intel version when starting the game.</p><p>Not to mention, \"Shadow of the Tomb Raider\" sent the Intel-based MacBook Air's fans whirring after less than an hour of gameplay, an issue I didn't have to worry about with the fanless M1 MacBook Air.</p><h2>Apps</h2><p><a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&xs=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-mac%2Fmacbook-airbook-air\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2f1661c741f0019aca217?format=jpeg\" alt=\"MacBook Air Apps 2\" height=\"669\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Kitchen Stories app (left) alongside the website (right)\n<p class=\"copyright\">Business Insider/Lisa Eadicicco</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>Apple's decision to put its own silicon in devices like the MacBook Air combined with its most recent desktop software makes the Mac feel a bit more like the iPhone.</p><p>Big Sur, the name of Apple's most recent macOS update, introduces redesigned app icons that more closely resemble those found on the iPhone, for example, in addition to other iPhone-like features. And, the keyboard on the M1 MacBook Air features new shortcuts in the function row for features like Do Not Disturb and dictation.</p><p>But, the most significant way Apple is bridging the Mac and iPhone experience is through apps. Since the Mac's processor is now based on the same basic architecture as that of the iPhone and iPad, iOS apps are capable of running on the Mac natively. Some of the iOS apps currently available on macOS ahead of launch include games like \"Among Us\" and \"Crossy Road\" as well as Facebook, Zillow, and Kitchen Stories.</p><p>These apps run just fine on the Mac. But, it'll probably take some time for developers to make changes that elevate their apps beyond what you'd experience when using the web-based version of the app.</p><p>That's especially true considering Mac laptops don't support touch input like many Windows devices do. Apple has always maintained that its desktop and mobile ecosystems should remain separate. But, I've never wanted a touch screen on the Mac more than I have in recent years after using the iPad Pro.</p><p>Apple's top-of-the-line tablet is the best argument yet for how good a touch-centric productivity device made by Apple could be. The MacBook Air offers some of the features I loved about working on the iPad Pro — namely its fanless design, long battery life, and fast performance — but feels a bit incomplete without a touch screen. That also makes it tougher to be excited about the prospect of iPhone apps on the Mac.</p><p>Still, there are ways for mobile apps to shine on the Mac. The Kitchen Stories app is a bit sleeker than the website and dives right into the featured recipes with compelling visuals as soon as you launch the app. The website, on the other hand, prominently features articles and blog posts in addition to recipes, which is great if you're looking for stories to read but perhaps is less ideal while you're in the middle of preparing a meal.</p><p>However, most people don't buy a laptop specifically to use mobile apps. Since the M1 chip is based on a different architecture than Intel's processors, desktop programs need to be optimized for Apple's new computers. Apple is addressing this by enabling Intel-based apps to run in its Rosetta 2 emulator, which essentially means apps should be able to run normally on M1 Macs regardless of whether they've been tweaked for Apple's new chip.</p><p>During my time using the M1 MacBook Air, I could barely tell the difference between apps that were optimized for Apple's chip and those that weren't. All of the third-party apps I've been using on the new MacBook Air — Slack, Google Chrome, Microsoft Word, Cisco WebEx, Adobe Lightroom, and Skitch — have not yet been updated to be optimized for Apple silicon.</p><p>But, they ran so flawlessly on the MacBook Air that the only way I could tell they weren't optimized for the M1 chip was by looking at the Mac's Activity Monitor.</p><h2>Battery life and webcam</h2><p><a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&xs=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-mac%2Fmacbook-airbook-air\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2fdca1c741f0019aca25c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Apple MacBook Air half open\" height=\"750\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lisa Eadicicco/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>While the improvements in performance are certainly appreciated, it's the upgrade to the MacBook Air's battery life that I appreciated the most.</p><p>The MacBook Air had 10% of its battery left after 12 hours of usage that involved a mix of photo editing in Lightroom, browsing the web in both Safari and Chrome, streaming video on YouTube, and a little bit of gaming. Apple claims the new Air should last for 15 hours when browsing the web and 18 hours when playing video in Apple TV Plus.</p><p>Those results may not align precisely with Apple's claims, especially since my usage circumstances differed from Apple's tests. But, it certainly outperformed the Intel-based MacBook Air, which lasted for roughly seven hours on a single charge when I <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-macbook-air-2020-review\">reviewed it earlier this year</a>.</p><p>It's important to remember that factors like screen brightness and the specific apps you're running will always impact battery life, so your results may differ from mine.</p><p>The M1-powered MacBook Air is also getting another desperately-needed upgrade: its webcam. Apple isn't alone; built-in webcams on most laptops are nowhere near the quality of those found on our smartphones. Until 2020, that probably didn't matter much. But, now that many people have been relying on webcams for office meetings, socializing, and most likely holiday gatherings in the near future, the cameras in our laptops have taken on a new importance.</p><p>The M1 MacBook Air still has a 720p camera, but because it runs on Apple's processor it also has the company's iPhone-grade image signal processor technology. That means it should offer better noise reduction and white balance, and in my experience it lived up to these claims.</p><p>Take a look at the difference below.</p><p><strong>M1 MacBook Air</strong></p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2fa071c741f0019aca23d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"FaceTime Camera M1 Mac\" height=\"720\" width=\"1080\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lisa Eadicicco/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>Intel MacBook Air</strong></p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2fa1a1c741f0019aca23e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"FaceTime Camera Intel Mac\" height=\"720\" width=\"1080\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lisa Eadicicco/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>It's still not as crisp as your smartphone's camera, but it's a major leap ahead of Apple's Intel-based Mac.</p><h2>Design, display, and keyboard</h2><p><a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&xs=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-mac%2Fmacbook-airbook-air\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2f1f61c741f0019aca21c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"MacBook Air Open\" height=\"750\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Business Insider/Lisa Eadicicco</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>In other critical areas, like the design, display, and keyboard, the MacBook Air hasn't changed much compared to the previous Intel-powered iteration. One difference, however, is that Apple has added support for wide color into the display rather than just standard color.</p><p>That means the screen should be able to display a broader spectrum of colors compared to the earlier version of the MacBook Air, although I didn't notice this too much in daily use. It's probably more important for photo and video editors that need precise color representation in a laptop.</p><p>Unfortunately, Apple's new M1-powered laptops haven't gotten the same makeover that other products like the iPad and iPhone have received in recent years. As such, they still have thicker borders framing their display, occupying space that could have been used to expand the screen without making the laptop itself more cumbersome. It makes the design feel a bit dated compared to Windows laptops, like the Dell XPS 13.</p><p>Apple also hasn't built Face ID into the Mac yet, despite the fact that dozens of Windows laptops support Microsoft's Windows Hello feature. The new MacBook Air does have Touch ID, as does its predecessor, but facial recognition would have provided a slightly more seamless experience. And if the MacBook Air's internals are similar to those of the Intel MacBook Air from earlier this year, <a href=\"https://www.ifixit.com/News/36480/theres-something-new-in-the-macbook-air\">the RAM and SSD are probably soldered</a>, meaning they'll be tough to upgrade after the fact.&#160;</p><p>Like the other laptops Apple has released this year, the M1-powered MacBook Air has the company's new Magic Keyboard. If you've used any of the earlier laptops Apple released between 2015 and 2019, you'll definitely notice the difference.</p><p>The Magic Keyboard is less flat and offers more feedback when typing, resulting in an experience that's generally more comfortable than its previous butterfly keyboard. Those older keyboards were also more prone to damage and malfunctions than the Magic Keyboard.</p><h2>The bottom line</h2><p><a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&xs=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-mac%2Fmacbook-airbook-air\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2f23f402d49001924f441?format=jpeg\" alt=\"MacBook Air marble background\" height=\"659\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Business Insider/Lisa Eadicicco</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>With its longer battery life and faster performance for the same price, it's clear that Apple's new M1 chip delivers big improvements. Popular apps like Microsoft Word and Slack that haven't yet been optimized for the chip still work flawlessly on the system, meaning the laptop's viability doesn't hinge on whether or not developers update their apps.</p><p>The addition of the M1 chip is a particularly useful upgrade for a laptop like the MacBook Air, which primarily appeals to students and professionals in need of a laptop for basic work that primarily involves web browsing and word processing. The fact that it can hold its own when it comes to gaming and photo editing make it that much better.</p><p>But, Apple's approach of shying away from touch screens and flexible 2-in-1 designs make me wonder how much better the experience could be if the company were to embrace those choices, especially now that iPhone apps can run on the Mac.</p><p>The new MacBook Air is certainly a step forward, but it also would have been nice to see some of the enhancements that have arrived on the iPad and iPhone translate to the Mac — like a bigger screen and Face ID.</p><p>All told, the M1 MacBook Air is Apple's first major attempt to bring the perks of mobile devices — like all-day battery life, fanless designs, and a wider selection of apps — to its desktop operating system. The full benefits of having the iPhone and Mac run on the same architecture may not be fully realized just yet, but so far the M1 is a success in the areas that matter most like performance and battery life.</p><p><strong>Pros:</strong> Fast performance; Super-long battery life; Much improved camera <br><strong>Cons</strong>: Lacks some features of similarly-priced Windows devices like facial recognition and a borderless screen; iPhone apps don't add much to the experience yet especially without touch screens</p><div id=\"ProductCard_5fab087019bb5e51403e5023\" 1-50-199_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=qjvyMnXNDsk:4Wo6AAkCV2M:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn23@2020_5/2020/11/17/16-31-51-909_52371e4c497000a2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/qjvyMnXNDsk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn92@2020_1/2020/11/17/16-31-54-277_f16fdb049a7883ae.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630688559},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"Lurpak producers correct UK government on Brexit and warn that a no-deal exit will mean higher prices","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/brexit-arla-lurpak-boss-warns-no-deal-higher-food-prices-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb3d8a41b1c03280d6990fe?format=jpeg\" alt=\"George Eustice\" height=\"750\" width=\"1500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Secretary of State for Environment, Food and Rural Affairs George Eustice.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Wiktor Szymanowicz/Barcroft Media via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Arla's UK boss warns that leaving the EU without a trade deal would lead to price rises in British shops.</li>\n<li>The dairy company was in the headlines on Sunday when UK Environment Secretary George Eustice said it would have to move production of Lurpak butter from Denmark to Britain to avoid tariffs in a no-deal scenario.</li>\n<li>However, Arla cannot do so because it would be illegal, its UK Managing Director Ash Amirahmadi said.</li>\n<li>Amirahmadi warned that tariffs on dairy imports would trigger price rises in the UK: \"I would be very surprised if our customers didn't have to absorb the cost.\"</li>\n<li>He said that the UK dairy sector was potentially heading for a winter \"triple whammy\" of leaving the EU without a trade deal coinciding with the second wave of the coronavirus and the demands of Christmas.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The UK boss of one of Europe's biggest dairy companies has corrected the UK government after it suggested that the company could simply move part of its production from the EU to Britain in the event of a no-deal Brexit, telling Business Insider that it would have to increase prices for UK consumers instead.</p><p>The UK Environment Secretary George Eustice told the BBC on Sunday that Arla, which makes the popular Lurpak brand of butter in Europe, could make the product in the UK instead to avoid costly tariffs if Britain fails to secure a trade deal with the EU by the end of the year.</p><p><a href=\"https://twitter.com/BBCPolitics/status/1327915454464204804?s=20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Eustice told BBC's Andrew Marr:</a> \"In a non-negotiated outcome, what would happen is companies like Arla, which is a big Danish company, sells brands like Lurpak in the UK that are manufactured in Denmark, they would have to relocate that production to the UK.\"</p><p>However, Ash Amirahmadi, Arla's UK Managing Director, told Business Insider that the company would not be able to move Lurpark production to the UK, as Eustice told the BBC's Marr, because it would be illegal.</p><p>\"The picture around moving products into the UK is a bit more complicated than that statement,\" he said.</p><p>\"If you take Lurpak on its own, it is subject to legal protection which means it can only be made in Denmark.</p><p>\"It can't be produced in the UK. The Secretary of State may or may not have known that.\"</p><p>He warned that tariffs on dairy products imported into the UK from abroad, like Lurpak from Denmark, would almost certainly lead to price rises in UK supermarkets and potentially a reduction in product availability.</p><p>\"We would have to pass on the cost to our customers,\" Amirahmadi told Business Insider.</p><p>\"Obviously it's not for us to tell customers what to do. But I would be very surprised if our customers didn't have to absorb the cost. If we are in a situation of no negotiated deal, then we are looking at increased retail inflation.\"</p><p>The dairy industry is set to be one of the hardest hit in the event of UK and EU negotiators failing to negotiate a trade deal before the end of the year.</p><p>Around 98% of UK dairy imports come from the EU and under UK government plans from January 1, 2021 they will have tariffs of around 35% slapped on them if negotiators fail to agree a free trade deal. A <a href=\"https://www.lse.ac.uk/business-and-consultancy/consulting/assets/documents/the-impact-of-brexit-on-the-uk-dairy-sector.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">2018 London School Economics report</a> into how Brexit would affect Arla specifically warned that \"any increases in trade costs would likely have a major impact on the domestic dairy market in the form of shortages of products and significantly higher prices.\"</p><p>Amirahmadi said that the dairy industry was particularly vulnerable to the UK trading with the EU on costly World Trade Organisation Terms, or what Prime Minister Johnson's government calls \"Australian-style\" trading rules, because \"dairy is high-volume, low-margin,\" meaning businesses would quickly struggle to afford increased costs.</p><p>He warned that the UK was \"potentially heading for a triple whammy\" — namely, the adverse effects of Brexit on food prices and availability coinciding with the impact of the coronavirus and the demands of the Christmas period.</p><p>\"We've got Christmas trading and nobody is really that clear how Christmas is going to trade this year, we've got a second wave of COVID-19 and a recession, and then the potential of products being less available in shops and prices being higher.</p><p>\"Consumers are going to be pretty grumpy,\" he said.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb3e2dad0c5f834e966ee46?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Arla\" height=\"750\" width=\"1500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Horst Galuschka/picture alliance via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Arla is urging Johnson's government to secure a free trade deal with Brussels, he said, warning that \"if we want to avoid availability issues and if we want to avoid consumer price inflation, then the only solution is a free trade agreement.\"</p><p>The UK negotiating team fronted by David Frost is in Brussels, Belgium this week where it is continuing negotiations with its EU counterparts, led by Michel Barnier. The two sides are in a race against time to secure a free trade agreement and get it ratified by EU countries and parliamentarians before the end of the year, when the UK will leave the EU's trading rules.</p><p>A spokesperson for Prime Minister Johnson said that the two sides were still grappling with disagreements over two issues: fisheries and what the EU calls a level playing field, which is intended to stop the UK undercutting European markets and vice versa.</p><p>\"Significant issues remain, particularly on the so-called level playing field and fisheries,\" they said. \"We are working hard to find solutions which fully respect UK sovereignty, but it is far from certain that an agreement will prove possible and time is now very short.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the slogan to read \"Standing Up For What's Right,\" an apparent act of defiance in its ongoing feud with President Donald Trump.&#160;</p><p>The new slogan appears on primetime chyrons to replace \"Democracy 2020,\" which it has used since the beginning of this election year.</p><p>It comes soon after Trump went on a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-fox-news-tweets-retweet-spree-new-network-2020-11\">retweet spree</a> against the network, making sure his 89 million followers saw the statement \"#foxnews is dead.\"</p><p>Trump's campaign was furious when the network accurately called Biden's win in Arizona long before other networks did.</p><p>Although Fox News' straight-news election reporters have largely pushed back against his claims of election fraud in their coverage, its primetime opinion hosts have fueled them.</p><p>Given that the slogan mainly goes with their shows, there is some ambiguity as to what is meant by the \"what's right\" of the slogan.</p><p>For a long time Trump's favorite network, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/times-trump-criticized-fox-news-anchors-2019-11\">Fox News has in recent years been replaced</a> in his affections by more straightforwardly supportive networks such as <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/one-america-news-network-donald-trump-tv-news-outlets-2019-10\">One America News (OAN)</a> and Newsmax.&#160;</p><p>In a likely reference to his own Monday</a>.&#160;</p><p>Fox News still continues to dominate primetime cable ratings, with \"Tucker Carlson Tonight\" averaging 5.36 million viewers in October, <a as the most-viewed right-wing news website.</p><p>Points during the election period — during which Newsmax also took time to bash Fox News — have seen a seven-fold increase in its viewership, CNN reported.&#160;</p><p>And it appears to want to bring Trump into the fold — its CEO Chris Ruddy said that he would be willing to offer Trump <a the Apple Watch Series 6, the Apple Watch SE, and the Apple Watch Series 3. All of them can be found for a deal at the moment in early Black Friday deals.&#160;</p><p>The $399 <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/black-friday-deals\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Apple Watch Series 6</a> is Apple's top model that comes with a new blood-oxygen sensor to measure SpO2 levels to track your overall respiratory and cardiac health. While it comes with core fitness tracking features and sensors, it doesn't come with the advanced health and fitness tracking sensors like an ECG or SpO2 sensor, and thus doesn't include some of the more advanced health and fitness tracking features as the Series 6. It runs on the same processor as the Series 5, giving it plenty of power for most people's needs.&#160;</p><p>Apple is still selling the 2017 <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-watch-series-3-review-1-year-later-2018-9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Apple Watch 3</a> for $199, making it an option for budget-conscious buyers to get the core Apple Watch experience.&#160;</p><p>Other Apple Watch models like the Series 5 and Series 4 can still be found, but they're not being given the Black Friday treatment as of yet.</p><h2>Early Black Friday Apple Watch deals</h2><p>Some deals exist for Apple's current Apple Watch models, like the Series 6, SE, and Series 3. For Series 5, the top model of 2019, we only saw a $20 discount on Black Friday from $429 to $409.
