Villas-Boas)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fb3d6d259ad4c30e23c2636?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn91@2020_2/2020/11/17/16-31-46-718_6b4d82c9ae3f31fa.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn83@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-54-041_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=fETXzCmH6YI:ZL8tS4F5v6c:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn44@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-48-227_ec8dd395c6ba42a7.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=fETXzCmH6YI:ZL8tS4F5v6c:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn95@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-45-684_d3b7e6e44c5e1ed1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn96@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-50-199_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=fETXzCmH6YI:ZL8tS4F5v6c:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn64@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-55-525_f745c1d99e763b8b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/fETXzCmH6YI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn96@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-46-661_c78db5af55e8f6ed.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630688467},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"Republicans leaders privately described Trump as a political liability and said they faced losing Senate runoffs","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/republicans-privately-call-trump-a-liability-who-lost-election-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb3c32a3ad3bb2fa0213b50?format=jpeg\" alt=\"donald trump lose again 2024\" height=\"1030\" width=\"2060\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President Donald Trump.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Key Republican figures expressed concerns about the runoff Senate elections in Georgia on a conference call on November 10, The Washington Post reported on Monday.</li>\n<li>In the call with the GOP strategist Karl Rove and party donors, Sen. David Perdue said an \"anti-Trump vote\" had cost the party.</li>\n<li>Sen. Todd Young said he was \"assuming the worst\" about the party's chance of holding on to control of the Senate.</li>\n<li>Participants on the call also acknowledged that Trump had likely lost the election to President-elect Joe Biden, The Post reported.</li>\n<li>Victories for Jon Ossoff and Raphael Warnock in Georgia would give the Democrats a narrow majority in the Senate.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Republican senators in Georgia, where runoff elections in January will determine which party controls the Senate, expressed concerns about their chances of victory and described President Donald Trump as a political liability in a conference call on November 10, <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/georgia-senate-runoffs-gop-t/2020/11/16/9d7c0678-2848-11eb-8fa2-06e7cbb145c0_story.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Washington Post reported on Monday</a>.</p><p>On the call, Sens. David Perdue and Kelly Loeffler, the Republican strategist Karl Rove, and party donors discussed strategies for defeating the senators' Democratic challengers early next year, The Post reported, citing \"a person who provided a detailed and precise account of what was said by each speaker on the call.\"</p><p>Perdue and Loeffler said that despite Trump's continued refusal to accept defeat in the presidential election, the January runoff elections would take place with President-elect Joe Biden on his way to the White House, The Post reported.</p><p>Perdue, who is being challenged by the Democratic candidate Jon Ossoff, said that maximizing Republican turnout would be particularly hard \"given that President Trump, it looks like now, may not be able to hold out.\"</p><p>But Perdue said Republicans might be better poised to hold the seats because of the absence of an \"anti-Trump vote.\"</p><p>\"I'm talking about people that may have voted for Biden but now may come back and vote for us because there was an anti-Trump vote in Georgia,\" he said, according to The Post. \"And we think some of those people, particularly in the suburbs, may come back to us. And I'm hopeful of that.\"</p><p>Sen. Todd Young of Indiana said he was \"assuming the worst but hoping for the best\" about Republicans' prospects of holding on to the seats.</p><p>\"And the worst-case scenario is that we have a Democrat in the White House, that we have Nancy Pelosi still with her hands on that speaker's gavel, which appears almost a certainty,\" Young said, according to The Post.</p><p>A Biden campaign source told Business Insider they were hopeful that Trump's behavior since losing the election would help the Democrats in Georgia. \"Trump's madness is helping interest in our Senate candidates,\" the source said.</p><p>The Republican figures on the call expressed concerns about turnout and about Georgia's changing demographics, fueled by more liberal voters in the capital, Atlanta, according to the report.</p><p>\"They changed, dramatically, the face of the electorate in Georgia. Many of these new voters are from California, Illinois, New York, New Jersey, and they're not of the conservative persuasion,\" Perdue reportedly said, adding: \"This is really not about messaging. It's not about persuasion in my race. It's more about getting the vote out.\"</p><p>Loeffler, who risks being unseated by the Democratic challenger Raphael Warnock, also said turnout would be key, telling others on the call that \"the question is about the Democrat turnout,\" The Post reported.</p><p>Victories for Ossoff and Warnock would give Democrats control of the Senate, as Vice President-elect Kamala Harris would have the tie-breaking vote in a split chamber. That would also give Democrats control of the White House, the House, and the Senate, which, in theory, would give Biden greater freedom to enact domestic policy.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read 2020 12:32:37 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5fb3c23859ad4c2c1075a847?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"87c64a39d1591d3846a5d8fc91ce5b1f","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn76@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-55-654_a558f4644f404aec.webp","destWidth":1381,"destHeight":1036,"sourceBytes":46952,"destBytes":46952,"author":"apayne@businessinsider.com (Adam Payne)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fb3c32a3ad3bb2fa0213b50?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn47@2020_1/2020/11/17/16-31-51-353_507d6cf8910d4756.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn83@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-54-041_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=eCnkWH6_e8c:aMU1kJR2piA:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn11@2020_5/2020/11/17/16-31-52-025_01e9f53343814cf1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=eCnkWH6_e8c:aMU1kJR2piA:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn71@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-55-608_8b022f939794984a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn96@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-50-199_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=eCnkWH6_e8c:aMU1kJR2piA:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn83@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-51-600_fed70b71127b6e9c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/eCnkWH6_e8c":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn4@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-48-482_3803157aa4e4e6b4.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630688557},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"Why won't my hotspot work? How to troubleshoot your phone's mobile hotspot and provide an internet connection for other devices","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/why-wont-my-hotspot-work","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2c6ee402d49001924f2eb?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman using laptop phone and tablet remote outdoors\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>If your mobile hotspot isn&#39;t working, here&#39;s how you can try to fix it.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Westend61/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>If your phone's hotspot won't work, there could be a number of different culprits causing the problem.</li>\n<li>Most issues with a hotspot can be solved by troubleshooting at home &#8212; and if you have an Android instead of an iPhone, you have more options to fix the problem.</li>\n<li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\">Visit Business Insider's Tech Reference library for more stories</a>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Picture this: You're out somewhere and you need to do some work on your laptop, but the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/wifi\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Wi-Fi</a> is unbearably slow. Normally, this wouldn't be a problem — your cell phone gets good <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/lte\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">LTE</a> service, you can just connect your computer to your phone's mobile hotspot. But you try to connect to it and it won't work. Why?</p><p>This is a question with many possible answers, and many of them also depend on what type of phone you have.&#160;</p><h2>How to troubleshoot a hotspot that won't work</h2><p>If your mobile hotspot isn't working, run through this troubleshooting list to figure out why.</p><h3><strong>Make sure your phone's internet connection is working</strong></h3><p>Go to your phone's settings app and check to make sure your cellular data is switched on. You should also try to use the internet on your phone to make sure you're not in an area with slow or bad reception.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2b865402d49001924f296?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Why_won_t_my_hotspot_work_ _1\" height=\"1423\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Make sure to turn your cellular data on by swiping the switch to the right, turning the button green.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Melanie Weir/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>You should also check and make sure you haven't exceeded your cellular data limit for the month — if you're on a prepaid plan with a limit, your data speeds will be throttled when you pass it, rendering your hotspot essentially useless. To solve this issue, contact your data provider.</p><h3><strong>Make sure the Wi-Fi of the device you're trying to connect to is working</strong></h3><p>If your device won't connect to your phone, it could actually be a device issue. Try connecting to your phone's hotspot with another device. If it works, the problem is likely not your phone.</p><p>Turn the Wi-Fi on your connecting device on and off and see if that fixes the problem. If not, try restarting your device. If you still have issues, you may need to take it in for repairs.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2b905402d49001924f29b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Why_won_t_my_hotspot_work_ _2\" height=\"800\" width=\"896\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Try turning the Wi-Fi on your connecting device off and on again.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Melanie Weir/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h3><strong>Make sure the password is right</strong></h3><p>If your hotspot is password protected, look at the password on your phone and make sure you've entered the password correctly on the device you're connecting with — if it's not, you won't be able to connect.</p><p>If you're still having trouble, you can also change the password to something that will be easier to enter without mistakes.</p><h3><strong>Disable battery saver or low power mode</strong></h3><p>Battery saver mode works by limiting certain non-essential functions on your phone to conserve battery life. This isn't supposed to include limiting your phone's ability to connect to a hotspot, but all software gets buggy from time to time. This is an issue that is known to occur, especially on Android.&#160;</p><p>Try turning battery saver off and see if that fixes the issue.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2b990402d49001924f2a0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Why_won_t_my_hotspot_work_ _4\" height=\"800\" width=\"904\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Make sure the low power mode on your device is turned off.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Melanie Weir/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h3><strong>Turn your phone's Wi-Fi on and off</strong></h3><p>Speaking of bugs in the system, even though your phone's Wi-Fi isn't usually the victim of them, it's not impossible for that to be the case. If it doesn't seem to be working, try switching it off and back on again and see if that fixes the issue.</p><h3><strong>Wi-Fi not working? Pair using Bluetooth or USB</strong></h3><p>Wi-Fi isn't the only way to connect devices to your phone's hotspot. You can also pair your phone and computer using <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/bluetooth\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bluetooth</a> or a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/usb\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">USB</a> cable.&#160;</p><p>To connect to an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/iphone\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">iPhone's</a> cellular network via Bluetooth, turn on Bluetooth on your phone, connect to it from your other device, and confirm the connection on your phone.&#160;</p><p>To connect to an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/android\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Android</a> via Bluetooth or USB tethering, go to \"Settings &#62; Network and Internet &#62; Hotspot and tethering\" and toggle the relevant switch to the on position, then connect with your other device.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2bb031c741f0019aca07b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Why_won_t_my_hotspot_work_ _6\" height=\"847\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Try using Bluetooth or a USB connection if Wi-Fi won&#39;t work.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Melanie Weir/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h3><strong>Try restarting your phone</strong></h3><p>Sometimes if your phone is on for too long, especially if several programs are running in the background, your phone can begin processing slower or even experiencing bugs — and it becomes more likely to happen if the battery life is low.&#160;</p><p>In that case, it's possible the problems you're experiencing with your hotspot could easily be simply solved by restarting your phone.</p><p>If you have an iPhone, this is about all you can do to fix any hotspot issues you might be having — if none of these troubleshooting options can solve your problem, it may be a bug in a software update, or you might need to take your phone in to be looked at.</p><h2>More troubleshooting options if you have an Android phone</h2><h3><strong>Roll back your software</strong></h3><p>Unlike iPhones, Android phones let you roll back software updates if you don't like them or they don't work on your phone.&#160;</p><p>Since it's possible that your hotspot issues are being caused by a bug in a software update, try going back to the older version of your OS and see if that fixes the issue. If it doesn't, you can always download the update again.</p><h3><strong>Disable automatic hotspot switching</strong></h3><p>With some newer phones, the hotspot will turn itself off if no device is connected to it for a few minutes. This might give you issues if your device goes into sleep mode, or if you leave the room and come back.</p><p>If this is your issue, go to \"Settings &#62; Network and Internet &#62; Hotspot and tethering &#62; Wi-Fi hotspot &#62; Advanced\" and switch the slider for \"Turn off hotspot automatically\" to the off position.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2bb8f402d49001924f2b2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Why_won_t_my_hotspot_work_ _7\" height=\"977\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Turn automatic hotspot switching off so that the toggle is no longer blue.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Melanie Weir/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h3><strong>Create a new, open mobile hotspot</strong></h3><p>While password-protected hotspots are safer because they're encrypted, that encryption can sometimes lead to issues connecting to a hotspot. Sometimes a hotspot will work better with your device if you just leave it open.</p><p>To change your hotspot to an open network, go to \"Settings &#62; Network and Internet &#62; Hotspot and tethering &#62; Wi-Fi hotspot\" and change the Security setting to \"None.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2bbf9402d49001924f2b7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Why_won_t_my_hotspot_work_ _8\" height=\"963\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Turn off the security to your hotspot to deal with encryption issues.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Melanie Weir/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>As a warning — this does leave you open to other people joining the network and using your cellular data, too. If you're in a public place, or are concerned about others nearby using your data, this may not be the best option.</p><h3><strong>Change the frequency band to 2.4GHz</strong></h3><p>Newer Android phones also come with the ability to change the frequency of the signal you send out to create the hotspot. While a 5GHz band is faster, many devices may not be able to pick it up, meaning you wouldn't see it listed under possible connections on the device you're trying to connect to your hotspot.</p><p>To switch back to the standard 2.4GHz band, go to \"Settings &#62; Network and Internet &#62; Hotspot and tethering &#62; Wi-Fi hotspot.\" Tap \"AP Band,\" then select 2.4GHz from the list.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2c4b0402d49001924f2dd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Why_won_t_my_hotspot_work_ _9\" height=\"963\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Switch your frequency band to a lower one.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Melanie Weir/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><div id=\"ProductCard_5d8e19fb2e22af18f40d281d\" style=\"position:relative; class=\"copyright\">Reuters/Gary Cameron</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>Amazon's launch of its own digital pharmacy on Tuesday sent rival pharmacy stocks reeling, with CVS, Walgreens, and Rite-Aid each falling more than 8%.</strong></li><li><strong>Amazon first entered the pharmacy business in 2018 with its $753 million acquisition of PillPack, which signaled to investors that Amazon's interest in offering prescription medicines directly to consumers was growing.</strong></li><li><strong>Now, the pharmacy section of Amazon's e-commerce website will offer discounts to paying Prime members, allow patients to pay with their health insurance, and display the price of the drug with and without insurance.</strong></li><li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestutm_source=msn.com&utm_medium=referral&utm_content=msn-slideshow&utm_campaign=bodyurl?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestarkets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Visit the Business Insider homepage for more stories</a>.</strong></li></ul><hr><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/amzn-stock\">Amazon's</a> foray into the prescription-medicine space deepened on Tuesday after the e-commerce giant <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-starts-selling-prescription-medication-in-us-2020-11\">launched a digital pharmacy store</a> as a section within its retail website.</p><p>Now, shoppers can buy their prescription medicines directly from Amazon's website, with the ability to pay with insurance or without. Amazon Prime members will receive discounts on certain medicines and two-day shipping, adding a few more perks to the list of Amazon Prime benefits.</p><p>The announcement resulted in a big hit to the share prices of competing pharmacies. Here's a rundown of the biggest stock moves:</p><ul><li><strong>CVS Health:&#160;</strong>-8%</li><li><strong>Walgreen Boots Alliance:&#160;</strong>-10%</li><li><strong>Rite Aid:</strong> -12%</li><li><strong>GoodRx:&#160;</strong>-19%</li></ul><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/multifamily-real-estate-investing-strategy-affordable-housing-units-evan-holladay-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">30 years old with a piece of 300 units: Here's how Evan Holladay is filling a unique multifamily real-estate niche with an under-the-radar strategy</a></em></p><p>This is hardly the first time a foray from Amazon into an industry has wiped out billions in market value from competing firms. Back in 2017, when the consumer conglomerate acquire Whole Foods, the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jeff-bezos-just-handed-corporate-america-a-50-billion-question-2017-6\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">entire grocery sector saw deep losses</a>.</p><p>The move has been in the works for some time, first hinted by Amazon's state by state application approval process to sell prescription medicines, which began in 2017, and followed up by <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-pharmacy-pillpack-acquisition-merger-latest-push-into-healthcare-2018-6\">its 2018 acquisition of PillPack</a> for $753 million.</p><p>\"The Amazon Prime prescription savings benefit saves members up to 80% off generic and 40% off brand name medications when paying without insurance,\" Amazon said in <a href=\"https://press.aboutamazon.com/news-releases/news-release-details/introducing-amazon-pharmacy-prescription-medications-delivered?tag=bisafetynet2-20\">a press release</a>.</p><p>The digital pharmacy will also display the cost of medicines with or without insurance coverage, adding a new layer of transparency to the pharmaceutical industry that has largely been absent up until now.</p><p>\"We work hard behind the scenes to handle complications seamlessly so anyone who needs a prescription can understand their options, place their order for the lowest available price, and have their medication delivered quickly,\" said TJ Parker, Vice President of Amazon Pharmacy.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a Women&#39;s Summit in Washington October 13, 2015.  REUTERS/Kevin Lamarque/File Photo\" height=\"2144\" width=\"4287\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Warren Buffett.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>The \"Buffett Effect\" lifted AbbVie, Merck, Bristol Myers Squibb, and Pfizer shares on Tuesday.</strong></li><li><strong>The four pharmaceutical stocks jumped after Warren Buffett's Berkshire Hathaway revealed that it invested in them last quarter.</strong></li><li><strong>The famed investor's company disclosed stakes worth $1.8 billion to $1.9 billion in AbbVie, BMS, and Merck, as well as a $136 million Pfizer position.</strong></li><li><strong>The four holdings were worth nearly $6 billion as of Monday's close, up from $5.7 billion at the end of September, representing a $300 million gain for Berkshire.</strong></li><li><strong><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/international?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</strong></strong><hr></li></ul><p>AbbVie, Merck, Bristol Myers Squibb, and Pfizer are the latest beneficiaries of the \"Buffett Effect.\"</p><p>The quartet of pharmaceutical stocks jumped in pre-market trading on Tuesday after Warren Buffett's Berkshire Hathaway <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-invests-pfizer-merck-abbvie-pharmaceutical-stocks-2020-11-1029808269\">revealed on Monday</a> that it invested in them last quarter. AbbVie, Merck, and Pfizer gained as much as 2%, and BMS rose as much as 3%, whereas benchmark S&#38;P futures slid around 0.5%.</p><p>Buffett famously moves markets with his decisions, as many investors trust his judgment and copy his stock picks. Others anticipate that will happen and rush to buy the same stocks in order to profit from the \"Buffett Effect,\" making it a self-fulfilling prophecy to an extent.</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read More:&#160;</em></strong><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-europe-rotation-value-investing-jpmorgan-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-europe-rotation-value-investing-jpmorgan-2020-11\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">JPMorgan shares 35 European stocks across 10 sectors that you need to own in the rotation to value — including one that could see EPS growth of almost 700% next year</a></em></p><p>The billionaire investor's company bought about 21 million AbbVie shares, 30 million BMS shares, 22 million Merck shares, and 3.7 million Pfizer shares in the third quarter, it disclosed in a regulatory filing. Those holdings give it a 1.2% stake in AbbVie, a 1.3% stake in BMS, a 0.9% stake in Merck, and a 0.07% stake in Pfizer, assuming they haven't changed since September 30.</p><p>The AbbVie, BMS, and Merck positions were each worth between $1.8 billion and $1.9 billion at the end of last quarter, while the smaller Pfizer position was worth $136 million. The four holdings were worth almost $6 billion in total as of Monday's close, up from $5.7 billion at the end of September, meaning Berkshire has already scored a $300 million gain on them.</p><div 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"6 ways to motivate your employees to keep learning and upskilling at work","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/ways-to-foster-supportive-learning-environment-at-work-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e4c001d2dae5c45f666d109?format=jpeg\" alt=\"employees talking to each other\" height=\"2000\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A strong learning environment can attract and retain top talent.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Klaus Vedfelt/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Businesses should invest in upskilling and training employees to keep up with emerging technologies and new business goals.&#160;</li>\n<li>When learning becomes one of your core company values, it increases job satisfaction, unlocks new career paths, and improves employee retention.</li>\n<li>Dedicate time and resources for self-learning, like workshops, one-on-ones, guest speakers, and a training and development department to employees.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>No company can reach its&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/business-goals\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/business-goals\">business goals</a>&#160;without a qualified and dedicated workforce. As new technologies emerge, on-job&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/training\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/training\">training</a>&#160;programs have become increasingly useful to enhance both employees' soft and practical skills. But&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/learning\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/learning\">learning</a>&#160;at work can go beyond formal training. Businesses should get creative so that employees are constantly developing their skills.</p><h2><strong>The benefits of ongoing training</strong></h2><p>While most companies invest in costly&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/recruitment\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/recruitment\">recruitment</a>&#160;processes to attract the right candidates, their efforts on&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/employee-engagement\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/employee-engagement\">employee engagement</a>&#160;and&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/education\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/education\">education</a>&#160;often fall short. Without any type of incentives or supportive programs, it's easy for employees to feel overlooked and unappreciated after a while —&#160;and for companies' growth to lag in turn.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-build-company-wellness-program-employees-healthy-motivated-2020-8\">How to build a comprehensive wellness program that keeps employees happy, healthy, and motivated for the long haul</a></em></p><p>Creating a strong learning environment can help your business&#160;attract and retain top talent. Benefits of investing in ongoing learning include:</p><ul><li><strong>Improved employee satisfaction.</strong>&#160;Unsatisfied employees will do the bare minimum. Low levels of&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/productivity\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/productivity\">productivity</a>&#160;and engagement can lead your business's profitability to experience significant setbacks. Training and development opportunities will keep employees motivated and excited about acquiring new skills.</li><li><strong>Training gives employees the opportunity to explore.</strong>&#160;Let employees explore areas outside their field with ongoing training. Interacting with other&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/team\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ai-metadata\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/team\">team</a>&#160;members, using new technologies and learning new technical skills can help employees visualize potential career paths.</li><li><strong>It helps with retention.</strong>&#160;Employees with no development opportunities will eventually feel stuck and leave. Development programs and efforts provide employees with real on-the-job experience, help&#160;them further their careers and train&#160;them for potential future roles within the company. Incorporating learning into your workplace can decrease turnover and drive&#160;down recruitment costs in the long run. As your company grows, you will have trusted and experienced employees filling new positions.</li><li><strong>It breeds loyalty.</strong>&#160;Going the extra mile and investing in training programs empowers employees and makes them feel valued. Employees reward companies that contribute to their professional and personal goals with loyalty.&#160;</li><li><strong>It increases productivity.</strong>&#160;Although many employers find development opportunities expensive, well-structured training in the workplace increases employees' productivity and contributes to the output of the firm. Training programs provide employees with first-hand experiences that help them perform their tasks in better and more efficient ways.</li></ul><p>But training doesn't always have to look like a structured program or course. Here are, as promised, six&#160;ways to implement successful on-the-job training.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-leaders-track-manage-employee-performance-remotely\">How to best manage your employees' performance remotely — without coming off as a micromanager</a></em></p><h2>1. Make it part of your company values</h2><p>A company's core values are underlying principles that guide the organization towards its goals. By setting growth as one of your business core values, you won't only attract employees with similar mindsets, but also inspire experienced team members to pass on their skills and knowledge to others.</p><h2>2. Bring in speakers</h2><p>Doing this regularly is the perfect way to break out of the office's daily routine. Guest speakers can share valuable experiences that inspire your team and bring a fresh perspective to the workplace.&#160;</p><h2>3. Set aside self-learning time</h2><p>Between excelling at work and dealing with home life, it's difficult for people to find&#160;time they can completely dedicate to self-improvement. Setting aside even a couple hours a week for employees to take an online course or explore new software can make a huge difference.</p><p>Give your employees the time and tools they need to learn by themselves, and you will have a more confident and motivated team. It's also easy to do and costs you nothing.</p><h2>4. Organize employee-led workshops</h2><p>Employee-led workshops can provide team members with useful hacks and insights. These activities can also enhance the sense of community between team members. By learning from doers, employees will have a more comprehensive understanding of new technologies.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/linkedin-3-ways-create-learning-culture-within-company-2020-7\">Learning new skills is the key to helping workers stay happy and productive right now. Here are 3 easy ways to create a learning culture within your company, according to a vice president at LinkedIn</a></em></p><h2>5. Implement monthly one-on-ones</h2><p>One-on-ones allow honest and transparent communication&#160;between managers and team members. From setting expectations and giving feedback to chatting and clearing up doubts, they can keep your employees motivated and focused on the company's goals.</p><p>To get to know your team better and help them develop, provide them with constructive feedback through monthly one-on-ones. Then, create development goals with them to guide their growth.</p><h2>6. Start a training-and-development department</h2><p>Creating a strong learning culture requires long-term planning, resources&#160;and expertise. The methods mentioned above are free, but once you're ready to invest in training, you can create a department dedicated to growth. Besides implementing training programs, this department can work on measuring the overall performance of the company and developing strategies to improve.</p><p>Training-and-development opportunities can change your employees and your business for the better. Besides being more productive, employees feel more appreciated, confident and loyal. Meanwhile, ongoing training has long-term positive effects on performance, allowing your business to outperform the competition&#160;— which is ultimately the goal of any and all of these approaches.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/ways-to-foster-supportive-learning-environment-at-work-2020-11'>Business according to the Census Bureau. Economists surveyed by Bloomberg expected sales to increase by 0.5%. The reading also marked an decline from September's 1.6% increase.</p><p>The October report does, however, mark the sixth straight jump in retail spending since consumer spending froze in April. Stimulus measures including the $2.2 trillion CARES Act fueled a V-shaped rebound through the summer as households' balance sheets were bolstered by direct payments and expanded unemployment benefits. Spending still sits well above pre-pandemic levels, but the mild pace of improvement signals its recent strength might be waning.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/multifamily-real-estate-investing-strategy-affordable-housing-units-evan-holladay-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">30 years old with a piece of 300 units: Here's how Evan Holladay is filling a unique multifamily real-estate niche with an under-the-radar strategy</a></em></p><p>Any slowdown would have serious effects on the broad recovery. Retail spending accounts for 70% of economic activity, and after record gross domestic product growth in the third quarter, growth is expected to slow significantly through the end of the year. The next few months also mark a make-or-break point for retailers, as the holiday season fuels the busiest spending months of the year.</p><p>Spiking COVID-19 cases place critical fourth-quarter spending at serious risk. The US reported 148,532 new cases on Monday, bringing the total number of infections above 11 million, according to <a href=\"https://covidtracking.com/data\">The COVID Tracking Project</a>. Hospitalizations surpassed 73,000 and deaths neared 240,000.</p><p>Cities began announcing new lockdown measures earlier in November, and early readings from consumer sentiment gauges show Americans <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/consumer-sentiment-falls-surging-covid19-cases-concern-economic-recovery-umich-2020-11\">quickly growing more pessimistic toward the US economy's future</a>.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:&#160;</strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stocks-buy-stay-at-home-stock-picks-post-pandemic-barclays-2020-11\" data-analytics-position=\"7\" data-analytics-module=\"\">Barclays details its ultimate strategy for picking stay-at-home market winners for a post-COVID world — and shares 2 stocks all investors should own before the recovery accelerates</a></em></p><p>It's unlikely any stimulus aid will help offset the drop in consumer confidence. President Donald Trump urged Congress to pass a \"<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-congress-big-focused-coronavirus-relief-bill-2020-11\">big and focused</a>\" relief bill in a Saturday tweet, but major areas of difference remain between Democrats and Republicans.</p><p>White House negotiations with Democrats on a new package dissolved ahead of November's elections. Senate Majority Mitch McConnell now leads talks on stimulus, and his prior calls for a $500 billion bill square off with Democrats' urges for a sweeping $2.2 trillion measure.</p><p>A Biden administration may be able to reach a compromise, but that punts stimulus into the new year. Americans may need to wait through the holiday season and the virus's deadliest wave yet before seeing new fiscal support.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a retailer surged 79% and customers bought more electronics, sporting goods, and groceries during the pandemic.</p><p>The company recorded total revenue of $134.7 billion in the quarter to October 31, a 5.2% increase on the same time period last year, it said Tuesday.</p><p>Shoppers also bought more household cleaning products, but delayed starts to the school term and some colleges operating online only meant stationery sales were down, as were apparel sales.</p><p>Comparable US sales, which only includes stores open at least a year, rose 6.4%, excluding fuel sales. This beat analyst expectations, who had estimated an increase of 4.16%, <a href=\"https://uk.reuters.com/article/us-walmart-results/walmart-beats-same-store-sales-estimates-on-buoyant-online-demand-idUKKBN27X1G0\">according to IBES data from Refinitiv</a>.</p><p>Walmart's operating income rose 22.5% to $5.8 billion, and the company paid around $600 million in incremental expenses related to COVID-19.</p><p>Online sales also grew 41% at Sam's Club, owned by Walmart, and comparable sales increased 11.1%, though it reported reduced tobacco sales.</p><p>Walmart International, however, posted a more moderate increase in sales. Net sales in the quarter reached $29.6 billion, an increase of 1.3% year-on-year. Part of this was caused by changes in currency rates, the company said.&#160; Excluding currency, net sales would have been $30.6 billion, an increase of 5.0%, led by Flipkart, sales in Canada, and Walmex.</p><p>On Sunday, Walmart announced it was <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-seiyu-deal-kkr-rakuten-walmart-japan-2020-11\">selling a majority stake in 300-store Japanese supermarket chain Seiyu</a>, which would bring its own stake down to 15%. In October, Walmart&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-sells-asda-for-8-8-billion-2020-10\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"760c1a79acbbc9584c57bd8319575bb9\">sold&#160;</a><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-sells-asda-for-8-8-billion-2020-10\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"760c1a79acbbc9584c57bd8319575bb9\">UK grocery chain Asda for $8.8 billion</a>&#160;after 21 years of ownership, marking a near-exit from the UK.</p><p>In the quarter, Walmart continued to diversify its business to try to meet changing customer needs during the COVID-19 pandemic</p><p>It unveiled plans to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-black-friday-stores-limited-capacity-3-day-event-2020-10\">revise Black Friday</a> by launching its deals over three separate days, with offers available online at least two days before they hit stores.</p><p>Walmart also <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-drone-delivery-partnerships-tom-ward-2020-9\">partnered with three different drone companies</a> to start experimenting with delivery tech as shoppers seek contact-free ways of getting groceries.</p><p>In September, the retail giant <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-unveils-amazon-prime-rival-walmart-plus-costing-98-annually-2020-8\">launched its Amazon Prime rival Walmart Plus</a>, which offers free grocery delivery and fuel discounts for $98 a year.</p><p>Walmart expected the demand for convenient, digital, and contact-free shopping to continue, it said.</p><p>\"We think these new customer behaviors will largely persist and we're well positioned to serve customers with the value and experience they're looking for,\" Walmart CEO Doug McMillon said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"Video games might actually be good for you, Oxford study finds","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/video-games-mental-health-gaming-wellbeing-oxford-study-research-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5efb8e70aee6a823ad1dc080?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Animal Crossing\" height=\"1080\" width=\"1440\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>&#34;Animal Crossing&#34; was one of two games used in the study.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Nintendo</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A new study from Oxford Univeristy found a positive correlation between time spent gaming and people's wellbeing.</li>\n<li>The study focused on 3,274 gamers playing \"Animal Crossing: New Horizons\" and \"Plants vs Zombies: Battle for Neighborville.\"</li>\n<li>Study lead Professor Andrew Przybylski told Business Insider the study was a \"baby step\" towards new methods for studying gaming in a more meaningful and nuanced way.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A new study from Oxford University suggests video games could have a positive influence on people's wellbeing.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://psyarxiv.com/qrjza/\">study</a>, conducted by the Oxford Internet Institute, focused on two games — \"<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/animal-crossing-new-horizons-on-track-to-be-best-selling-switch-game-2020-11\">Animal Crossing: New Horizons</a>\" and \"Plants vs Zombies: Battle for Neighborville.\" The study involved 3,274 gamers over the age of 18.</p><p>Working in tandem with the games' creators, Nintendo for Animal Crossing and EA for Plants vs Zombies, the study tracked the amount of time survey respondents spent in-game, and combined this with a survey of players' mental wellbeing.</p><p>\"Contrary to many fears that excessive game time will lead to addiction and poor mental health, we found a small positive relation between game play and wellbeing,\" the study found.&#160;</p><p>Study lead Professor Andrew Przybylski told Business Insider this was a major step forward for research into the psychological effect of playing video games. Previously, studies have relied on asking subjects to estimate how much time they spend playing, which can be unreliable, he said.</p><p>For this study, Nintendo and EA reached out to regular players of their games to invite them to take part in the study. Respondents were then assigned a unique identifier key code, which they plugged in when completing the Oxford survey.</p><p>Oxford then sent the keys back to Nintendo and EA, who in turn released the player data. \"That way, like nobody had both parts of the puzzle,\" said Przybylski.</p><p>\"This study actually has us looking over the shoulder of gamers with a stopwatch,\" Przybylski said.</p><p>He added that reaching out to subjects via Nintendo and EA was helpful, as previous studies have searched for respondents on places like Reddit and gaming addiction forums, which increases the possibility that problem gamers make up part of the sample.</p><p>Przybylski emphasized that the study was not definitive, and came with major caveats. \"This is two games out of a million […] these are social video games, and this is just a correlation,\" he said.</p><p>He described the study as a \"baby step\" towards better methodologies for studying gaming, and emphasised that purely studying time spent in-game was not enough to gain a proper understanding of gaming.</p><p>\"It would be like studying nutrition if all you have was the amount of time that people spent in restaurants,\" he said.</p><p>He's hopeful, however, that the study will be a good proof-of-concept, and could lead to more co-operation between academics and the gaming industry, leading to better studies of gaming behaviors.</p><p>\"There's a wide range of pro-social and antisocial behaviors that happen in games, and there's a wide range of positive and negative experiences that we might be more or less likely to get into if we're having a good or a bad day,\" he said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Hamilton)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5efb8e70aee6a823ad1dc080?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn57@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-29-623_9c4e466370b95569.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn83@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-54-041_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=XBAwtB6fINs:hl7R7dFIyBE:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn15@2020_5/2020/11/17/16-31-52-901_8a9a2e6813739083.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=XBAwtB6fINs:hl7R7dFIyBE:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn43@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-52-179_421eb45254009baa.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn96@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-50-199_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=XBAwtB6fINs:hl7R7dFIyBE:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn32@2020_2/2020/11/17/16-31-55-329_8bb7c85e74b827dd.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/XBAwtB6fINs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn55@2020_1/2020/11/17/16-31-46-420_3f46e898b55f995c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630688584},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"I'm a chess grandmaster who's made over $280,000 from esports tournaments. As the highest-rated blitz player in the world, I spend up to 7 hours a day playing chess online.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/job-diary-professional-chess-esports-athlete-tsm-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faadf411df1d50018219f37?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hikaru Nakamura lead\" height=\"1683\" width=\"2244\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Hikaru Nakamura is a professional esports athlete and champion chess player.\n<p class=\"copyright\">TSM</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Hikaru Nakamura is a 32-year-old esports athlete based in Los Angeles, California.</li>\n<li>He is the first chess player to join the esports team TSM (formerly <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/top-esports-organizations-and-teams-power-list-faze-100-thieves-2020-4#team-solomid-18\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"0675549005f5e514d0b629bd4ca571df\">Team SoloMid</a>). According to <a href=\"https://www.esportsearnings.com/players/75837-hikaru-nakamura\">Esports Earnings</a>, Nakamura has made over $281,000 in winnings from online chess tournaments in 2020.</li>\n<li>At 15, Nakamura became the youngest American to win the title of chess Grandmaster, and competed worldwide as a professional chess player before transitioning to esports. He's currently the <a href=\"https://ratings.fide.com/top.phtml?list=men_blitz\">highest-ranked</a> blitz player worldwide.&#160;</li>\n<li>When he's not prepping for a competition, Nakamura streams on Twitch for four to seven hours a day to an audience of 570,000 followers.</li>\n<li>Here's what his job is like, as told to freelance writer Claire Turrell.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Some people know me as Hikaru Nakamura, while others may know me as GMHikaru. I'm an esport athlete and chess grandmaster. I've been playing computer games since I was eight years old, and I was just signed by USA esport giant TSM as its first esport chess player.</p><p>My stepfather and brother are both chess players and my interest started when I followed them to tournaments. In 2003, I became the youngest American to earn the title of <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/2020/8/27/21404322/hikaru-nakamura-chess-tsm-esports-sign-contract-player-twitch\">grandmaster</a> at the age of 15 years and 79 days.</p><p>I realized chess could be more than a hobby for me when I dropped out of Dickinson College in 2006 and decided to pursue a career as a professional chess player, competing around the world.</p><h2><strong>I was first introduced to console games at the age of 6.</strong></h2><p><strong><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faae0161df1d50018219f47?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hikaru Nakamura 1\" height=\"2986\" width=\"3978\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Hikaru Nakamura.\n<p class=\"copyright\">TSM</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></strong></p><p>It was 1994, and I was in Japan with my mom and brother visiting my biological father. I played games like Mario Kart with the old cartridges, but it wasn't until 1998 that I had my first real introduction to PC games, with StarCraft: Brood War. I also played chess online, but I didn't start playing it seriously until much later.</p><p>In 2018, I started streaming on the gaming platform Twitch, where people also broadcast themselves playing games like Fortnite and Call of Duty. Currently, my Twitch channel <a href=\"https://www.twitch.tv/gmhikaru\">GMHikaru</a> has over 570,000 followers.</p><p><em><strong>Read more</strong>: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tv-networks-have-hard-time-getting-young-viewers-watch-sports-2020-5\">Older fans may leap back into watching sports on TV post-pandemic, but networks are going to have a tougher time winning back younger viewers</a></em></p><h2><strong>In August 2020, I signed with esports organization TSM as its first esports chess player.</strong></h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faae241f7d1cb0019e3ae7d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"credit_Hikaru Nakamura jersey\" height=\"891\" width=\"1188\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Nakamura wears this esports jersey when competing under TSM.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Hikaru Nakamura</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>TSM is one of the world's largest esports organizations with teams playing games such as League of Legends, Fortnite, and Valorant. It's about to open a huge <a href=\"https://www.latimes.com/sports/story/2019-09-11/largest-esports-training-center-north-america-los-angeles\">gaming facility</a>&#160;in Playa Vista, California, which will have a theatre, scrim rooms, academy coaching rooms, a gym, float tank, and nap pods. However, at the moment, like everyone else, I'm working from home.</p><p>The one big change to my life during COVID-19 is my transition from a professional chess player to a full-time streamer. Ironically, I cut down on my traditional over the board competitions in the beginning of 2020, as I was a little burned out and wanted to refocus on defending my US Championship Title.</p><p>I only played in a few events from October 2019 through March 2020 when everything got shut down. Lockdown has allowed me to focus full time on streaming and share the game of chess with the Twitch audience.</p><h2><strong>The biggest misconception about chess in esports is that it's less prestigious than the board game.</strong></h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faae0ee1df1d50018219f51?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hikaru Nakamura Eric Rosen\" height=\"2745\" width=\"3660\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Nakamura and fellow Twitch streamer Eric Rosen.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Eric Rosen</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>People might not realize that online chess has been around since 1993, which predates almost all other esports. While traditional games can take up to five hours, online chess games move at a blistering pace and can be completed in as quickly as 10 minutes.</p><p>Fans are now becoming aware of the expertise that's needed, such as mouse skills, which are extremely important when players have only seconds left on the clock.&#160;</p><p>Other elements that you get in the esports game, which you don't get with the board game, is the ability to pre-move and make moves in 0.1 seconds. This makes it a big pull for fans as it's very viewer friendly.</p><h2><strong>On an average day when I'm not competing, I'll stream for four to seven hours.</strong></h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faae2cb1df1d50018219f6e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hikaru Nakamura streaming_\" height=\"1011\" width=\"1348\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Nakamura streams live games, analysis, and interactive games on Twitch.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Hikaru Nakamura</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>I wake up around 6 a.m., boot up my stream around 8 a.m., and stream sometimes until 3 p.m. I play chess, give analysis, and invite some of my subscribers to play against me to make my streams interactive.</p><p>After that, I usually take an hour or two to clear my head while uploading VODs (videos on demand) so that my video editing team can work on the content and upload it to YouTube.</p><p>From there, I usually try to discuss content ideas or what the plans are for the next couple of streams before zoning out and reading a book or watching Netflix and going to sleep around 10 p.m.</p><p><em><strong>Read more</strong>: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/started-own-sports-agency-now-represent-8-top-wnba-stars-2020-10\">I started my own sports agency when I was 22 and now represent 8 top WNBA stars — including the legendary Lisa Leslie. Here's how I landed major clients and built my business.</a></em></p><h2><strong>If it's a competition day, my schedule is more rigorous.</strong></h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faae30b1df1d50018219f72?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hikaru Nakamura 2\" height=\"1080\" width=\"1920\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Nakamura competes online for four to five hours on tournament days.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Hikaru Nakamura</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>I'll wake up around 5 a.m., as most competitions start at 7 a.m. I spend two hours working on chess preparation and my opening strategy, and then I'll compete online for four to five hours. Once I've finished, I'll do a couple of hours of streaming to discuss my games and review the moves that I made. After that, I'll head to bed around 9 p.m.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.esportsearnings.com/players/75837-hikaru-nakamura\">I've played</a> in six major online competitions so far in 2020, and I'll play at least two more before the end of the year.</p><p>I generally try to eat an energy-packed meal like pasta before a stream, since it can go on for hours without a break. If I'm behind schedule, I'll usually eat a couple of breakfast bars and survive on coffee. I've never been overly superstitious when it comes to competitions, but from time to time, I will wear the same shirt multiple days if I had a great game.</p><h2><strong>As a streamer, the days tend to blur together, so I very rarely pay attention to whether it's a weekday or the weekend.</strong></h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faae1e3f7d1cb0019e3ae78?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Credit_Eric Rosen 2 Hikaru Nakamura\" height=\"2333\" width=\"3111\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Nakamura says his weekends and weekdays tend to blur together when he&#39;s playing online.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Eric Rosen</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Since I tend to stream six or even seven days of the week, it makes no difference to me. I try to take one day off a week and go hiking in Topanga National Park in California.</p><p>As of right now, there are no meet-and-greet with fans, although I hope to hold one after we get through this trying period of time. Still, I enjoy connecting with people when I'm streaming or through social media. I post about upcoming streams on Twitter or share shots on Instagram when I'm hiking.</p><p>My wildest esports experience was when I was the No. 1 most watched channel on the streaming platform Twitch, and I wasn't even playing. It was when I was a commentator on a match in May 2020 between XQC (Felix Lengyel) and the late Reckful (Byron Bernstein) who was a good friend of mine.</p><p>Since the pandemic, the popularity of chess esports has rocketed and this growing fan base on Twitch helps tremendously. I don't really use any mental tricks in terms of staying level headed before competitions, but I do find that knowing that I have such a large audience of fans who will support me whether I win or lose makes a world of difference.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-55-138_72f14aa7304aba59.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/r_gUu0ZJyCY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn59@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-53-871_65570f73bb3d1f49.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630688498},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"A ton of industries are selling things Gen Z doesn't care about, like alcohol, razorblades, and even cars","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/gen-z-could-end-many-industries-risk-razorblades-doorbells-cars-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2a97a402d49001924f204?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Gen Z\" height=\"1309\" width=\"1746\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">shaunl / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A Bank of America Research primer on Gen Z entitled \"OK Zoomer\" highlights the rising generation's new consumer spending habits &#8212; and lots of incumbent industries aren't popular.&#160;</li>\n<li>The report found that Gen Z, those born between the years 1996 and 2016, prioritizes sustainability, activism, and technology.&#160;</li>\n<li>With Gen Z expected to overtake millennials in global spending power by 2031, five major consumer products have been deemed at risk of missing the Gen Z spending train.&#160;</li>\n<li>Gen Z's spending habits will likely be most different for cars, razorblades, alcohol, golfing &#8212; and doorbells.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>If businesses thought <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/millennials-killing-industries-decade-wealth-2020-1\">millennials had a reputation for ruining things</a>, then they haven't seen Generation Z yet.&#160;</p><p>A new BofA Global Research primer on Gen Z entitled \"OK Zoomer\" revealed that the generation born between 1996 and 2016 could spell trouble for numerous industries, including automobiles, alcohol, and shopping malls. For the report, Bank of America polled over 14,500 people over the age of 16 in the US, UK, France, Japan, Germany, South Korea, China, India, Mexico, and Brazil. The poll was conducted via SurveyMonkey in August 2020.</p><p>The trouble has to do with Gen Z's values, which differ significantly from previous cohorts, with major implications for future spending. Sustainability, tech-savviness, and activism have taken hold, posing risks to lots of things the economy produces in huge quantities.&#160;</p><p>For example, BofA found that 31% of Gen Zers believe going into debt for a car is unnecessary, compared to about 25% of millennials. Furthermore, while 41% of millennials said they were thinking about buying a car next year, only 31% of 18-to-24-year-olds said the same thing.&#160;</p><p>BofA predicts Gen Z's global income will grow to $33 trillion in 2030, eventually surpassing that of millennials in 2031.&#160;</p><p>This economic spending power means Gen Zers have a sizeable influence over the industries they wish to invest in and keep around. Right now, those deemed safe include luxury, eCommerce, and big technology platforms. Keep scrolling to find out what's at risk of having its fate sealed by Generation Z.&#160;</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tCars\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5eadd4863dac9a7a257b2f83?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Parked cars.\" height=\"1413\" width=\"1884\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Parked cars.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Alan Schein Photography/Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>BofA found that although Gen Zers account for 14.8% of eligible drivers, only 11.7% of licensed drivers belong to the generation. Indeed, the number of teenagers obtaining driver's licenses is slowly falling, the report said, from 69.3% in 1978 to 51.7% in 2011.&#160;</p><p>Thirty-one percent of Gen Zers polled said they found car debt to be unnecessary, with 60% saying they didn't mind using shared mobility services.&#160;</p><p>Furthermore, 31% of Gen Zers said they were fine with the possibility of having a robot drive them, compared to just 13% of boomers. Interest in low-carbon transportation is also on the rise, BofA said.</p>\n\tShaving razors\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2ab09402d49001924f212?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Shaving\" height=\"2661\" width=\"3548\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Photo by Joel Sharpe /Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The report cites <a href=\"https://www.marketwatch.com/story/men-with-beards-are-killing-the-razor-industry-2019-08-01\">a comment made by the CFO of P&#38;G,</a> who said the US has seen an 11% decline in men's shaving products over the past five years, citing data from Euromonitor.</p><p>The US men's razor and blades market fell to $2.2 billion in 2018 from $2.4 billion in 2015, <a href=\"https://fingfx.thomsonreuters.com/gfx/editorcharts/PROCTERGAMBLE-RESULTS/0H001QEMC7LY/index.html\">Euromonitor found</a>.&#160;</p>\n\tAlcohol\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9adeb06f5b3100117242a6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"friends drinking\" height=\"1413\" width=\"1885\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Nikada/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Most Gen Zers of legal drinking age in their respective countries claim to not be drinking as much as previous generations, according to the BofA report.&#160;</p><p>Also, about half of legal Gen Z drinkers say they don't drink at all, compared with 31% of millennials. Only 21% of those between the ages of 18 and 24 say they drink more than once a week.&#160;</p><p>In the US, underage drinking has been on the decline, though it's declining slower for girls than for boys. The survey reported that between 2009 and 2019, underage drinking in boys between 12 and 20 fell from 28.5% to 17.2%, and from 25.8% to 19.9% for girls in the same age range.&#160;</p>\n\tGolfing\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ebbadd848d92c412078bcca?format=jpeg\" alt=\"UK lockdown sport golf\" height=\"800\" width=\"1067\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Alex Pantling/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Citing data from CB Insights and the National Golf Foundation, BofA reports that golf has struggled to attract Generation Z and that since the mid-1990s, the number of 18-to-35-year-olds who play golf fell from 9 million to 6 million. Since 2008, the game has lost nearly 5 million players overall.</p>\n\tDoorbells\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2ab33402d49001924f216?format=jpeg\" alt=\"GettyImages 1217632997\" height=\"3547\" width=\"4730\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">FilippoBacci / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Many Gen Zers and millennials would rather text someone that they are outside of their homes instead of ring a doorbell, BofA reported. The trend was previously reported <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/ask-not-for-whom-the-doorbell-tolls-they-wont-answer-it-1503864316\">in a 2017 Wall Street Journal article</a> in which one 20-year-old described doorbells as \"terrifying.\"&#160;</p><p>Jim Waterson, media editor at the Guardian, conducted a Twitter poll in 2017 which surveyed 11,502 people, 54.4% of which said that doorbells were \"<a href=\"https://twitter.com/jimwaterson/status/892678645243932672\">scary weird</a>.\" &#160;</p>\n</div><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 24@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-55-255_372fea5be77321cb.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630688551},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"Saving money might be hard, but it can kick off a lifetime of financial security and even long-term happiness","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/saving-cash-kicks-off-financial-security-happiness-2020-10","description":"<div class=\"content-header\"><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/master-your-money\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://media.tbistatic.com/bistudios/_00/dev_edit/mym/banner/MYM_banner.png?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Master your Money - presented by Fidelity Investments\" height=\"\" width=\"\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p></div><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9ad9d06f5b31001172427a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"millennials friends celebrating\" height=\"1398\" width=\"1865\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Saving money isn&#39;t always easy, but it&#39;s necessary.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Luis Alvarez/DigitalVision/Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Maintaining a savings account is the foundation for financial security.</li>\n<li>Without one, all it takes is one unplanned expense or unforeseen job loss to throw you off course.</li>\n<li>If your necessary expenses are covered and there's cash left over, saving it is the best option.</li>\n<li>Plus, research shows that financial security contributes greatly to happiness.</li>\n<li>This article is part of a series focused on millennial financial empowerment called <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/master-your-money\">Master your Money</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Uncertainty should be in the running for buzzword of 2020.</p><p>The pandemic hit Americans unexpectedly and hard, resulting in millions of job layoffs, an especially turbulent stock market, and more talk of \"stimulus\" than most of us had heard in a decade.</p><p>Now we're experiencing the beginning of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/k-shaped-economic-recovery-chart-low-wage-workers-pandemic-economy-2020-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">an economic recovery</a> that widens the gap between workers at the top and bottom of the pay scale.</p><p>According to Business Insider and Insider Intelligence's \"Master Your Money Invest &#38; Thrive Survey,\" which was conducted in July and sampled 2,020 millennials (defined as ages 21 to 38), nearly 20% of respondents said they didn't feel secure in their financial situation.</p><p>About 22% said they felt somewhat secure, 32% feel moderately secure, 17% feel very secure, and 10% feel extremely secure.</p><p>Perhaps the meaning of financial security has changed for you during this crisis, but one truth remains: If you can afford to, saving money is always a good idea.</p><h2><strong>Saving money isn't always easy, but it's necessary</strong></h2><p>The \"Invest &#38; Thrive\" survey also found that millennials often think they don't make enough money to save and, therefore, enough to invest. From a simple numbers perspective, you can afford to save money if your household's basic necessities — food, shelter, healthcare — are covered and there's money left over.</p><p>But it's worth noting even for people who have money left over, there are psychological factors at play too. Socking away money for an unknown crisis, instead of spending the cash on a dinner out with friends or flights to see family, might feel like too much of a sacrifice at the moment.&#160;</p><p>Plus, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/money-mistake-recover-financial-plan-2020-7\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">research shows</a> that many of us suffer from present bias, the tendency to overemphasize the importance of today's needs and wants and underemphasize events or expenses in the future.</p><p>Still, a cash reserve that's kept out of financial markets and easily accessible is the foundation on which financial security can exist. Without one, all it takes is one unplanned expense or job loss to throw you off course.</p><h2><strong>Financial security is built on savings, and even contributes to overall happiness</strong></h2><p>While an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/personal-finance/how-much-money-to-save-in-emergency-fund-rules\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">emergency fund</a> may not rescue you from every crisis — particularly if it lasts beyond the expert-recommend three to six months of cash savings — it is still your first line of defense.</p><p>When asked if they had an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/personal-finance/emergency-fund-more-important-than-ever-during-economic-crisis\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">emergency fund</a>, 57% of the millennial survey respondents said yes. Separately, when asked how much they were putting into a savings account each month, 25% said they didn't have a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/personal-finance/what-are-the-best-savings-accounts-right-now\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">savings account</a> and another 5% said they were not saving any money.</p><p>Yet everyone needs a bail-out fund. Not only does it protect your financial health, it improves your mental health too.</p><p>In <a href=\"https://www.theatlantic.com/health/archive/2017/10/get-rid-of-everything/543384/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">an interview with The Atlantic</a>, New York Times best-selling author and happiness researcher Dan Buettner said financial security \"really does deliver more happiness over time than most anything that money can be spent on — after your needs are taken care of and you maybe treat yourself occasionally.\"</p><p>In 2010, while promoting his book \"Thrive: Finding Happiness The Blue Zones Way,\" Buettner <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2010/11/28/131571885/how-to-thrive-dan-buettner-s-secrets-of-happiness\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">told NPR</a> that actions such as buying insurance and — yes — signing up for an automatic savings plan are hallmarks of financial security, which has \"three times greater impact on our happiness than just income alone.\"&#160;</p><p>And remember that no amount is too small when it comes to saving money. If you have to build your emergency fund $10 at a time, it's far better than nothing.&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a starting Tuesday with <a href=\"https://press.aboutamazon.com/news-releases/news-release-details/introducing-amazon-pharmacy-prescription-medications-delivered\">the launch of its Amazon Pharmacy service</a>.</p><p>Amazon said Prime members would be eligible for two-day delivery of medications and price cuts on both generic and brand-name drugs.</p><p>Amazon said Pharmacy customers could type their insurance information and select payment options in a \"pharmacy profile.\" Customers will be able to buy drugs through Amazon's main website.</p><p>Prime members can get discounts of up to 80% on generic drugs and 40% on brand-name medications when paying without insurance, Amazon said.</p><p>Amazon said it would also show comparisons to highlight whether it's cheaper for customers to pay through insurance or to rely on the company's discounts.</p><p>Patients can ask their doctors to send prescriptions straight to Amazon Pharmacy, Amazon said.</p><p>This is Amazon's latest push into healthcare. The company <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-pharmacy-pillpack-acquisition-merger-latest-push-into-healthcare-2018-6\">bought a small drug-delivery startup called PillPack</a> in 2018. In June 2019, Amazon <a href=\"https://www.investopedia.com/news/amazon-launches-its-own-line-overthecounter-drugs/\">launched a brand of over-the-counter medications</a>, and in August it <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-halo-app-wristband-launch-detect-mood-speech-body-fat-2020-8\">launched a health-monitoring wristband called Halo</a>.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazons-7-biggest-bets-in-healthcare-amazon-care-pillpack-halo-2020-11?r=ih-sub\">The 7 ways Amazon is building a healthcare empire, and why one analyst thinks doctors visits are next</a></em></p><p>\"As more and more people look to complete everyday errands from home, pharmacy is an important and needed addition to the Amazon online store,\" Doug Herrington, Amazon's senior vice president of North American consumer, said in a statement.</p><p>\"PillPack has provided exceptional pharmacy service for individuals with chronic health conditions for over six years.
