feed your dog, you probably head to the pantry and open up a bag of dry kibble or a can of wet food. While there are plenty of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-dog-food\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">high-quality commercial dog foods</a> on the market, this type of food has its limitations.</p><p>The process through which traditional dog food is made often strips away the original nutritional integrity, and most brands design their foods to provide for only the most basic nutritional needs of dogs in certain life stages and different breed sizes.</p><p>Each dog is unique, and so are their nutritional needs. Fresh dog food companies offer customized meals that cater to a dog's unique nutritional profile. That's what fresh food from <a href=\"https://thefarmersdog.otegtm.net/AerNj\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored\">The Farmer's Dog</a> has to offer.</p><p>When I opened my home to a new companion — a Cavalier King Charles Spaniel puppy I named Archie — I selected a popular dog food brand that offered a small-breed puppy formula and called it a day. Archie is the kind of dog that will eat anything that falls on the floor or anything I offer him by hand.</p><p>When it comes to eating from his own bowl, however, he can be a little picky. Most days he doesn't show any interest in his food until one of my cats tries to eat it. So, when I was given the opportunity to try <a href=\"https://thefarmersdog.otegtm.net/AerNj\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored\">The Farmer's Dog fresh food</a>, I was interested to see how he would like it.</p><p>Before I get into the details, I want to point out that The Farmer's Dog is not the only fresh food service available to dog owners. We've also tried products from <a href=\"http://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&u=1088116&m=75374&afftrack=biipf_011320_farmers-dog-review&urllink=www.petplate.com%2F.petplate.com%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow nofollow sponsored\">PetPlate</a> and <a href=\"https://olliepets.sjv.io/eoOKX\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Ollie</a>, so I'll be mentioning my experience with them as a point of comparison.</p><h2>How the signup process works</h2><p>The first step in testing <a href=\"https://thefarmersdog.otegtm.net/AerNj\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored\">The Farmer's Dog</a> food was to create an online profile for myself and Archie using the company website. The whole process took less than five minutes.</p><p>I plugged in basic information such as my name, email address, and zip code along with some facts about Archie including his sex, age, weight, and breed. From there, I was asked to evaluate his body composition, activity level, and eating preferences. After plugging in the necessary information, I learned that Archie needs roughly 460 calories per day.</p><p><a href=\"https://thefarmersdog.otegtm.net/AerNj\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5b1e96821ae66249008b4f26?format=jpeg\" alt=\"15390970_1173550359399937_7011280303773039205_n\" height=\"720\" width=\"960\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">The Farmer&#39;s Dog</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>After completing Archie's profile, I was given three formulas to choose from: turkey, beef, or pork. With my background in pet nutrition, I decided to steer clear of the beef option due to its risk for triggering food allergies and selected the turkey formula. In addition to turkey as the main ingredient, this recipe also included other nutritious ingredients like parsnips, chickpeas, carrots, broccoli, spinach, and fish oil. Each of the three recipes also includes something called \"Farmer's Dog Nutrient Blend\" to ensure balanced nutrition.</p><p>After placing my order, the product arrived quickly and in perfect condition. Packed with dry ice to keep the product frozen, the food was preportioned in bags that contained enough food for one day. All I had to do was thaw the first bag and put the rest in the freezer. The bags themselves were frozen flat so they took up minimal space in my already jam-packed freezer.</p><h2>What it's like to feed</h2><p>My shipment came with what looked like a takeout container with a plastic lid, so I was able to fold up the open food bag and place it in the container in the fridge until dinner time. I found it a little disappointing that the bags themselves were not resealable — I needed to cut them open with scissors.</p><p>Once the product thawed, I began incorporating it into Archie's diet. I followed the included instructions to mix some of the fresh food with his dry food, working up to feeding him half a bag twice a day. While I found the food bags easy to freeze, once they were open it was a little bit tricky to store them.</p><p>When I offered Archie his first bowl of The Farmer's Dog food, he was a little cautious. He spent a couple of seconds sniffing it with interest and then sampled a bite. He didn't act overly excited about the food, but he did seem to find it more appealing than his regular dry food alone. Over the next few days, as I phased out the kibble and began feeding him the fresh food only, he continued to enjoy it.</p><p>During the first few days of feeding Archie his new fresh food, he experienced some mild diarrhea. It isn't unusual for his stools to change a little in consistency from one day to the next (he likes to sneak mouthfuls of cat food whenever he can), so I wasn't worried.</p><h2>What makes it stand out</h2><p>After a few days of solely feeding Archie <a href=\"https://thefarmersdog.otegtm.net/AerNj\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored\">The Farmer's Dog</a> food, his bowel movements became more solid and regular. He also became a little more interested in eating at mealtime rather than ignoring the food for a couple of hours before eating it. Overall, I was very pleased with <a href=\"https://thefarmersdog.otegtm.net/AerNj\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored\">The Farmer's Dog</a> fresh food, and Archie seemed to like it as well.</p><p>There were three protein options to choose from (Pet Plate and Ollie currently offer four) and found the flat food bags easier to freeze and store than the larger containers Ollie food came in. The fact that each bag contained enough food for one day was also very convenient because it enabled me to keep the food as fresh as possible.</p><p>On the downside, I had to throw away several portions when Archie didn't eat them right away because my house doesn't have air conditioning, and I was worried about the food going bad. Also, while at first I didn't like the fact that the food bags were not resealable, I got used to using the storage container, and it didn't end up being a significant inconvenience.</p><h3><a href=\"https://thefarmersdog.otegtm.net/AerNj\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored\"><strong><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5b1fc0eb1ae66223008b4c3a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"1\" height=\"600\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">The Farmer&#39;s Dog</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></strong></a></h3><h2>The bottom line</h2><p>The fact of the matter is that fresh food will always be the best option for your dog when it comes to quality nutrition. You need to be careful when selecting a fresh food product, however, to ensure that your dog isn't allergic or sensitive to any of the ingredients and to make sure that the formula is backed by board-certified veterinary nutritionists.</p><p>If you can't afford the high price tag of fresh food from <a href=\"https://thefarmersdog.otegtm.net/AerNj\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored\">The Farmer's Dog</a>, you have the option of using the product as a food topper instead of your dog's sole source of nutrition. By mixing a little of the fresh food with their kibble you can boost their daily nutrition without draining your bank account.</p><p>If you want to improve your dog's nutrition (and their health by extension) and you're considering fresh food, we wholeheartedly recommend <a href=\"https://thefarmersdog.otegtm.net/AerNj\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored\">The Farmer's Dog</a>.</p><p><strong>Pros: </strong>Fresh food customized to your dog, unprocessed ingredients; recipes by board-certified veterinary nutritionists comply with AAFCO standards; cooked in human-grade kitchens; convenient shipping; packaged as daily portions</p><p><strong>Cons:&#160;</strong> Limited protein options, especially for dogs with food allergies or sensitivities; bags are not resealable; may cause&#160;digestive upset during the transition from dry food to fresh food; fresh food may go bad if not eaten immediately, expensive</p><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Jobs in healthcare, medical research, and hospitals have been especially important amid the pandemic. Workers in these jobs have been treating patients as <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-1-million-daily-coronavirus-cases-end-of-2020-report-2020-11\">cases continue to rise</a>, working on a vaccine, and researching the novel coronavirus.&#160;&#160;</p><p>The outbreak has had an effect on almost everyone's daily life in some way, such as schools and businesses closing down to stem the spread. Hospital staff in particular are confronting the virus every day and putting their own health <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-jobs-most-at-risk-to-a-coronavirus-outbreak\">at risk</a> to help test or treat those infected by coronavirus. The US has had over 11 million cases per <a href=\"https://coronavirus.jhu.edu/map.html\">John Hopkins' coronavirus tracker</a>, and some states are<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/states-restrictions-surging-coronavirus-cases-2020-11\"> adding stricter rules</a> as cases continue to surge right before Thanksgiving. There were over 166,000 cases recorded on November 16, according to the tracker.</p><p>Additionally, there has been recent progress in developing a vaccine against COVID-19. The pharmaceutical company Pfizer and its partner BioNTech has reported that their experimental vaccine is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-coronavirus-vaccine-success-plans-for-emergency-approval-fda-2020-9\">more than 90% effective</a> in preventing COVID-19. The biotech firm Moderna has also reported that its experimental <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-works-to-prevent-covid-19-company-says-2020-11\">vaccine is 94.5% effective</a>.</p><p>According to <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2019-07-16/which-u-s-jobs-pay-the-most-top-ten-professions-by-salary\">a Bloomberg report</a> from last year citing data from the <a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/iag/tgs/iag622.htm\">US Bureau of Labor Statistics</a>, four out of the top five highest-paid jobs in the US are in the medical field, with physicians, surgeons, and general practitioners reporting salaries over $200,000.</p><p>We decided to look at how their coworkers fare in hospitals based on the latest <a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/oes/current/oessrci.htm\">industry-specific data from May 2019</a>.</p><p>Business Insider took a look at typical salaries in 30 selected hospitals jobs with various job duties. Hospitals are a major part of the giant US healthcare industry, with spending on the sector as a whole set to reach nearly 20% of the US economy.</p><p>Hospitals have long been a big employer. <a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/iag/tgs/iag622.htm\">BLS</a> figures indicate that hospitals employ around 5.15 million Americans, according to the most recent data in October.</p><p>People who work in hospitals perform a wide range of jobs, including nurses who take care of patients, lab technologists who run complicated tests to detect disease, and radiology technicians who manage the scans that can help diagnose patients.</p><p>Those skilled occupations could explain why <a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/opub/mlr/2018/article/healthcare-jobs-and-the-great-recession.htm\">hospital workers tend to make more</a> than the average healthcare worker. The average hospital worker made over $34 an hour and worked just over 37 hours a week on average, according to<a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/iag/tgs/iag622.htm\">&#160;government data</a> from September 2020.</p><p>There are about 6,146 hospitals across the US today, according to industry group the <a href=\"https://www.aha.org/statistics/fast-facts-us-hospitals\">American Hospital Association</a>, ranging from nonprofit community ones to for-profit hospitals and hospitals run by state and local governments or the federal government.</p><p>Here are some of the more prominent occupations at hospitals, and how much they make as of May 2019, ranked by their annual average salaries. We also included each job's description as defined by <a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/\">O*NET</a>.</p><p><em>A previous version of this article used May 2018 data and noted that figures were median annual earnings, but these figures were average annual earnings.</em></p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\t30. Janitors and cleaners, except maids and housekeeping cleaners, earn an average of $30,690 a year, and there are 77,890 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ceffa5711e20545301aec43?format=jpeg\" alt=\"hospital janitor maid\" height=\"1414\" width=\"1885\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">ER Productions Limited/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/37-2011.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Keep buildings in clean and orderly condition. Perform heavy cleaning duties, such as cleaning floors, shampooing rugs, washing walls and glass, and removing rubbish. Duties may include tending furnace and boiler, performing routine maintenance activities, notifying management of need for repairs, and cleaning snow or debris from sidewalk.</p>\n\t29. Orderlies earn an average of $30,740 a year, and there are 38,690 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/57ae2a25db5ce9b2008b688c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"orderly nurse gurney stretcher hospital\" height=\"667\" width=\"889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://www.shutterstock.com/pic-156022646/stock-photo-male-nurse-pushing-stretcher-gurney-bed-in-hospital-corridor-with-doctors-and-senior-female-patient.html?src=ZGHzdP3D0qGw2sZUOr3TFQ-1-28\" target=\"_blank\">Spotmatik Ltd/Shutterstock</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/31-1132.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Transport patients to areas such as operating rooms or X-ray rooms using wheelchairs, stretchers, or moveable beds. May maintain stocks of supplies or clean and transport equipment.</p>\n\t28. Nursing assistants earn an average of $32,550 a year, and there are 406,350 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ceda13511e2050d452f0aa7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"nurse\" height=\"3623\" width=\"4830\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/31-1131.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Provide basic patient care under direction of nursing staff. Perform duties such as feed, bathe, dress, groom, or move patients, or change linens. May transfer or transport patients. Includes nursing care attendants, nursing aides, and nursing attendants.</p>\n\t27. Cooks (institution and cafeteria) earn an average of $32,990 a year, and there are 34,700 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ceff97e11e205438b5fd4f2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"hospital kitchen\" height=\"1414\" width=\"1885\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jasmin Merdan/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/35-2012.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Prepare and cook large quantities of food for institutions, such as schools, hospitals, or cafeterias; clean and inspect galley equipment, kitchen appliances, and work areas to ensure cleanliness and functional operation.</p>\n\t26. Phlebotomists earn an average of $35,300 a year, and there are 48,820 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5b15762c1ae6624f008b4867?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Phlebotomist\" height=\"1477\" width=\"1970\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tim Boyle/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/31-9097.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Draw blood for tests, transfusions, donations, or research. May explain the procedure to patients and assist in the recovery of patients with adverse reactions.</p>\n\t25. Security guards earn an average of $37,880 a year, and there are 43,640 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ceff94911e2054b4e7675c8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"hospital security\" height=\"1414\" width=\"1885\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">ER Productions Limited/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/33-9032.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Guard, patrol, or monitor premises to prevent theft, violence, or infractions of rules. May operate X-ray and metal detector equipment.</p>\n\t24. Emergency medical technicians and paramedics earn an average of $39,760 a year, and there are 48,680 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5a4bdb30cf698a23008b4590?format=jpeg\" alt=\"emergency medical technicians emt paramedics\" height=\"708\" width=\"944\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Joerg Koch / Stringer / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-2042.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Assess injuries, administer emergency medical care, and extricate trapped individuals. Transport injured or sick persons to medical facilities.</p>\n\t23. Pharmacy technicians earn an average of $40,000 a year, and there are 69,270 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5b0414a14c9ab9861c8b4743?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Pharmacy technician prescriptions\" height=\"1334\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A technician stocks the shelves of the pharmacy at White House Clinic in Berea, Kentucky, U.S., February 7, 2018.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-2052.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Prepare medications under the direction of a pharmacist. May measure, mix, count out, label, and record amounts and dosages of medications according to prescription orders.</p>\n\t22. Medical dosimetrists, medical records specialists, and health technologists and technicians (all other) earn an average of $49,330 a year, and there are 122,000 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ceff86a11e20551d877d415?format=jpeg\" alt=\"medical records technician\" height=\"2720\" width=\"3626\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">BSIP/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-2072.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Compile, process, and maintain medical records of hospital and clinic patients in a manner consistent with medical, administrative, ethical, legal, and regulatory requirements of the health care system.&#160;</p>\n\t21. Surgical technologists earn an average of $49,810 a year, and there are 79,720 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5c5caaf9d7ab6725fd5f52a6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"surgical technician\" height=\"2003\" width=\"2671\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">BSIP/UIG via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-2055.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Assist in operations, under the supervision of surgeons, registered nurses, or other surgical personnel. May help set up operating room, prepare and transport patients for surgery, adjust lights and equipment, pass instruments and other supplies to surgeons and surgeon's assistants, hold retractors, cut sutures, and help count sponges, needles, supplies, and instruments.</p>\n\t20. Clinical laboratory technologists and technicians earn an average of $56,840 a year, and there are 159,580 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ceff77c11e20539d2052a46?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Clinical laboratory technologist\" height=\"1840\" width=\"2453\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Andy Cross/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-2011.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Perform complex medical laboratory tests for diagnosis, treatment, and prevention of disease. May train or supervise staff. Operate, calibrate, or maintain equipment used in quantitative or qualitative analysis, such as spectrophotometers, calorimeters, flame photometers, or computer-controlled analyzers.</p>\n\t19. Dietitians and nutritionists earn an average of $63,450 a year, and there are 21,920 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e73843fc485406897530644?format=jpeg\" alt=\"hospital fruit dietitian\" height=\"1334\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Robert Kneschke / EyeEm/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-1031.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Plan and conduct food service or nutritional programs to assist in the promotion of health and control of disease. May supervise activities of a department providing quantity food services, counsel individuals, or conduct nutritional research.</p>\n\t18. Radiologic technologists and technicians earn an average of $63,980 a year, and there are 125,310 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cb4f9f6aefeef25ca6d4485?format=jpeg\" alt=\"radiologic technologist\" height=\"3019\" width=\"4025\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Associated Press</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-2034.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Take X-rays and CAT scans or administer nonradioactive materials into patient's blood stream for diagnostic purposes. Includes technologists who specialize in other scanning modalities.</p>\n\t17. Public relations specialists earn an average of $64,370 a year, and there are 4,800 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ceff7f311e2053e41152b19?format=jpeg\" alt=\"hospital public relations pr\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2667\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mike Windle/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/27-3031.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Engage in promoting or creating an intended public image for individuals, groups, or organizations. May write or select material for release to various communications media.</p>\n\t16. Healthcare social workers earn an average of $65,600 a year, and there are 50,430 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5810ff4db28a647b548b4ab4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Healthcare social worker elderly patient care\" height=\"662\" width=\"883\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://www.shutterstock.com/pic-162942518/stock-photo-social-worker-visit-sick-old-male-patient-in-hospital.html?src=3fZOul8cai65IGwcnPfQVg-1-3\" target=\"_blank\">Shutterstock/ChameleonsEye</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/21-1022.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Provide individuals, families, and groups with the psychosocial support needed to cope with chronic, acute, or terminal illnesses. Services include advising family care givers, providing patient education and counseling, and making referrals for other services. May also provide care and case management or interventions designed to promote health, prevent disease, and address barriers to access to healthcare.</p>\n\t15. Registered nurses earn an average of $79,400 a year, and there are 1,816,170 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ceda07911e205107216e732?format=jpeg\" alt=\"nurses\" height=\"3648\" width=\"4864\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-1141.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Assess patient health problems and needs, develop and implement nursing care plans, and maintain medical records. Administer nursing care to ill, injured, convalescent, or disabled patients. May advise patients on health maintenance and disease prevention or provide case management. Licensing or registration required.</p>\n\t14. Nuclear medicine technologists earn an average of $79,920 a year, and there are 13,230 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d5d8702f02ef801a1189328?format=jpeg\" alt=\"nuclear medicine\" height=\"2833\" width=\"3778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Sergei Bobylev / Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-2033.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Prepare, administer, and measure radioactive isotopes in therapeutic, diagnostic, and tracer studies using a variety of radioisotope equipment. Prepare stock solutions of radioactive materials and calculate doses to be administered by radiologists. Subject patients to radiation. Execute blood volume, red cell survival, and fat absorption studies following standard laboratory techniques.</p>\n\t13. Physical therapists earn an average of $91,250 a year, and there are 64,840 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cb4f934aefeef2815171ec2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"physical therapist assistant\" height=\"1238\" width=\"1651\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Associated Press</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-1123.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Assess, plan, organize, and participate in rehabilitative programs that improve mobility, relieve pain, increase strength, and improve or correct disabling conditions resulting from disease or injury.</p>\n\t12. Physician assistants earn an average of $113,420 a year, and there are 31,300 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/560331f19dd7cc14008bca7a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Physician Assistant\" height=\"1591\" width=\"2121\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/dominique-entzminger-a-physician-assistant-of-family-news-photo/57260746\" target=\"_blank\">Joe Raedle / Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-1071.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Provide healthcare services typically performed by a physician, under the supervision of a physician. Conduct complete physicals, provide treatment, and counsel patients. May, in some cases, prescribe medication. Must graduate from an accredited educational program for physician assistants.</p>\n\t11. Nurse practitioners earn an average of $115,770 a year, and there are 51,120 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5de56584fd9db2616c68fe46?format=jpeg\" alt=\"missouri nurse practitioner\" height=\"1319\" width=\"1759\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Dan Gill</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-1171.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Diagnose and treat acute, episodic, or chronic illness, independently or as part of a healthcare team. May focus on health promotion and disease prevention. May order, perform, or interpret diagnostic tests such as lab work and X-rays. May prescribe medication. Must be registered nurses who have specialized graduate education.</p>\n\t10. Medical and health-services managers earn an average of $123,930 a year, and there are 136,030 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ceff6fe11e20544166906c6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"health service manager medical\" height=\"1188\" width=\"1584\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">sturti/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/11-9111.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Plan, direct, or coordinate medical and health services in hospitals, clinics, managed care organizations, public health agencies, or similar organizations.</p>\n\t9. Pharmacists earn an average of $127,210 a year, and there are 82,050 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5b58c5f9e199f327008b4595?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Walgreens pharmacy pharmacist\" height=\"2333\" width=\"3111\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A pharmacist works at an internal pharmacy run by Walgreens at a Cisco health clinic at Cisco Systems in San Jose, California, U.S., March 22, 2018\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters/Elijah Nouvelage</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-1051.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Dispense drugs prescribed by physicians and other health practitioners and provide information to patients about medications and their use. May advise physicians and other health practitioners on the selection, dosage, interactions, and side effects of medications.</p>\n\t8. Financial managers earn an average of $147,330 a year, and there are 10,160 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ceff64b11e20551024b50b5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"hospital administrator cfo\" height=\"1020\" width=\"1360\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tom Werner/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/11-3031.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Plan, direct, or coordinate accounting, investing, banking, insurance, securities, and other financial activities of a branch, office, or department of an establishment.</p>\n\t7. General internal medicine physicians earn an average of $172,210 a year, and there are 12,910 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5a2eff270b0f2720008b467a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"internist doctor physician\" height=\"1271\" width=\"1695\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Rick Bowmer/AP Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-1216.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Physicians who diagnose and provide non-surgical treatment of diseases and injuries of internal organ systems. Provide care mainly for adults who have a wide range of problems associated with the internal organs.</p>\n\t6. Nurse anesthetists earn an average of $193,090 a year, and there are 14,880 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5602bfec9dd7cc15008bc7fc?format=jpeg\" alt=\"anesthesiologist\" height=\"667\" width=\"889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://www.shutterstock.com/cat.mhtml?lang=en&#38;language=en&#38;ref_site=photo&#38;search_source=search_form&#38;version=llv1&#38;anyorall=all&#38;safesearch=1&#38;use_local_boost=1&#38;autocomplete_id=&#38;searchterm=ANESTHESIOLOGIST&#38;show_color_wheel=1&#38;orient=&#38;commercial_ok=&#38;media_type=images&#38;search_cat=&#38;searchtermx=&#38;photographer_name=&#38;people_gender=&#38;people_age=&#38;people_ethnicity=&#38;people_number=&#38;color=&#38;page=1&#38;inline=317874593\" target=\"_blank\">ChaNaWiT/Shutterstock</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-1151.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Administer anesthesia, monitor patients' vital signs, and oversee patient recovery from anesthesia. May assist anesthesiologists, surgeons, other physicians, or dentists. Must be registered nurses who have specialized graduate education.</p>\n\t5. Family medicine physicians earn an average of $204,700 a year, and there are 20,490 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/57c0a50a09d293c4058b4c3b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"doctor patient\" height=\"2334\" width=\"3112\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jim Bourg/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-1215.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Physicians who diagnose, treat, and help prevent diseases and injuries that commonly occur in the general population. May refer patients to specialists when needed for further diagnosis or treatment.</p>\n\t4. Obstetricians and gynecologists earn an average of $209,930 a year, and there are 3,870 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5a2efd0e8229f21e008b4677?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Obstetrician gynecologist\" height=\"1232\" width=\"1643\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Orlin Wagner/AP Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-1218.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Physicians who provide medical care related to pregnancy or childbirth and those who diagnose, treat, and help prevent diseases of women, particularly those affecting the reproductive system.&#160;</p>\n\t3. Anesthesiologists earn an average of $210,570 a year, and there are 4,160 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ccb3b01021b4c2461706414?format=jpeg\" alt=\"anesthesiologist doctor patient\" height=\"1004\" width=\"1339\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Carlos Osorio/AP Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-1211.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Physicians who administer anesthetics prior to, during, or after surgery or other medical procedures.</p>\n\t2. Chief executives earn a median of $216,300 a year, and there are 5,260 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ceff4d311e2053de648d3c7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Richard J. Murphy, CEO of South Nassau Communities Hospital.\" height=\"2555\" width=\"3407\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Richard J. Murphy, CEO of South Nassau Communities Hospital.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Newsday LLC/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/11-1011.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Determine and formulate policies and provide overall direction of companies or private and public sector organizations within guidelines set up by a board of directors or similar governing body. Plan, direct, or coordinate operational activities at the highest level of management with the help of subordinate executives and staff managers.</p>\n\t1. Surgeons earn a median of $221,690 a year, and there are 8,460 employed in hospitals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e5ff6b8fee23d61347ebe42?format=jpeg\" alt=\"surgeons\" height=\"905\" width=\"1206\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">sheff/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>What they do,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.onetonline.org/link/summary/29-1067.00\">according to O*NET</a>: </strong>Physicians who treat diseases, injuries, and deformities by invasive, minimally invasive, or noninvasive surgical methods, such as using instruments, appliances, or by manual manipulation.</p>\n</div><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a If you're shopping for Christmas presents, Cyber Monday may be one of the final deal opportunities this year.&#160;</p><p>Below, you'll find answers to the web's most frequently asked questions regarding Cyber Monday, Cyber Week, Amazon, and the rest of the sales happening this month.&#160;</p><bi-shortcode id=\"table-of-contents-sticky\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-type=\"h2\">Table of Contents: Masthead Sticky</bi-shortcode><h2>When does Amazon's Cyber Monday sale start?&#160;</h2><p>Cyber Monday happens every year following the weekend after <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/black-friday-deals\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"6f373ef450cf753e61e0b3aa31ed093d\">Black Friday</a>. This year, the online-focused shopping holiday lands on Monday, November 30. Cyber Monday sales can start as early as Saturday morning after Black Friday.&#160;</p><p>This year, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-black-friday-deals\">Amazon's Black Friday sale</a> officially starts Friday, November 20 with new discounts released every day. However, many sales that happen during Black Friday will likely carry over through Saturday and Sunday.&#160;&#160;</p><p>We expect some \"doorbusters\" to be released on Cyber Monday, with limited supplies.&#160;Though Cyber Monday sales once only took place on Monday, we'll likely see some deals last through the rest of the week.&#160;</p><h2>Are there any early deals?&#160;</h2><p>Before Cyber Monday and Black Friday, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-holiday-dash-sale-2020\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Amazon's Holiday Dash sales event</a> offers fresh deals every day through November 19 then followed closely by Amazon's pre-Black Friday sale which will last through November 27.</p><p>During these sales events, shoppers can find daily markdowns on electronics, home goods, fashion, and more. We expect each Amazon and its competition to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stores-that-price-match\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">price-match each other</a> during Cyber Monday.&#160; Shoppers can expect big savings on digital content, streaming media players, smart home products, and more.&#160;</p><p>In fact, there's a good chance we can see a repeat of what we saw during <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-prime-day-best-deals\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Prime Day</a>. We expect to see several Amazon-branded goods and Echo devices see lows similar to those found last month.&#160;</p><p>During Cyber Monday, shoppers should pay attention to two types of deals: daily deals and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-prime-day-lightning-deals-2020\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"27d5cc920c2bfffa9c7d4bdc485de798\">Lightning deals</a>. The former are one-day offers, usually grouped by brand or category, and change at the end of the day. The latter are limited-stock offers released throughout the day. We expect to see the best deals to come in the Lightning deal form.&#160;</p><h2>Should I get Amazon Prime?</h2><p>Amazon Prime subscribers will get the most out of Amazon's Cyber Monday. We've found that shoppers can make up the cost of the subscription with their savings from shipping alone. but said \"that's not anti-business.\"</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>President-elect Joe Biden and Vice President-elect Kamala Harris spoke with labor leaders and top CEOs on Monday during a conference call on the economy, <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-biden-economy/biden-meets-with-tech-retail-auto-ceos-labor-leaders-idUSKBN27W27V\">a transition aide told Reuters</a>.</p><p>The CEOs represented a range of industries including tech, retail, and automobile manufacturing.</p><p>General Motors' CEO Mary Barra, Microsoft's CEO Satya Nadella, Target's CEO Brian Cornell, and Gap's CEO Sonia Syngal all took part in the call, the aide told Reuters.</p><p>The meeting signaled that the CEOs and labor leaders accept Biden as president-elect, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-struggles-walk-back-tweet-admititng-biden-won-2020-11\">despite President Donald Trump's refusal to concede</a>.</p><p>Union presidents also attended. These included American Federation of Labor and Congress of Industrial Organizations (AFL-CIO) president Richard Trumka, as well as the heads of the Service Employees International Union, the United Auto Workers, the United Food and Commercial Workers, and the American Federation of State, County, and Municipal Employees, sources told <a href=\"https://www.foxbusiness.com/business-leaders/target-microsoft-gm-ceos-to-meet-with-biden-harris\">Fox Business</a>.</p><p>During the call, Biden discussed his plans for economic recovery from the pandemic — and also called himself a \"union guy.\"</p><p>\"Unions are going to have increased power,\" <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/11/16/biden-holds-joint-meeting-with-union-leaders-and-retail-auto-tech-ceos.html\">Biden told attendees.</a></p><p>He clarified \"that's not anti-business.\"</p><p>Biden also joked that he should be given \"a Nobel Prize\" for bringing union leaders and CEOs together for the call.</p><p>AFL-CIO President Trumka <a href=\"https://aflcio.org/speeches/trumka-federal-government-must-act-protect-workers\">told Biden and Harris</a> what the government and companies need to do to ensure workers stay safe during the pandemic.</p><p>The US needs to manufacture more personal protective equipment, invest in retrofitting workplaces to meet ventilation and distancing requirements, and ensure all COVID-19 cases are counted and reported, he said.</p><p>The \"most important thing\" is reestablishing the mission of the Occupational Safety and Health Administration (OSHA) to focus on protecting workers, Trumka told Biden and Harris. There are fewer inspectors now than at any point in the agency's history, he added.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-cabinet-women-warren-rice-duckworth-2020-11?r=gd-sub\">Joe Biden has an extensive selection of women to pick from, thanks to his VP vettings. Here's who could make it into his Cabinet.</a></em></p><p>Target CEO Brian Cornell planned to discuss the importance of retail during the pandemic and ask for clear guidance for companies on COVID-19 safety measures, the company <a href=\"https://www.foxbusiness.com/business-leaders/target-microsoft-gm-ceos-to-meet-with-biden-harris\">told Fox Business.</a></p><p>\"We know that the coronavirus has been challenging for American families this year and appreciate the opportunity to educate and advise on this critically important topic,\" a spokesman said.</p><p>Americans <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-retail-sales-miss-october-estimates-economic-recovery-slows-coronavirus-2020-11\">spent less at retailers than expected</a> in October as the economic recovery decelerated amid a worsening pandemic.</p><p>After the coronavirus pandemic drove a record plunge in economic output in the second quarter, the US's summer recovery fueled the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-q3-gdp-record-growth-economic-reopening-recession-coronavirus-pandemic-2020-10\">largest-ever jump in gross domestic product in the third quarter</a>.</p><p>On November 6,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-concede-biden-meeting-ceo-electoral-college-presidential-election-2020-11\">more than 24 CEOs of top US firms met Goldman Sachs recommends buying so-called deep value stocks ahead of any subsequent positive developments.</p><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-strategy-stock-market-2021-outlook-covid-vaccine-goldman-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Click here for more details</a></h3><hr><h2>Quote of the week</h2><p><em>\"Many of the stocks trading with the lowest valuations today are those with business models most directly harmed by the pandemic and its impact on economic activity. 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"The rise of Airbnb CEO Brian Chesky, who got his start renting out air mattresses on his floor and is now headed toward a highly anticipated IPO","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-ceo-brian-chesky-30-billion-startup-2016-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d83cb652e22af357c306b32?format=jpeg\" alt=\"brian chesky\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Airbnb CEO Brian Chesky.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mike Windle/Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Brian Chesky didn't take a traditional route into the tech world: he's a former hockey player who studied industrial design in college.</li>\n<li>He and cofounder Joe Gebbia had the idea for Airbnb in 2007: When a design conference came to town and all the hotels were booked up, they decided to rent out their apartment for those who needed a place to stay.</li>\n<li>Airbnb, then called Airbedandbreakfast.com, officially launched in August 2008. Now, 12 years later,&#160;Airbnb is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-files-s1-public-ipo-paperwork-revenue-losses-covid-19-2020-11\">headed toward an initial public offering</a>.&#160;</li>\n<li>Chesky, Airbnb's CEO, is worth <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/profile/brian-chesky/?sh=723cbddb44d3\">an estimated $3.1 billion</a> these days.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Brian Chesky didn't know much about tech before starting Airbnb.</p><p>The now 39-year-old CEO majored in industrial design in college, and dabbled in hockey and bodybuilding in his 20s. But now, he's grown an idea that stemmed from overbooked hotels into a multi-billion-dollar startup, and has become one of Silicon Valley's key players.</p><p>On Monday, Airbnb <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-files-s1-public-ipo-paperwork-revenue-losses-covid-19-2020-11\">publicly revealed its paperwork for an initial public offering</a>, slated to be one of the most highly anticipated IPOs of the year.&#160;</p><p>Here's how the Brian Chesky, an upstate New York native, became one of the richest young tech founders in America.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tChesky grew up in Niskayuna, New York, north of Albany. He was into hockey, and he also liked to draw and design new versions Nike sneakers, which turned into an interest in art.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/57b1c180ce38f222008b69c2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Niskayna NY\" height=\"2293\" width=\"3057\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Niskayuna, New York.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mike Groll/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://fortune.com/longform/brian-chesky-airbnb/\">Fortune</a></em></p>\n\tChesky's high school yearbook quote was \"I'm sure I'll amount to nothing.\" He thought it was funny — his dad didn't.\n\t\n\t<blockquote class=\"instagram-media\" data-instgrm-captioned  style=\"background:#FFF; border:0; border-radius:3px; box-shadow:0 0 1px 0 rgba(0,0,0,0.5),0 1px 10px 0 rgba(0,0,0,0.15); margin: 1px; max-width:540; padding:0; width:99.375%; width:-webkit-calc(100% - 2px); width:calc(100% - 2px); data.width~540;\">\n\t<div style=\"padding:8px;\">\n\t\t<div style=\"background:#F8F8F8; line-height:0; margin-top:40px; padding:62.4537037037% 0; text-align:center; width:100%;\">\n\t\t\t<div style=\"background:url(data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAACwAAAAsCAMAAAApWqozAAAABGdBTUEAALGPC/xhBQAAAAFzUkdCAK7OHOkAAAAMUExURczMzPf399fX1+bm5mzY9AMAAADiSURBVDjLvZXbEsMgCES5/P8/t9FuRVCRmU73JWlzosgSIIZURCjo/ad+EQJJB4Hv8BFt+IDpQoCx1wjOSBFhh2XssxEIYn3ulI/6MNReE07UIWJEv8UEOWDS88LY97kqyTliJKKtuYBbruAyVh5wOHiXmpi5we58Ek028czwyuQdLKPG1Bkb4NnM+VeAnfHqn1k4+GPT6uGQcvu2h2OVuIf/gWUFyy8OWEpdyZSa3aVCqpVoVvzZZ2VTnn2wU8qzVjDDetO90GSy9mVLqtgYSy231MxrY6I2gGqjrTY0L8fxCxfCBbhWrsYYAAAAAElFTkSuQmCC); He saw this and yelled, \"Nothing?! Nothing?!\" I thought it was funny... he didn't. Now, off to Rhode Island School of Design. ✈️ 🎓See you soon Dad! #RISD</a></p> <p style=\" color:#c9c8cd; font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; line-height:17px; margin-bottom:0; margin-top:8px; overflow:hidden; padding:8px 0 7px; text-align:center; text-overflow:ellipsis; white-space:nowrap;\">A post shared by  Brian Chesky (@bchesky) on May 31, 2017 at 11:06am PDT<time style=\" font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; line-height:17px;\" datetime=\"2017-05-31T18:06:25+00:00\">May 31, 2017 at 11:06am PDT</time>\n\t\t</p></div></blockquote><script async defer src=\"//platform.instagram.com/en_US/embeds.js\"></script><p>\"Earlier this year, he was happy to find out I'd be speaking at both my high school and college as the commencement speaker,\" Chesky&#160;<a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/BUxCO3Qj5yf/?taken-by=bchesky&#38;hl=en\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">wrote on Instagram</a> in 2017. \"See you soon Dad!\"</p><p>&#160;</p>\n\tIn 1999, Chesky attended Rhode Island School of Design, where he served as captain of the hockey team and studied industrial design.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/57b1c1bbce38f238008b6b12?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Rhode Island School of Design campus\" height=\"2003\" width=\"2671\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Rhode Island School of Design.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Gretchen Ertl/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://fortune.com/longform/brian-chesky-airbnb/\">Fortune</a></em></p>\n\tAt RISD, Chesky met Joe Gebbia, with whom he would eventually cofound Airbnb. Right before graduation, Gebbia reportedly pulled Chesky aside and said: \"Before you get on the plane, there's something I need to tell you. We're going to start a company one day, and they're going to write a book about it.\"\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/57b1ef4dce38f238008b6c6b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"JoeGebbiaAirbnb\" height=\"3174\" width=\"4233\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Airbnb cofounder Joe Gebbia.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Airbnb</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://fortune.com/longform/brian-chesky-airbnb/\">Fortune</a></em></p>\n\tIn his early 20s, Chesky was a competitive bodybuilder. He was described in a 2014 profile as still having \"16-inch biceps.\"\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/57b1d07ddb5ce9b61b8b69e8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"brian chesky airbnb\" height=\"2211\" width=\"2948\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Brian Chesky, on the left.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kevork Djansezian/Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>In a 2014 <a href=\"http://www.fastcompany.com/3027107/punk-meet-rock-airbnb-brian-chesky-chip-conley\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Fast Company profile</a>, Chesky is described as an imposing figure: \"A former hockey player and bodybuilder with 16-inch biceps, the CEO commands attention. His boomerang grin and slant nose work to sharply focus his attention on you. Rather than turn his head toward me, he physically picks up his chair and pivots it directly so we're eye to eye.\"</p>\n\tAfter graduating from RISD, Chesky moved to Los Angeles to work as an industrial designer, for which he made $40,000 a year.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb3d52c15164e2d394668ed?format=jpeg\" alt=\"los angeles\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2667\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Los Angeles, California.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/profile/brian-chesky/?list=rtb/#28e717b144d3\">Forbes</a></em></p>\n\tBut shortly thereafter, he moved to San Francisco and in with Gebbia. The two unemployed grads soon ran out of cash. When a design conference came to town in October 2007 and caused all the hotels to sell out, Gebbia pitched Chesky the idea of renting out their space to those who couldn't find a place to stay — a \"designers bed and breakfast.\"\n\t\n\t<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Bill Gross  (@Bill_Gross) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/699646672125558784\">February 16, 2016</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://fortune.com/longform/brian-chesky-airbnb/\">Fortune</a></em></p><p><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></p>\n\tThe roommates ended up housing three people that weekend, offering up air mattresses and floor space, as well as Pop-Tarts for breakfast.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d83a9892e22af30e275f1f4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Brian Chesky\" height=\"2521\" width=\"3361\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mike Segar/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://fortune.com/longform/brian-chesky-airbnb/\">Fortune</a></em></p>\n\tA few months later, Gebbia and Chesky were joined by their engineer friend, Nathan Blecharczyk. Together, the three guys started what was at the time called Airbedandbreakfast.com in August 2008. Chesky \"gravitated naturally to the role of leader,\" Fortune wrote in 2015.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/57b1c6e6db5ce92c168b6a3b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Nathan Blecharczyk, Brian Chesky, Joe Gebbia, airbnb, sv100 2015\" height=\"1037\" width=\"1382\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>From left: Airbnb cofounders Joe Gebbia, Nathan Blecharczyk, and Brian Chesky.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.airbnb.com/press/resources\" target=\"_blank\">Airbnb</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://fortune.com/longform/brian-chesky-airbnb/\">Fortune</a></em></p>\n\tSince then, Airbnb has not only shortened its name, but has listings in more than 191 countries worldwide. The company has served an estimated 800 million guests since its 2008 launch. Airbnb was last valued at $18 billion, making it one of the most valuable startups in the US.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5669fd2472f2c14d028b4c1f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Airbnb employees\" height=\"750\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.glassdoor.com/Photos/Airbnb-Office-Photos-E391850.htm\" target=\"_blank\">Glassdoor/Airbnb</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://press.airbnb.com/fast-facts/\">Airbnb</a>, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-files-s1-public-ipo-paperwork-revenue-losses-covid-19-2020-11\">Business Insider</a></em></p>\n\tNow 39, Chesky's net worth stands at $3.1 billion. It's unclear how much of a stake Chesky owns in Airbnb, but it's estimated at just under 15%.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/57b1cba5db5ce950008b6b6b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"brian chesky\" height=\"1630\" width=\"2173\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Chris Weeks/Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/alexkonrad/2014/03/20/airbnb-cofounders-are-billionaires/#73799fc73e1c\">Forbes</a></em></p>\n\tIn 2015, Chesky was named to the Time 100 as one of the most influential people alive. Apple's former design chief, Jony Ive, wrote at the time that Chesky's \"audacity is fabulous.\"\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d83b4c02e22af0cb06b1316?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Brian Chesky Airbnb\" height=\"2294\" width=\"3058\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Brian Chesky, Chief Executive Officer of Airbnb smiles during a session at the annual meeting of the World Economic Forum (WEF) in Davos January 23, 2014.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Denis Balibouse</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source:&#160;<a href=\"http://www.businessinsider.com/jony-ive-airbnb-brian-chesky-time-100-list-2015-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Business Insider</a></em></p>\n\tChesky is not married, though he was previously in a relationship with artist Elissa Patel. Chesky has a golden retriever named Sir Richard Parker who hangs out at Airbnb headquarters and accompanies him on road trips.\n\t\n\t<blockquote class=\"instagram-media\" data-instgrm-captioned  style=\"background:#FFF; data.width~540;\">\n\t<div style=\"padding:8px;\">\n\t\t<div style=\"background:#F8F8F8; line-height:0; margin-top:40px; padding:62.4537037037% 0; text-align:center; width:100%;\">\n\t\t\t<div style=\"background:url(data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAACwAAAAsCAMAAAApWqozAAAABGdBTUEAALGPC/xhBQAAAAFzUkdCAK7OHOkAAAAMUExURczMzPf399fX1+bm5mzY9AMAAADiSURBVDjLvZXbEsMgCES5/P8/t9FuRVCRmU73JWlzosgSIIZURCjo/ad+EQJJB4Hv8BFt+IDpQoCx1wjOSBFhh2XssxEIYn3ulI/6MNReE07UIWJEv8UEOWDS88LY97kqyTliJKKtuYBbruAyVh5wOHiXmpi5we58Ek028czwyuQdLKPG1Bkb4NnM+VeAnfHqn1k4+GPT6uGQcvu2h2OVuIf/gWUFyy8OWEpdyZSa3aVCqpVoVvzZZ2VTnn2wU8qzVjDDetO90GSy9mVLqtgYSy231MxrY6I2gGqjrTY0L8fxCxfCBbhWrsYYAAAAAElFTkSuQmCC); font-size:14px; line-height:17px;\" datetime=\"2015-05-10T17:08:12+00:00\">May 10, 2015 at 10:08am PDT</time>\n\t\t</p></div></blockquote><script async defer src=\"//platform.instagram.com/en_US/embeds.js\"></script><p>&#160;</p>\n\tIn 2016, Chesky, as well as Airbnb's two other cofounders, all publicly signed the Giving Pledge, a philanthropic initiative started by Warren Buffett and Bill and Melinda Gates. By doing so, they promise donate more than half of their wealth within their lifetimes.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/57b1ccfbdb5ce949188b69e8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"founders airbnb Joe Gebbia Brian Chesky\" height=\"1350\" width=\"1800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>From left: Airbnb cofounders Brian Chesky, Nathan Blecharczyk, and Joe Gebbia.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://a0.muscache.com/airbnb/press/resources/founders-airbnb-2000.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Airbnb</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/billionaires-join-the-bill-gates-and-warren-buffet-giving-pledge-to-give-away-their-wealth-2016-6\">Business Insider</a></em></p>\n\tUp until 2016, Chesky was still renting out his couch in his San Francisco apartment on Airbnb. But after getting caught flouting a San Francisco law that requires hosts to register with the city, Chesky was forced to take the listing down.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/57b1d0f9db5ce91d008b6b11?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Brian Chesky, co-founder and Chief Executive of AirBnb, attends the Reuters Global Technology Summit in San Francisco June 18, 2013. REUTERS/Stephen Lam\" height=\"533\" width=\"711\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Chesky, co-founder and CEO of AirBnb, attends the Reuters Global Technology Summit in San Francisco\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomson Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source: <a href=\"http://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-ceo-violated-sf-registration-law-2016-1\">Business Insider</a></em></p>\n\tWhile he remains CEO, Chesky handed over daily operations of the company to Blecharczyk in 2014. These days, Chesky remains focused on Airbnb's future moves.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/57b1d0eadb5ce950008b6b8e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Brian Chesky\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2667\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Airbnb CEO Brian Chesky\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kimberly White/Getty Images for Fortune</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source:&#160;<a href=\"http://www.vanityfair.com/news/2016/11/airbnb-brian-chesky\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Vanity Fair</a></em></p>\n\tAirbnb announced in September 2019 that it planned to go public in 2020.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d83b5462e22af1e7e6158fb?format=jpeg\" alt=\"brian chesky\" height=\"1252\" width=\"1670\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mike Windle/Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-announces-plan-to-go-public-in-2020-ipo-2019-9\">Business Insider</a></em></p>\n\tBut its IPO was a question mark for much of 2020 after the coronavirus pandemic hit: in early March, Airbnb's revenue plummeted 80% due to virus-related travel restrictions. Airbnb burned through its cash reserves and opted to raise $2 billion in debt and equity financing to stay afloat. Its valuation, previously $31 billion, slipped to $18 billion.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb3da1584aa302f7e425128?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Brian Chesky Airbnb\" height=\"2049\" width=\"2732\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-ceo-brian-chesky-pandemic-challenges-resiliency-ipo-interview-2020-9?r=ah-sub\">Business Insider</a>, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-paying-10-percent-interest-debt-valuation-cut-18-billion-2020-4?r=ts-sub\">Business Insider</a></em></p>\n\tAirbnb laid off 1,900 employees, about 25% of its full-time staff, and hundreds of contractors. The move was met with frustration from employees who said they felt betrayed by the decision, but Chesky was also praised for his handling of the layoffs: employees were given generous severance packages and Chesky offered to help find them jobs elsewhere.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb3dbee165ecf320e6728d5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"airbnb\" height=\"1355\" width=\"1807\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Employees at Airbnb&#39;s headquarters.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Gabrielle Lurie/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-under-scrutiny-for-laying-off-1900-employees-2020-7\">Business Insider</a>, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-layoffs-generous-severance-package-2020-5\">Business Insider</a>, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/bchesky/status/1257915103615172608\">Brian Chesky/Twitter</a></em></p>\n\tOver the past few months, things have started to turn around for Airbnb as people have begun to rethink how they travel. Though the pandemic decimated Airbnb's business in the first several months of the year, the company is forging ahead with its IPO.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb3e168d980a12f8c2c6e4a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Brian Chesky\" height=\"1345\" width=\"1793\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mike Cohen/Getty Images for Smith/Getty; BFA; Olivia Atherton; Skye Gould/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>In August 2014, Jennifer Brody was working as a studio manager at California's Palo Alto SoulCycle when she met Conor Kelly, a \"master instructor\" with SoulCycle. Kelly was in town from the East Coast to teach a class.</p><p>After the class ended, Brody, who is a Black woman, said she changed out of her workout clothes and put a bandana on her head. When she passed Kelly in the studio, she said, he laughed and said \"Whoa — Aunt Jemima!\" in an apparent reference to the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/aunt-jemima-is-changing-its-name-mascot-over-racial-stereotype-2020-6\">syrup and pancake brand</a>.</p><p>\"That he felt OK calling me 'Aunt Jemima' in the middle of a studio lobby in Palo Alto was disgusting,\" Brody recently told Business Insider. Brody said she told a couple of instructors of color about Kelly's remark, but she didn't officially report it because, she believed, \"There wasn't anyone who would have cared.\"</p><p>\"SoulCycle kind of turned the cheek on a lot of stuff as long as they were making money,\" Brody added.</p><p>While SoulCycle instructors were fawned over by riders and the company's top brass, insiders said inappropriate behavior became more commonplace as SoulCycle's cult following grew.</p><p>While top-tier talent was lavished with perks like Soho House memberships and, in one case, a Mercedes-Benz while teaching in the Hamptons, insiders said some of SoulCycle's most successful instructors discriminated against a pregnant woman, fat-shamed employees, slept with riders, and used homophobic and racist language.</p><p>Business Insider spoke with more than 30 SoulCycle insiders — including current and former riders, studio staff, instructors, and corporate employees — many of whom accused SoulCycle of turning a blind eye to egregious behavior because the instructors were too valuable to let go of.&#160;</p><h2><a 00:31:28","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:28","title":"A US Navy destroyer just shot down an intercontinental ballistic missile target for the first time","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-navy-destroyer-shoots-down-icbm-target-in-historic-test-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb3d70d7b258c2d5e4ab5e6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A US warship fires an SM-3 Block IIA interceptor\" height=\"500\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A US warship fires an SM-3 Block IIA interceptor\n<p class=\"copyright\">Missile Defense Agency</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The US Navy destroyer USS John Finn successfully intercepted a mock intercontinental ballistic missile (ICBM) Tuesday morning, the Missile Defense Agency announced.</li>\n<li>In the first-of-its-kind test, the destroyer fired an SM-3 Block IIA, a weapon originally designed to eliminate mid-range missiles, at the mock ICBM.</li>\n<li>\"We have demonstrated that an Aegis [ballistic missile defense]-equipped vessel equipped with the SM-3 Block IIA missile can defeat an ICBM-class target,\" MDA Director Vice Adm. Jon Hill said in a statement</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A US Navy destroyer shot down an intercontinental ballistic missile target for the first time on Tuesday in a historic missile defense test, the Missile Defense Agency announced.</p><p>Early Tuesday, an unarmed target missile simulating an enemy ICBM threat was launched from the Ronald Reagan Ballistic Missile Defense Test Site on the Kwajalein Atoll in the Marshall Islands toward an area of open ocean near Hawaii.</p><p>During this defense of Hawaii scenario, the Aegis Ballistic Missile Defense System-equipped destroyer USS John Finn collected tracking data from the Command and Control Battle Management Communications network and fired off a Standard Missile-3 Block IIA interceptor, which successfully destroyed the target missile.</p><p>The MDA released an animation of the intercept.</p><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/4Hi8pqwf7FY\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe><p>\"This was an incredible accomplishment and critical milestone for the Aegis BMD SM-3 Block IIA program,\" Vice Adm. Jon Hill, the MDA director, said in a statement.</p><p>\"We have demonstrated that an Aegis BMD-equipped vessel equipped with the SM-3 Block IIA missile can defeat an ICBM-class target,\" he added.</p><p>The SM-3 Block IIA is an interceptor developed by Raytheon Missiles &#38; Defense in partnership with Japan's Mitsubishi Heavy Industries. Tuesday's intercept test was the sixth time the ship-launched interceptor has been tested against a simulated missile threat. Although the interceptor was originally built to take down intermediate-range ballistic missiles, the US military has demonstrated a new capability.</p><p>\"This first-of-its-kind test shows that our nation has a viable option for a new layer of defense against long-range threats,\" said Bryan Rosselli, the vice president of Strategic Missile Defense at Raytheon Missiles &#38; Defense, in a separate statement.</p><p>As Tuesday's ICBM intercept test was a preliminary test of a new combat capability, the ICBM target did not deploy countermeasures.</p><p>Even though the test was not a complex, fully-operational evaluation, the test stressed the interceptor, pushing it beyond what it was initially designed to do. The MDA said in its statement that the SM-3 Block IIA will be evaluated further.</p><p>A sea-based counter-ICBM capability would augment the existing ground-based missile defense systems in place to protect the US from threats long-range missile threats, such as those posed by China, Russia, and more recently North Korea.</p><p>Although the MDA did not mention North Korea specifically in its statement on Tuesday's intercept test, an a<a href=\"https://www.japantimes.co.jp/news/2020/11/17/world/us-aegis-icbm-test-intercept/\">gency spokesperson explained to the Japan Times</a> that the target missiles are \"designed to simulate a threat missile from a rogue nation.\"</p><p>While US missile defense systems would theoretically be able to stop a North Korean missile, it is unclear how they would fair against more advanced ICBM threats, such as those posed by China and Russia.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/us-navy-destroyer-shoots-down-icbm-target-in-historic-test-2020-11'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a REUTERS/Carlo Allegri/File Photo\" height=\"2332\" width=\"4665\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>FILE PHOTO: A Bank of America logo is pictured in the Manhattan borough of New York City\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\n<ul><li><strong>Investor bullishness surged to its highest point since January 2018 amid US election outcomes and encouraging vaccine progress, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/bac-stock\">Bank of America</a> strategists said Tuesday.</strong></li><li><strong>Fund managers' allocations to stocks hit a net 46% overweight in the November 6 to November 12 period, closing in on the 50% threshold that indicates \"extremely bullish\" levels, according to the bank.&#160;</strong></li><li><strong>The recent rotation to value stocks can continue through the end of the year, but the strategists recommend investors \"sell the vaccine\" as the market comes close to reaching \"full bull.\"</strong></li><li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestutm_source=msn.com&utm_medium=referral&utm_content=msn-slideshow&utm_campaign=bodyurl?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestts&#38;utm_medium=ingest\">Visit the Business Insider homepage for more stories</a>.</strong></li></ul><hr><p>November has so far brought a spate of good news for stock bulls, but Bank of America fears the market might now be too cheerful for its own good.</p><p>The bank's latest fund manager survey shows investor optimism surging this month to its highest point since January 2018. Managers' allocations to stocks reached a net 46% overweight, inching closer to the 50% threshold that indicates sentiments are \"extremely bullish.\"</p><p>The survey took place from November 6 to November 12, signaling US election outcomes and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-coronavirus-vaccine-success-plans-for-emergency-approval-fda-2020-9\">encouraging progress</a> on Pfizer and BioNTech's coronavirus vaccines led to the jump in bullishness. Investors rotated into value stocks on November 9 <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stock-market-value-rotation-previews-2021-action-strategy-outlook-jpmorgan-2020-11-1029798647\">at the fastest pace since 2008</a>, and cash holdings fell below their pre-pandemic levels.</p><p>Rising exposure to riskier assets signals investors are more convinced than ever that the US recovery is on track, but Bank of America's strategists advised clients to avoid blindly entering a crowded trade.</p><p>\"Reopening rotation can continue in the fourth quarter but we say 'sell the vaccine' in coming weeks and months as we think we're close to 'full bull,'\" the team led by Michael Hartnett wrote in the Tuesday note.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/multifamily-real-estate-investing-strategy-affordable-housing-units-evan-holladay-2020-11\" data-analytics-position=\"1\" data-analytics-module=\"\">30 years old with a piece of 300 units: Here's how Evan Holladay is filling a unique multifamily real-estate niche with an under-the-radar strategy</a></em></p><p>The survey's timing fails to capture a similar, albeit smaller, value rotation seen Monday after Moderna announced that its own vaccine was <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-works-to-prevent-covid-19-company-says-2020-11?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">highly effective</a> at protecting against COVID-19. The Dow Jones industrial average and S&#38;P 500 closed Monday <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stock-market-news-today-moderna-vaccine-dow-record-recovery-optimism-2020-11-1029808168\">at record highs</a> and investors <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/airline-cruise-stocks-moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-data-market-reopening-recovery-2020-11-1029806318?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">pushed further into the so-called reopening trade</a>.</p><p>Despite last week's shift from tech giants to small-caps, fund managers surveyed said they still view tech stocks as the most crowded trade by a massive margin. Month-over-month allocation shifts show investors placing larger bets on small-caps, emerging-market assets, banks, and energy stocks. Positioning weakened in bonds, cash, and consumer staples stocks, according to the bank.</p><p>The coronavirus resurgence remains the biggest tail risk among surveyed managers, with a potential tech bubble and civil unrest following behind. The reading comes as virus cases spiked to record highs in the US and continue to trend higher. Several cities reinstated partial lockdown measures over the past week to curb community spread, reviving concerns of a double-dip recession.</p><p>Still, 91% of respondents expect the economy to grow stronger over the next year, and more investors say the economy is in the early stages of an expansionary cycle as opposed to mired in recession.</p><p><em><strong>Now read more markets coverage from
